## Fixed (pending in-game validation) - Re-aim looped arrival: descent trigger for the post-parking approach (branch `reaim-descent-trigger`)

**Bug:** a looped re-aim interplanetary mission whose re-aimed transfer arrives EARLIER than recorded (captureShift < 0) left the post-parking destination approach — deorbit→landing, or the rendezvous→dock at a station — rendering at the wrong destination rotation, icon frozen on the parking orbit, the body-fixed clip drawn off-site/disconnected. PR #1177 shifts the transfer member's destination parking conics ~|captureShift| earlier to meet the early transfer; the SEPARATE body-fixed approach members then play at the unshifted loop clock = the wrong rotation phase.

**Fix:** detach the approach member SET from the loop clock and re-anchor it to the first rotation-aligned live moment after the icon reaches the parking-orbit deorbit point. The icon circles the shifted parking conic (anchored to triggerUT so it reaches the deorbit point exactly at the handoff — smooth + exact, no hop), then the recorded clip plays forward at the live rate, window-dispatched across the chain members. `Reaim/DescentTrigger.cs` holds the pure math (`ComputeDescentMemberHead`), the set selection (`SelectDescentMemberIndices`, by the transfer member's last target-body conic-end seam), and the window dispatch (`TryResolveDescentMemberHead`); `LoopUnit` gains a `DescentMemberIndices` set + per-member fields gated by `HasDescentTrigger` (byte-identical off); `MissionLoopUnitBuilder` engages off the destination parking loiter run with build-time `captureShift = geomTof − recordedTof`, and DECLINES (faithful fallback) unless the set is contiguous, starts at the seam, and `conicEnd` sits in the post-SOI-exit region; `ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT` applies the multi-member override and suppresses the boundary-overlap secondary (R6). Discovered mid-build (via a chain-structure investigation + 2 adversarial reviews) that the failing subject ("Route: KSC → Duna") is a multi-member CHAIN whose "descent" is actually an orbital rendezvous + station DOCK at ~237 km — the trigger math is identical for landing or dock. 36 pure xUnit tests (math + set selection + window dispatch + resolver integration); full suite 15906 green.

**Playtest follow-ups (all fixed):** the descent rendered correctly for a frame then the icon snapped back to the loiter while the line persisted — three compounding defects: (1) the polyline chain-run forward pass drew the descent line on the loop clock, bypassing the trigger — the `CollectChainRunMembers` exclusion missed it because a descent member rec can be `chain=none` (non-chain early-return) and the head-leg bridge + run loop reached it too; gated all four sites via `IsDescentTriggerMember`. (2) the FLIGHT `GhostPlaybackEngine.UpdateUnitMemberPlayback` never applied the trigger, so the descent got no engine ghost/icon in flight, only a ghost-less polyline marker; wired it via `GhostPlaybackLogic.ResolveDescentMemberEngineRender` (override `spanLoopUT=descentHead` + `decision=Render`), R6 secondary suppressed, M4b phasing-knob shift gated off for descent members. (3) observability: new `DESCENT REVERTED` event, single-leg polyline draw line, teardown-reason tagged with the descent member index, recordingId on the lifecycle traces.

**Playtest follow-up 4 — the captureShift "two paths" leak (CORRECTED diagnosis; the first fix here was a NO-OP):** the icon-on-the-wrong-path symptom persisted across two TS playtests. The first investigation MISLABELED rec 44's `dataEnd=2570542381` as "the recorded landing" and concluded rec 44 carries its own descent; the clamp-to-seam fix it produced (commit 44ddc8d61) was a **0.01 s no-op** because rec 44 actually ENDS at the deorbit seam (`dataEnd ≈ deorbit(seam) = 2570542380.99`) — the post-seam descent lives entirely in the SEPARATE members 42/43/45/46. The REAL cause (log `logs/2026-06-20_1600`): **both Duna paths belong to rec 44, split by the captureShift.** PR #1177 shifts rec 44's destination parking conics ~|captureShift| (≈33 days) earlier to meet the early transfer, so the icon rides the SHIFTED parking ellipse (path one). Once the loiter head passes the shifted conic end (`conicEnd = deorbit + captureShift`), `ForwardRenderWindow`'s past-end branch (`currentUT <= dataEndUT + 1`) still fires because `dataEndUT` is the UNSHIFTED `rec.EndUT` ~33 days later, painting rec 44's OWN unshifted recorded approach tail + a ~33-day-gap seam bridge (path two — `runLegs=7 bridgeLegs=7`). The icon cannot follow path two: it is a render-only polyline, and the real re-anchored descent (the separate members) was Loitering. **Fix:** repurpose `ClampChainDataEndForDescentTransfer` to cap the forward-run `chainDataEndUT` at the **shifted conic end** (`RecordedDeorbitUT + CaptureShiftSeconds`, captureShift negative) instead of the unshifted seam, so the past-end branch fails the moment the icon leaves the shifted conic — killing both the bogus tail and the gap bridge; the shifted parking the icon rides is untouched. The no-op Clamp A (`ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT` memberEndUT clamp) is **removed**. **Logging holes filled (kept):** the TS marker-decision trace now threads the real loop-shifted effUT (was printing `currentUT` into both slots), and a non-rate-limited on-change `icon-flip` (`GhostOrbitIcon`) event fires once per actual proto↔orbit-segment suppress flip. Net +1 xUnit (Clamp B shifted-conic-end cap, the 3 no-op Clamp A tests removed); full suite 16088 green.

**Observability — PROVISIONAL auto-slow warp (TEMPORARY DIAGNOSTIC — REMOVE after a clean descent log):** the actual descent (re-entry/landing, the separate members) renders for only ~5.7 h (`descentEnd − deorbit ≈ 20513 s`) once per ~454-day loop = **0.05 % of the loop**, so manual warp keeps stepping over it (cycle 9 SKIPPED entirely; cycle 10 window ~17 h ahead of where the capture ended) and we have never captured an in-window frame. To get ONE clean capture, `Reaim/DescentWarpControl.cs` decelerates warp as the descent approaches: the descent resolver (reached in BOTH the tracking station and FLIGHT via the polyline Driver's per-frame walk — one call site covers both scenes) calls `NotifyDescentState` each frame; the pure `DecideWarpAction` returns a **deceleration ramp** — `StepDown` one warp level whenever the next step (`warpRate·dt`) would consume > ½ the remaining time-to-trigger, and `DropToRealtime` at the trigger / first Descent frame. **First attempt FAILED** (log `logs/2026-06-20_1731`, 1,000,000× warp, `auto-drop`=0, Loiter→Done with no Descent frame): the original single-frame lookahead (`nextUT ≥ trigger`) undershot because at 1M× the loiter was only ~2 frames wide and the actual per-frame UT jump exceeded `rate·dt`, so the next frame leapt over the whole window. The ramp can't overshoot (it bleeds 1M→100k→…→1× as the trigger nears) and is robust to dt hiccups. Acts at most once per frame (the resolver calls per descent member); drops once per cycle (then re-warp is free). Two **concrete sealed** KSPAddons (Flight + TrackingStation — the abstract-base shape of the first attempt is a suspected reason `Awake` never wired) wire the Unity seam (`TimeWarp.CurrentRate` / `CurrentRateIndex` / `Time.unscaledDeltaTime` / `frameCount` / `SetRate(idx,true)`) and log `DescentWarpControl wired (<scene>)` on Awake; null in xUnit so the resolver call is a no-op there. A rate-limited `warp-ctl … action=…` trace shows the per-frame decision so a no-op is debuggable from one log. Gated by the temporary `autoDropWarpForDescent` setting (default on). +12 xUnit (`DescentWarpControlTests`, incl. the replayed 1M× failure frame). **SUPERSEDED:** this ramp design was replaced by the distance-proportional cap (see the entries below). The whole control is a **TEMPORARY DEBUG AID that BREAKS GAMEPLAY (it forces warp deceleration) and MUST BE REMOVED once the descent rendering is fully debugged** — it ships only to make the descent reachable during the rendering debug, NOT as a permanent feature. Removal recipe in the `DescentWarpControl.cs` banner.

**Warp scaffold was DEAD ON ARRIVAL — live/recorded frame mismatch (FIXED 2026-06-20, log `logs/2026-06-20_1800`):** the auto-slow ramp never acted in ANY capture (`auto-drop`=0, `descent warp ramp`=0, `action=None` on every `warp-ctl` line) — not because the player was at 1×, but because `DecideWarpAction`'s past-the-descent guard `currentUT >= descentEndUT` compared a **LIVE** `currentUT` (~3.96e9) against a **RECORDED** `descentEndUT` (~2.57e9, `unit.DescentEndUT` is recorded-frame). A recorded UT is far below any live UT, so the guard fired on every frame and returned `None`, silently disabling the entire control. The existing `DescentWarpControlTests` passed because they used same-frame toy values (`Trigger=1000`, `DescentEnd=21513`) and never exercised the cross-frame call site. **Fix:** new pure `DescentWarpControl.DescentWindowEndLiveUT(triggerUT, recordedDeorbitUT, descentEndUT) = triggerUT + (descentEndUT − recordedDeorbitUT)` converts the window end into the live frame; `NotifyDescentState` now takes `recordedDeorbitUT` and feeds the live window end to `DecideWarpAction` (param renamed `descentWindowEndLiveUT`); the call site in `ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT` passes `unit.RecordedDeorbitUT`. +3 xUnit (frame-conversion + NaN + a cross-frame regression test replaying the real 2026-06-20 UTs that StepDowns now vs `None` on the raw recorded end). Note the trigger timing itself was always correct — the log proves it fires at the FIRST rotation-aligned opportunity (`entry 3962526852.9 → trigger 3962534821.3`, 7968 s, `siteRotResidual=0.0000°`); the descent simply never rendered because the dead control let a warp frame leap over the 5.7 h window (and at 1× it is too slow to reach by hand).

**Frame-mismatch fix was NECESSARY but INSUFFICIENT — the step-down ramp itself can't catch a sub-frame window; REPLACED with a distance-proportional cap (2026-06-20, log `logs/2026-06-20_1800` re-test):** with the dead guard fixed, the player re-tested and the descent SKIPPED AGAIN (`phase=Descent`=0, `DESCENT SKIPPED`=1, still `auto-drop`=0 / `ramp`=0). The log proved why: the player lives at **1,000,000×** (4 of 6 logged warp decisions) and the cycle-14 trace was first seen already at `Done`, 18.9 M s past the window, on a `dt=0.379 s` **lag-spike** frame. At 1M× one frame jumps ≥20,000 s (≈ the entire 20,513 s window) and a lag spike jumps ~400,000 s, so a single inter-frame jump straddles the whole loiter+window between two resolver calls — the step-down ramp's ~1-frame-wide deceleration zone is simply leapt over (it steps down one level only when `warpRate·dt > ttt/2`, which never gets a frame to fire on). **Fix:** replace `DecideWarpAction`/`DescentWarpAction` with a PROPORTIONAL CAP — pure `ComputeMaxWarpRate(currentUT, triggerUT, descentWindowEndLiveUT)` returns the max allowed rate: `+Infinity` past the descent (free warp), `clip / DescentWatchSeconds` (≈1000× → the clip plays over ~20 s) inside the window, and `distance / WorstFrameSeconds` (WorstFrameSeconds=2, halved from 4 after a playtest "slows too soon / takes too long" trim — starts the run-in half as far out and ~2x faster; a frame at the cap advances `cap·WorstFrameSeconds ≤ distance` so it still cannot overshoot, with ~5x headroom over the worst observed 0.4 s frame) approaching — so the cap tightens as the descent nears and CANNOT overshoot. Pure `SelectRateIndexForCap(maxRate, TimeWarp.warpRates)` picks the highest level ≤ cap; `NotifyDescentState` caps DOWN only (never speeds the player up; they keep full slower control and re-warp freely once past). New `RateLevelsProvider` seam (`TimeWarp.fetch.warpRates`); the `Time.unscaledDeltaTime` seam + the per-cycle `droppedCycleByKey` dedup are gone (the cap is continuous, not a one-shot). Log line is now `warp-cap … cap=Nx targetIdx=…` / `descent warp cap: idx A -> B`. 16 `DescentWarpControlTests` (frame conversion, the cap's no-overshoot invariant `cap·WorstFrameSeconds ≤ distance`, level pick, and the replayed 1M× regression). Suite green.

**THE ACTUAL "icon won't transition" bug — transfer/loiter member's icon never hands off to the descent (FIXED 2026-06-20, confirmed from log `logs/2026-06-20_1334`):** the trigger math, the descent-member detach, and the warp are all beside the point for the user-visible symptom. In the ONLY run that ever rendered a descent (13:34, `DESCENT RENDERED cycle=8`), the descent member DID render (`member=45 phase=Descent render=True head=2570542481`) — but at the SAME instant the transfer/loiter member was ALSO drawn (`rec=44 Marker DRAWN headUT=2567696156` on the parking, `outcome=drawn-non-proto`). Two icons coexist: the prominent native proto-icon circling the loiter + the descent marker. The user tracks the loiter proto-icon and reports "the icon stayed on the loiter" — exactly the 3-segment screenshot (loiter line = transfer member's shifted conic; descent line = the descent members; the short disconnected one = the brief seam-windows / the deferred orbit-segment leak). The descent trigger only detaches the DESCENT members; the non-descent transfer member renders on the normal path (`GhostPlaybackLogic.cs:8434`) with zero awareness of the descent phase (credit: external investigation). **Fix:** in `ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT`, for a CURRENTLY-RENDERING non-descent member of a descent-trigger unit, compute the unit-wide descent phase (`DescentTrigger.ComputeDescentMemberHead`) and HIDE the member while it is `Descent` — a clean handoff (the design already guarantees position-continuity at the seam, `conicEnd == recordedDeorbit`). Untouched in Inert/Loiter/Done (the loiter icon is correct until the trigger). Gated to `HasDescentTrigger` + `decision==Render`, so byte-identical everywhere else. New always-on `transfer/loiter member … unitDescentPhase=… -> HIDDEN/kept` trace makes the double-icon (or its absence) greppable. +1 xUnit (`Resolver_TransferMember_HiddenDuringDescent_CleanHandoffNoDoubleIcon`, with a loiter-region transfer member added to `BuildDescentUnit`). Suite green. **FLIGHT follow-up (NOT fixed):** the flight `GhostPlaybackEngine` is a separate path; the external investigation found it does not even apply the descent trigger for the unit in flight (`owner=33` lacks `HasDescentTrigger` in the engine's `LoopUnitSet` while the map resolver's has it — a suspected stale/different cached set), so the flight 3D ghost needs that engine-side investigation before the symmetric engine handoff hide is added. The user's repro is the Tracking Station (the map resolver), which this fix covers.

**Playtest follow-up 5 — the descent renders DISCONNECTED from the loiter (I1, FIXED 2026-06-20, log `logs/2026-06-20_1944_descent-fired`):** with the handoff + warp working, the re-anchored descent (the post-seam members, 49 km → surface) rendered but with NO visible connection from the loiter/parking down to it — "only the final descent to landing polyline rendered; the segments from loiter to that did not render." Root cause: the deorbit/approach legs DOWN TO the seam (transfer member rec=44's Duna legs 4-10, 1645 km → 49 km, leg 10 the 196 km → 49 km deorbit ending AT the seam `RecordedDeorbitUT`) live INSIDE the transfer member, NOT in the descent set. During Loiter the transfer member renders (`kept`) but its loopUT sits ~|captureShift| (≈33 days) BELOW those legs' recorded UTs, so the per-leg head-UT gate (`ShouldDrawLegAtHeadUT(…, headUT)`) is false every frame; during Descent the transfer member is HIDDEN by the handoff. So the deorbit legs draw in NO phase. **Fix (playback-only, I1):** in the polyline PRIMARY leg loop, Loiter-phase only, for the transfer member's contiguous post-shifted-conic deorbit-tail legs (`conicEnd < legEnd ≤ seam+eps`), substitute a re-anchored pre-seam head `recordedDeorbitUT + (currentUT − triggerUT)` (which is < seam while `currentUT < triggerUT`) so the legs sweep down to the seam and join the descent member's first head AT the trigger — rendering continuous loiter → deorbit → entry → surface. Two new pure helpers in `Reaim/DescentTrigger.cs` (`TryComputeTransferDeorbitHead` Loiter-only, `ResolveTransferLegHeadUT` per-leg head pairing) + the cycle-resolving wrapper `GhostPlaybackLogic.TryResolveTransferDeorbitHeadForMember` (resolves the unit cycle via the production `DecideUnitMemberRender` path — one source of truth, no parallel formula). Gated on the EXACT existing descent-transfer predicate (`HasDescentTrigger && !IsDescentTriggerMember`), so byte-identical for non-descent units and for every phase except Loiter on the transfer member. No change to the forward-run pass, the handoff, `ClampChainDataEndForDescentTransfer`, or the warp scaffold. +9 xUnit (`TransferDeorbitHead_*`, `ResolveTransferLegHeadUT_*`, `TransferDeorbitHeadForMember_*`); full suite 16114 green.

**I2 (loiter two-line flicker) — DEFERRED, no longer reproduces:** the premise (loiter-phase oscillation between the shifted parking conic and the Duna approach hyperbola with `line-blink` + `gap-vs-retire` spam) does NOT reproduce in the current HEAD (post Clamp-A-removal). The `2026-06-20_1944` log shows the transfer icon stably on the shifted parking conic throughout the loiter window (zero hyperbola covering-segment changes inside it, only pre-loiter approach line-blinks ~70 s before the trigger). If a fresh capture after I1 shows a real loiter two-conic flicker, fix via a clamped `segSelectUT` fed ONLY to the covering-segment selection (NOT `effUT`, to avoid perturbing the icon epoch), gated on the same descent-transfer predicate during Loiter.

**I4 (flight-engine deorbit-tail continuity) — DEFERRED, flight-only:** the flight `GhostPlaybackEngine` DOES apply the descent trigger — it renders the descent members + the transfer handoff in flight via `ResolveDescentMemberEngineRender` (override `spanLoopUT`/`decision`), so the descent itself works in flight. What is deferred is only the engine analogue of the I1 deorbit-tail continuity (the engine positions a live ghost, not a polyline head — a separate larger change). The user's repro is the Tracking Station (the map resolver), which I1 covers; if the flight descent ever diverges from the map a stale flight `LoopUnitSet` cache is the first suspect, but no FLIGHT-scene log has shown that.

**The two deferred RENDER-ONLY cosmetics — FIXED (pending in-game validation, branch `reaim-descent-render`):**

- **C1 — descent ICON ride (TS non-overlap single-marker path).** The descent LINE rode the re-anchored `descentHead` (via the polyline primary pass's `ResolveTrackingStationSampleFrame`), but the descent-set member's atmospheric MARKER tried the body-fixed resolve FIRST (`ParsekTrackingStation.DrawAtmosphericMarkers`) and only fell back to `TryAnchorMarkerToPolyline` — so at the descent head it pinned off the gap-filled below-surface chord or bracket-missed (`ride=not-attempted` / `skipped-position-fail`). Fix: for a descent-SET member (`GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer.IsDescentTriggerMember`), anchor the marker to the DRAWN polyline FIRST (the same head the line uses — `effUT` is already the `descentHead`), falling through to the unchanged body-fixed-first chain only when the leg has not drawn this frame. Byte-identical for every non-descent marker; overlap descent members already ride via `DrawOneTsOverlapInstanceMarker`. The always-on `atmosMarker-{i} … rodePolyline=` line shows the ride in a capture.
- **C2 — post-landing SUBORBITAL looping ghost (descent-continuation-aware orbit source).** Once the descent has handed off / landed, the non-descent TRANSFER member is no longer hidden by the handoff (it hides only in Descent, GhostPlaybackLogic.cs:8445-8467; in Done it does not), so the TS CREATE funnel (`ResolveTrackingStationGhostSourceCore` → `ResolveMapPresenceGhostSource`, the log-confirmed firing path — the per-tick UPDATE pass refuses the tail for loop members via `EndpointTailAllowedInTrackingStationUpdate`) synthesized an `EndpointTail` coast from the transfer member's recorded deorbit endpoint = a sub-surface ellipse drawn as a closed loop. Fix: new pure `GhostPlaybackLogic.IsTransferMemberDescentContinuation` (true iff the transfer member's LIVE-frame descent phase ∈ {Descent, Done}, via `ComputeDescentMemberHead` — the SAME machinery the handoff uses, NOT a raw recorded-UT inequality) drives a new `transferMemberDescentContinuation` flag threaded through `ResolveTrackingStationGhostSourceCore` to `ResolveMapPresenceGhostSource`, where it early-returns `None` ("transfer-member-descent-continuation") BEFORE the covering-segment / EndpointTail / Segment resolution — so the ghost RETIRES cleanly with NOTHING to fall back to. This is the descent-continuation-aware fix, NOT the reverted **J2** (commit 9fecdfcb6): J2 declined the tail INSIDE `TryResolveEndpointTailForMapPresence`, which fell through to a stale launch/transfer Segment (Sun/Ike) and put a clickable ghost on the wrong body. Pre-seam (Inert/Loiter) the flag is false, so the shifted parking (loiter) conic keeps rendering, byte-identical. +6 xUnit (phase semantics, loiter-conic preservation, byte-identical-off, the resolver gate returning None with no fallback). Full suite green.

**Observability add (branch `reaim-descent-render`) — per-frame full map-object snapshot, scoped to the loiter + descent windows.** To catch extra / stale trajectory lines that RENDER but never appear in the change-based per-pid tracer (the polyline `VectorLine`s + forward arcs are NOT in `ghostMapVesselPids`, so `MapRenderProbe` never sampled them), the `mapRenderTracing` tracer now dumps EVERY rendered map object per frame while a descent-trigger unit is in Loiter (the loiter orbit) or Descent (descent-to-landing). Wiring: pure `GhostPlaybackLogic.TryGetDescentUnitRenderPhase` (unit-level phase, member-agnostic, via the production `DecideUnitMemberRender` + `ComputeDescentMemberHead`) → the polyline `Driver` (exec-order -50) publishes the window via `MapRenderTrace.NoteDescentRenderWindow(frame, …)` → the end-of-frame `MapRenderProbe` (exec-order 10000, same frame) reads `TryGetDescentRenderWindow` and emits `phase=SceneSnapshot` lines: (1) every `FlightGlobals.Vessels` orbit line that is `active` (full scene, ghost or not, so an unexpected ellipse shows), and (2) every live Parsek polyline leg / forward arc via `GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer.EmitRenderedPolylineSnapshot` (each line's `active` / `drawnThisFrame` / `staleActive` / `lastDrawnFrame`). Deliberately UN-rate-limited per-frame inside the window (huge but searchable, per request); the window bounds the volume to loiter+descent; entirely no-op when `mapRenderTracing` is off (default). +3 xUnit (`DescentUnitRenderPhase_*`). Grep `phase=SceneSnapshot` to isolate the per-frame map state; `staleActive=True` flags a VectorLine the deactivation sweep has not yet hidden.

**Pending:** in-game confirmation that (1) the transfer/loiter icon HANDS OFF — only the descent icon shows once it fires (`transfer/loiter member … -> HIDDEN` + `DESCENT RENDERED`), no double icon; (2) the proportional cap auto-decelerates the player from any warp into the descent (`warp-cap …` then `descent warp cap: …`) so it's reachable; (3) **(I1)** the Duna deorbit/approach polyline draws contiguous from the loiter parking conic down through the deorbit legs into the descent member's entry leg, `siteRotResidual` still 0.0000°; (4) **(C1)** the descent ICON now rides the line all the way to the landing (`atmosMarker … rodePolyline=True`), no vanish / pin at the seam; (5) **(C2)** NO sub-surface looping ghost after touchdown (no clickable phantom orbit through the planet, and NO wrong-body fallback — the loiter parking conic still renders before the seam). Capture a low-warp log that INCLUDES the trigger crossing + the post-landing window. NOTE: the in-window cap (~1000× → ~20 s) is a MAX; warp DOWN to 1× to study the landing.

**⚠ REMOVE THE WARP CAP — but in a SEPARATE follow-up PR, AFTER the rendering fixes (C1/C2) are in-game validated and merged.** `DescentWarpControl` forcibly decelerates the player's time-warp near a re-aim looped descent. It ships (default on, gated by `autoDropWarpForDescent`) ONLY as a temporary aid to make the descent reachable while validating its rendering — it is NOT a permanent feature and must be deleted before any release. It is intentionally KEPT in the `reaim-descent-render` PR (the C1/C2 fixes) so the descent stays reachable for that validation; its removal is the next PR, stacked on top once the user confirms the rendering is clean. Removal recipe: delete `DescentWarpControl.cs` + `DescentWarpControlTests.cs` + the `ParsekSettings.autoDropWarpForDescent` field + the `NotifyDescentState` call in `GhostPlaybackLogic.ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT`.

## ~~Bug - static GameEvent handler in OnLoad NREs and wipes the recording index~~ (DONE, branch `fix-onload-static-handler-nre`)

The M4b escrow work (`logistics-m4-multistop`) added
`GameEvents.onGameSceneSwitchRequested.Add(OnGameSceneSwitchClearEscrow)` to
`ParsekScenario.SubscribeVesselLifecycleEvents`, with `OnGameSceneSwitchClearEscrow`
declared `static`. KSP's `EventData<T>.Add` builds an `EvtDelegate` whose ctor runs
`originatorType = evt.Target.GetType().Name` (verified by decompiling Assembly-CSharp);
`evt.Target` is null for a static method, so `Add` throws `NullReferenceException`.
Because the subscription runs inside `OnLoad`, the exception aborted the entire OnLoad
**before recordings were loaded** (`OnLoad: exception phase=initial-baseline ... 0 recordings`),
and the next save then wrote `0 RECORDING_TREE` nodes to `persistent.sfs` — a silent
recording-index wipe. The CleanOrphanFiles guard preserved the sidecar files on disk
(`writing 0 RECORDING_TREE nodes but disk has N stranded sidecar recording ID(s)`), so no
data was lost, but every recording vanished from the UI. Recovery: redeploy a non-buggy
DLL, then load the freshest quicksave that still has the `RECORDING_TREE` nodes.

**Fix:** make `OnGameSceneSwitchClearEscrow` an instance method (its body only makes a
static `RouteStore.ClearAllEscrow` call, so instance-ness has no behavioral cost;
`OnDestroy` already unsubscribes it). Regression guard:
the parameterized `ScenarioGameEventHandlerContractTests.ScenarioGameEventHandler_MustBeInstanceMethod_NotStatic`
(now covers all six subscribed ParsekScenario handlers). General rule established: **no
`ParsekScenario` handler subscribed to a KSP GameEvent may be `static`** — KSP's
`EventData.Add` dereferences `evt.Target` (null for static).

## Dev - Logistics in-game tests: auto-spawn unloaded vessel (no manual second craft)

The 7 logistics FLIGHT in-game tests (origin-debit / pickup / multi-stop delivery,
`InGameTests/Logistics*RuntimeTests.cs`) need a live FLIGHT active vessel. The
LOADED-path tests use the ActiveVessel directly - a fueled PRELAUNCH pad rocket
satisfies them after `WaitForActiveVesselUnpack` (they check `loaded && !packed` +
an LF tank; no test rejects PRELAUNCH on `vessel.situation`, so no relaxation was
needed). The UNLOADED-path tests need a SEPARATE on-rails (unloaded) vessel with
LiquidFuel and used to SKIP whenever the save had none, forcing the player to
hand-place a second vessel.

Maintainer-chosen design: "use my pad rocket + auto-spawn the rest". New shared
fixture `InGameTests/Helpers/UnloadedFuelVesselFixture.cs`:
`EnsureUnloadedLiquidFuelVessel(minStoredLf, minFreeCapacity, result)` (coroutine)
(a) reuses any suitable pre-existing unloaded vessel (fast path, behavior-identical
for saves that already have one); else (b) snapshots the ActiveVessel via
`VesselSpawner.TryBackupSnapshot`, rewrites its LiquidFuel RESOURCE amounts via the
pure `AdjustSnapshotLiquidFuel` (>= minStoredLf stored, >= minFreeCapacity free,
flowState forced True) and spawns a FRESH-identity copy (preserveIdentity:false ->
regenerated pid, no collision) into a high (~250 km) parking ORBIT far from the
active vessel via `VesselSpawner.SpawnAtPosition(..., orbitOverride)` so KSP keeps
it on-rails / unloaded; (c) waits a bounded number of frames for the spawn to
register in `FlightGlobals.Vessels` AND settle unloaded, resolving by the returned
pid; (d) on any failure leaves `result.Vessel == null` so the caller falls back to
the existing `InGameAssert.Skip` (never worse than before). Cleanup: a SPAWNED
vessel is removed via `Vessel.Die()` + protoVessels drop in the test's finally
(`UnloadedFuelVesselFixture.Cleanup`); the batch baseline restore is the backstop.
Rewired tests: `OriginDebit_UnloadedOriginVessel_WritesProtoSnapshot`,
`OriginDebit_UnloadedDebit_SurvivesKspSaveRoundTrip`,
`MultiStop_UnloadedEndpoint_DeliversAtBothDocks`,
`PickupDebit_UnloadedEndpointVessel_WritesProtoSnapshot` (the per-suite
`TryFindUnloaded*` finders were folded into the fixture). The
inventory-pickup tests are unchanged (no unloaded variant; an unloaded inventory
fixture would need a stored cargo part the pad rocket may lack). Pure piece unit-
tested in `Source/Parsek.Tests/UnloadedFuelVesselFixtureTests.cs`. Test-infra only
(no user-facing CHANGELOG line). LIVE validation via Ctrl+Shift+T is pending.

## ~~Bug - `OnMainMenuTransition` is a static GameEvent handler: silently dead since 2026-03-22~~ (DONE - merged onto `logistics-m4-multistop`; in-game playtest PENDING)

`ParsekScenario.OnMainMenuTransition` was `private static` and subscribed to
`GameEvents.onGameSceneLoadRequested` from `RegisterMainMenuHook()` (called during `OnLoad`).
KSP's `EventData<T>.Add` builds an `EvtDelegate` whose ctor unconditionally runs
`originatorType = evt.Target.GetType().Name` (verified by decompiling Assembly-CSharp); `evt.Target`
is null for a static method, so `Add` throws `NullReferenceException`. The `Add` was wrapped in
`try/catch (NullReferenceException)` whose comment wrongly blamed "GameEvents not ready ... will
retry on next OnLoad". The throw is **deterministic** (static handler), so the hook **never**
registered - present on `main` since commit `d398cac43` (2026-03-22). It does not crash and did not
wipe recordings (unlike the sibling `OnGameSceneSwitchClearEscrow` NRE fixed by `a73950f90` in the
logistics-m4 work / PR #1180); it just meant `OnMainMenuTransition` never fired, so its main-menu
session reset (`initialLoadDone`, pending-cleanup clears, `PlaybackScopeTracker.Reset`,
`RouteStore.ClearAllEscrow`) and its **unconditional per-scene-switch**
`LedgerOrchestrator.FlushStalePendingRecoveryFunds` + `RecoveryPayoutContextStore.Clear` were inert
for ~3 months.

**Fix:** make `OnMainMenuTransition` (and `RegisterMainMenuHook`) instance methods, subscribe
idempotently (Remove-then-Add, mirroring `SubscribeVesselLifecycleEvents`), drop the register-once
`mainMenuHookRegistered` static flag and the misleading try/catch, and unsubscribe in `OnDestroy` so
the now-instance subscription does not leak a stale `Target` across scenario re-instantiation.
Regression guard: the parameterized `ScenarioGameEventHandlerContractTests.ScenarioGameEventHandler_MustBeInstanceMethod_NotStatic`
(now covers all six subscribed ParsekScenario handlers). Because removing `static`
re-activates ~3 months of dormant session-reset + ledger/recovery-funds logic, this landed as its own
commit merged onto `logistics-m4-multistop` (PR #1180). **In-game playtest (REQUIRED, still PENDING):** (1) return
to the main menu from flight/KSC - confirm no crash and a subsequently loaded save starts clean;
(2) load a different save without restarting KSP - confirm no stale state bleeds between saves;
(3) recovery-funds accounting - confirm the now-active per-scene-switch flush does not double-flush,
mis-attribute, or wrongly clear pending recovery payouts; watch `KSP.log` for the registration now
succeeding and any new per-scene-switch ledger activity. **Playtest result: PENDING.**

## Fixed - Better Time Warp support: snapshot stock warp altitude limits before the mod zeroes them (branch `bettertimewarp-support`)

**Investigation:** BetterTimeWarpContinued (cloned at `mods/BetterTimeWarpContinued/`) raises the warp ceiling by reassigning `TimeWarp.fetch.warpRates` / `physicsWarpRates` and overriding every body's `timeWarpAltitudeLimits` to `{0,0,0,0,0,0,100000,2000000}` at `MainMenu` startup. No Harmony, no programmatic warp/time control. A full trace of Parsek's warp reads found everything safe: value-threshold reads (`ShouldSuppressVisualFx` >10×, `ShouldSuppressGhosts` >50×, map-reseed >1×) stay correct at any rate; index/`>0` reads (`CurrentRateIndex`, `SetRate(0)`, time-jump/rewind save-restore `SetRate(index)`) are unaffected since the 8-rails/4-physics index structure is preserved; no hardcoded rate tables anywhere.

**Bug (benign):** `FlightRecorder.ComputeApproachAltitude(CelestialBody)` prefers `body.timeWarpAltitudeLimits[4]` (KSP's 100× warp limit) as the airless-body recording-split approach threshold. Better Time Warp zeroes index [4], and `CelestialBody` objects persist for the whole session, so by the time Parsek reads the array in flight it is already 0 → the `[4] > 0` guard fails → Parsek silently falls back to `body.Radius * 0.15` (clamped [5000, 200000]). Not a crash; the split altitude just degrades off the stock per-body value.

**Fix:** new `StockWarpAltitudeLimits` + a `[KSPAddon(KSPAddon.Startup.PSystemSpawn, true)]` capturer that registers `PSystemManager.Instance.OnPSystemReady` (same hook ContractConfigurator uses) — it fires during `PSystemSpawn`, before the `MainMenu` addons that override the limits — and snapshots each body's stock `timeWarpAltitudeLimits` (cloned). `ComputeApproachAltitude` now routes through the pure `SelectApproachAltitude(stock, live, radius)`: prefer the captured stock value (stock-first by design: the split threshold is a stock notion, not a warp-safety knob), then the live array, then the radius fallback. The capture is **write-once** — once a non-empty snapshot exists it is never overwritten, so a later `OnPSystemReady` re-fire (Kopernicus PSystem rebuild) reading the already-zeroed live arrays cannot clobber the good snapshot; the addon is `DontDestroyOnLoad` + unsubscribes in `OnDestroy`. Fail-safe: the cache is always either empty (⇒ behavior identical to before) or correct, never wrong. In-game proof line: `[StockWarpLimits] captured stock timeWarpAltitudeLimits for N bodies`. Unit-tested in `StockWarpAltitudeLimitsTests` (selection precedence + negative fall-through, capture/lookup, clone isolation against both in-place edit and reference reassignment, write-once-cannot-clobber, all-invalid leaves uncaptured); in-game `StockWarpLimitsCaptured` (FLIGHT) asserts the capture ran and the body-name key matches the lookup.

**Residual (pre-existing, not mod-specific, NOT closed here):** the higher rates Better Time Warp unlocks amplify the known map-render-at-high-warp issues (warp-reseed lag, icon teleport) and make on-rails recording sample more coarsely (could skip an atmosphere/SOI boundary). Both already occur at stock 100000×.

## Fixed - looped re-aim span>synodic mission: correct transfer at EVERY relaunch via synodic-multiple cadence (branch `reaim-synodic-multiple-cadence`)

**Bug:** a looping interplanetary re-aim mission whose recorded flight is LONGER than the Kerbin->destination transfer window (span > synodic, e.g. s15 "Kerbal X #2", span/synodic ~1.185) re-aimed correctly only at the FIRST relaunch. Root cause: `ReaimWindowPlanner` had two clocks - a RELAUNCH clock (`RelaunchUTForWindow(k) = D0 + k*cadence`, where the body-relative escape leg + the #1172 LAN-rotated park sit) and a DEPARTURE clock (`DepartureUTForWindow(k) = D0 + k*synodic`, where the transfer is aimed). The F2 park-end override (the only path that aims the transfer at LIVE Duna) fires only when the two coincide. For a normal mission (synodic > span) cadence = max(span, synodic) = synodic, so the clocks coincide every window. For span > synodic the cadence was `max(span, synodic) = span` (NOT a synodic multiple), so the clocks diverged by `k*(span - synodic)` and only window 0 was correct (the F2 gate fell back to the sane-but-not-live Increment-1 path at k>=1).

**Fix:** make the relaunch cadence the smallest synodic MULTIPLE >= span (`Ceiling(span / synodic - 1e-9) * synodic`, the `-1e-9` mirroring `QuantizeCadenceToMultipleOfP` so a sub-ulp-above-synodic span never spuriously doubles a normal mission's cadence) AND step the departure clock by that same cadence (`DepartureUTForWindow` now uses `CadenceSeconds`, the SAME expression as `RelaunchUTForWindow`). The two clocks are now bit-identical for the same `k`, so they coincide at EVERY window: the F2 override fires every relaunch, the transfer reaches the destination's live position, and because the cadence is >= span each loop finishes before the next begins (a single instance, no self-overlap). Normal missions (synodic > span) and direct transfers (`DepartedFromHeliocentricPark = false`) are byte-identical (Ceiling gives 1*synodic => cadence == synodic => departure unchanged; the override path is park-gated). Behaviorally: the ghost relaunches every Nth synodic window with a hidden inter-window gap.

**Supersedes + retires the self-overlap milestone.** This closes the every-window transfer-aim gap that the deferred "Re-aim SELF-OVERLAP scheduling milestone" (Approach A, Increment 2) existed to solve, WITHOUT the overlap machinery. The now-obsolete and dangerous self-overlap scaffolding was removed: `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.ShouldFlipToSelfOverlapCadence` + its `effectiveOverlapCadence`-flip block (it gated on the RAW synodic + span>synodic, which this fix does not change, so a flip would have forced `UnitMemberOverlaps` true and re-engaged overlap, contradicting the single-instance contract), the `ParsekConfig.ReaimSelfOverlapEnabled` flag, and the dead uncalled `ReaimPlaybackResolver.TryResolveWindowSegmentsForWindow` explicit-window overload. The resolver's `(member, window)` cache + `TryResolveWindowSegmentsCore` + eviction band are kept (the live currentUT path uses them). The Missions-window loop-period cell now reads the actual relaunch cadence (`CadenceSeconds`) instead of `1*synodic` so the period and the T-minus countdown agree.

**Residual seams it does NOT close (separate, still open):** (a) the #1174 launch-rotation seam (body-fixed ascent vs inertial escape - #1174's per-loop launch hold still handles it, additively); (b) the deferred cross-SOI ~62 deg patched-conic encounter kink at the destination SOI handoff.

**Tests:** `ReaimWindowPlannerTests` updated to the coinciding contract (cadence == smallest synodic multiple >= span; `DepartureUTForWindow(k) == RelaunchUTForWindow(k)` at every window for the span>synodic shape; the #1172 park-placement re-proved at cadence=2*synodic; normal-case byte-identical; s15-shape focused test; a sub-epsilon-span cadence-floor guard test) and the self-overlap-flip / explicit-window-overload tests removed. Full headless suite green (15,860).

---

## Changed - Recordings tab loop/period restricted to player-viewable recordings

The Recordings window/tab now shows the per-row **Loop** checkbox and **Period** cell only for recordings the player can actually watch as a flying ghost — a takeoff / landing (launch site, Prelaunch start, or `SegmentPhase` atmo/approach/surface), a docking segment, or a valid relative track approaching a base or station (a `ReferenceFrame.Relative` `TrackSection` with a resolvable anchor). Pure orbital coasts (a map line only, no watchable flight phase) and debris no longer get a loop toggle. The header / group / chain aggregate Loop toggles and the bulk-write exclude the same non-loopable rows so they stay consistent with which rows show a toggle.

Implemented by routing `RecordingsTableUI.ShouldSuppressRowLoopUi`, `ComputeLoopAggregate`, and `BulkSetLoopPlayback` through the (previously dead-code, now extended) `Recording.IsLoopableRecording`, which gained a relative-track case (`Recording.HasViewableRelativeTrack`, excluding parent-anchored children/debris). The split optimizer already re-derives `SegmentPhase` per half and leaves a split-off coast without the launch's start fields, so a coast tail correctly loses the toggle while the ascent half keeps it.

The visibility gate is paired with a model-layer guarantee so that "no loop toggle means it does not loop": the OnLoad sweep `RecordingStore.SanitizeDebrisLoopPlayback` was generalized to `RecordingStore.SanitizeNonLoopableLoopPlayback`, which clears a stale `LoopPlayback=true` on any `!IsLoopableRecording(rec)` recording (debris and pure orbital coasts alike; `IsLoopableRecording` already returns false for debris, so the predicate subsumes the former debris-only sweep). Post-change the UI never sets the flag on a non-loopable row (per-row toggle hidden, bulk write skips it) and the load sweep clears any pre-existing one, so the engine never loops a recording that has no toggle. This does NOT touch Mission looping: a Mission loops via `Mission.LoopPlayback` + the shared span clock and never reads a member recording's `LoopPlayback` (the loop-unit interception in `GhostPlaybackEngine` sits above the per-recording loop gate), and standalone chain looping is per-recording so the real legs keep their flags while only the no-loop-value coast legs are cleared.

---

## Fixed - looped re-aim launch->escape render seam (span>=synodic regime), borrow-at-launch / repay-at-SOI-exit

**Symptom (mission `s15` / `Kerbal X #2`, recording `aa48920e`):** an engaged re-aim loop whose recorded span exceeds its Kerbin->destination synodic period (so `cadence == spanDuration != synodic`) renders the body-fixed launch ascent + Kerbin parking + escape (all inside Kerbin SOI) rotated 82-220 deg away from the frozen inertial escape conic. The in-SOI segments are drawn every frame at the LIVE Kerbin rotation (`GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer.BuildLegVectorLine` -> `CelestialBody.GetWorldSurfacePosition`), but when the loop replays time-shifted Kerbin has spun to a different orientation than at the recorded launch, while the recorded escape `OrbitSegment` and the heliocentric transfer (both inertial) did not rotate. The launch->escape handoff opens a visible map/tracking-station gap and the icon jumps across it at high warp. `PadAlignLaunch` (the existing fix for the `cadence == synodic` case) deliberately bails here because it cannot quantize the loop period to whole sidereal days without shifting which synodic window each loop catches.

**Fix (design `docs/dev/design-reaim-launch-hold-seam.md`, BORROW-AT-LAUNCH / REPAY-AT-SOI-EXIT; render/playback-time only, recorded data IMMUTABLE):** a complementary per-loop launch ALIGNMENT for the regime PadAlignLaunch declines. For replayed loop N the launch happens `delta_N` EARLIER (at `L_N - delta_N`) where `delta_N = (Off_N mod T_sid + T_sid) mod T_sid` in `[0, T_sid)`, `Off_N = (phaseAnchorUT - spanStartUT) + N*cadence`, `T_sid = abs(launch body sidereal day)`. Launching `delta_N` earlier makes `currentUT - spanStartUT` a whole multiple of `T_sid` throughout the verbatim in-Kerbin-SOI replay, so the live Kerbin rotation equals the recorded rotation and the body-fixed ascent / parking / escape coincide with the frozen inertial escape conic (seam closes), launch on the real pad. The borrowed `delta_N` is REPAID as a COAST hold inserted at the Kerbin-SOI-exit boundary, so everything from the SOI exit onward (heliocentric transfer, trans-target burn, destination arrival + its arrival hold, landing) is UNCHANGED vs baseline (targeting + the Duna arrival hold are byte-identical). There is NO pad absence: the launch is earlier and the ghost briefly coasts at the SOI boundary. (This replaces the earlier FLAWED forward-shift attempt that launched at `L_N + H_N`, rendered the ghost absent before launch, and subtracted `(W_N - H_N)` from the arrival hold; that overflowed the cadence budget and added a pre-launch wait.) Implemented as:
- `GhostPlaybackLogic.ComputePerLoopLaunchAdvanceSeconds` (pure, the backward residual `delta_N = Off_N mod T_sid`; mirrors `ComputePerLoopArrivalHoldSeconds`: sawtooth in N bounded to `[0, T_sid)`, degenerate/NaN -> 0).
- `ReaimClassifier` now records `RecordedSoiExitUT = segs[helioIdx].startUT` (the launch-body->heliocentric handoff). For a heliocentric-parking departure (s15) this is BEFORE `RecordedDepartureUT` (the trans-target burn from the park) - the park + burn are inertial, so the repay belongs at the SOI exit, not the departure burn.
- `TryComputeSpanLoopUT` computes `delta_N` after `cycleIndex` (so cadence / phase anchor / cycle index / the resolver's window-index<->departure map are unchanged), launches at `L_N - delta_N` (a borrow-from-the-prior-cycle's-idle-tail model: region A renders the current cycle's instance, region B renders the next instance's early launch in this cycle's tail so the navigable launch time `L_{N+1} - delta_{N+1}` actually shows the launch), and inserts a `delta_N` coast hold at the SOI-exit boundary via the existing `ApplyArrivalHoldToPhase` machinery (composed sequentially with the Duna arrival hold on one phase axis). The `delta_N > slack_{N-1}` edge (the zero-slack loops where the per-loop arrival hold fills the launching cycle) is now closed by the BOUNDARY-OVERLAP launch render (see the follow-up below); the cap helper is kept for the diagnostic only.
- The Duna-side arrival hold is UNCHANGED (the `(W_N - H_N)` subtraction is REMOVED): the SOI-exit repay nets to zero with the earlier launch, so the SOI entry / arrival occur at the same live UT as baseline and `W_N` aligns the destination rotation phase with no compensation.
- `MissionLoopUnitBuilder` gates `LaunchHoldEngaged = re-aim engaged && !pad.Applied && plan.Supported && a valid SOI-exit boundary` (no double-correction with PadAlignLaunch), resolves `T_sid = bodyInfo.RotationPeriod(plan.LaunchBody)`, carries `RecordedSoiExitUT`, and emits an Info `Reaim` line. `PadAlignLaunch` is unchanged and STAYS for `cadence == synodic`.
- The map / TS / KSC surfaces inherit the shift for free via `ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT` (reads the launch-alignment + SOI-exit fields from the `LoopUnit`); the unpacked-arg call sites (`GhostPlaybackEngine.UpdateUnitMemberPlayback`, its watch-clock resolver, the loop-synced-debris parent clock, `ParsekKSC.UpdateUnitMemberPlayback`) forward the new `soiExitAtUT` arg. The `HiddenPreLaunchHold` decision + pre-launch-absence paths are REMOVED (no pad absence). The navigable launch time (`MissionsWindowUI.ComputeNextRelaunchUT`) reports `L_N - delta_N`. `bodyFixedShift` is untouched.

**Tests:** `LaunchHoldTests` (pure helper: realigns `(Off_N - delta_N)` mod T_sid, range `[0,T_sid)`, already-aligned->0, degenerate/NaN->0, sawtooth in N), `LaunchHoldClockTests` (in-SOI rotation alignment through ascent/parking/escape via both region A + region B, SOI-exit repay coast hold, post-SOI-and-onward byte-identical to baseline, NO pad absence, targeting + cadence==synodic / not-engaged byte-identical, arrival hold unchanged, delta>slack capped, TS-sampler parity), `LaunchHoldLoggingTests` (the per-loop Verbose `Reaim` launch-advance line fires with non-zero `delta_N` across two cycles + the builder Info-line / ctor-wiring source-text gate), `GhostPlaybackEngineTests` (watch<->render<->TS clock parity: early launch at spanStart, post-SOI baseline, never absent below span), `MissionsWindowPeriodicityDisplayTests` (next-relaunch reports `L_N - delta_N`).

**Note:** this is the body-fixed-ascent vs inertial-escape ROTATION seam. It is distinct from (and does not address) the separate cross-SOI heliocentric-transfer encounter seam tracked in the "Looped re-aim interplanetary transfer: no continuous encounter into the destination SOI" item below (that is the deferred patched-conic-chain rework). Confirm in the s15 playtest whether the cross-SOI residual is now the dominant remaining artifact.

**Follow-up - BOUNDARY-OVERLAP launch render (closes the zero-slack `delta_N > slack` residual):** on ZERO-SLACK loops (the per-loop Duna arrival hold fills the launching cycle, `slack_{N-1} == 0`) the cap above truncated the launch advance to 0 and the seam stayed open (`residualDeg` up to ~211 on s15 loop 19). Design `docs/dev/plan-launch-boundary-overlap.md` (Design B) closes it by rendering the early-launching NEXT instance N+1 as a SECONDARY ghost during the borrow window, so the launch realigns without being capped - the previous (primary) instance is far downstream near Duna by then, so two ghosts at different places. Engaged ONLY when `delta_N > slack_{N-1}` (the gate guarantees already-aligned slack&gt;0 loops + the targeting path are BYTE-IDENTICAL). Render/playback-time only; recorded data IMMUTABLE. Implemented as:
- `GhostPlaybackLogic.ComputeBoundaryOverlapAdvanceSeconds` (gated: the old capped advance when `rawDelta <= cappedDelta`, the FULL raw delta otherwise). `ComputeCappedLaunchAdvanceSeconds` is KEPT (it remains the `residualDeg` source of truth and the diagnostic).
- `GhostPlaybackLogic.ComputeSpanLoopFrame` (new) returns the primary loopUT/cycle PLUS an optional secondary (loopUT/cycle = N+1) present only inside the borrow window AND only when the boundary overlap engages; `TryComputeSpanLoopUT` is the primary-only wrapper (every existing caller byte-identical). On an aligned loop the OLD single-output region-B flip is preserved (no secondary); on an engaged loop the primary stays on N (camera never yanked) and the secondary carries N+1. New `DecideBoundaryOverlapSecondaryRender` + `ResolveTrackingStationSampleFrame` seams.
- `GhostPlaybackEngine` positions the secondary in `overlapGhosts[i]` STORAGE via `UpdateBoundaryOverlapSecondary` / `SpawnBoundaryOverlapSecondary` / `PositionBoundaryOverlapSecondaryAt` (audio-muted, `isBoundaryOverlapSecondary` flag, demoted-shell lifecycle), NEVER the self-overlap `UpdateOverlapPlayback` / expiry path; the unconditional overlap teardown is GATED on a live secondary; the watch camera sites (`WatchModeController.FindWatchedGhostState` / `TryGetWatchedGhostAnchorWorldPosition`) EXCLUDE `isBoundaryOverlapSecondary`.
- `GhostMapPresence` creates the secondary's ProtoVessel as an `overlapInstanceVessels[(recIdx, N+1)]` entry INSIDE `RunOverlapPerInstanceSweep` (registered in `drivenThisFrame` so the reaper spares it; `TryEnsureBoundaryOverlapSecondaryInstance` + `ReapBoundaryOverlapSecondaryInstances`); the in-SOI escape window resolves to a recorded `Segment` source (verified on aa48920e: `Kerbin 2547277751.0-2547281403.4`, sma 1.37e6, ecc 0.538, `source=Segment`), so it is loop-shift driven like an overlap instance. `GetGhostVesselPidForRecording` checks `vesselsByRecordingIndex` first, so the secondary pid never shadows the primary.
- `GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer` draws the secondary's in-SOI ascent leg as an additive non-ownership second head keyed on the secondary pid (`ResolveTrackingStationSampleFrame` second-head pass + same-leg defensive guard); `MissionsWindowUI.ComputeNextRelaunchUT` reads `ComputeBoundaryOverlapAdvanceSeconds` so the "Warp to..." time lands on the realigned (uncapped) launch. `ParsekKSC` unchanged (no map surface - the seam is a map/TS artifact).
- **Pre-Segment ascent ICON fix (playtest follow-up):** the secondary's proto-vessel map presence (icon + escape conic) cannot exist during atmospheric ascent — there is no `OrbitSegment` to seed it, so `ResolveMapPresenceGhostSource` returns `None` and the create defers until the recorded escape Segment (~274s later). Item 46's "resolves to a recorded `Segment`" describes the POST-ascent window only; the ascent itself is a pre-Segment gap, confirmed in playtest by `boundary-overlap secondary map-presence: created=False source=None` lines climbing `lagFromSpanStartSec` 30->217s+. So the ascent polyline drew with no icon riding it for those minutes (map view; TS only looked clean because warp skipped the gap). Fix: the marker passes draw the secondary's ascent icon as an ADDITIVE non-proto marker riding the shared polyline. `GhostMapPresence.TryResolveBoundaryOverlapSecondaryMarker` (gates map-surface / non-debris / non-null, then delegates the live-secondary test to `ResolveTrackingStationSampleFrame`) feeds the secondary head UT + cycle to `DrawOneOverlapInstanceMarker` (flight `ParsekUI.DrawMapMarkers`) / `DrawOneTsOverlapInstanceMarker` (`ParsekTrackingStation`), the same per-instance primitive the self-overlap markers use; it self-gates per cycle (once the Segment proto icon owns the cycle it returns false — no double). The blocker was that the per-instance head path (`TryGetLiveOverlapHeadUTs`) gates on `ShouldDriveOverlapPerInstance`, false for a launch-hold (non-overlap) member, so the secondary fell through to the single-marker proto gate that only draws the primary (far downstream near the destination). The marker rides the SAME `set.legs[li]` ascent leg the second-head pass stamps `lastDrawnFrame` on this frame, so `TryAnchorMarkerToPolyline` finds it. NO `continue`: the primary marker still draws. Inert for every non-launch-hold member / aligned loop / non-map surface.

**Boundary-overlap tests:** `BoundaryOverlapClockTests` (gated advance capped-vs-full-raw; zero-slack HasSecondary inside the borrow window / false outside; §7 invariants: primary effectiveSpan never truncates, boundary continuity secondary->next-primary, in-SOI secondary rotation-aligned residualDeg~0; byte-identity fence: wrapper==frame primary, aligned loop never has a secondary, schedule:null windowIndex unchanged; per-member `DecideBoundaryOverlapSecondaryRender` / `ResolveTrackingStationSampleFrame`), `BoundaryOverlapLoggingTests` (`secondaryActive=True` + residualDeg~0 on a zero-slack loop, the one-shot `boundary-overlap engaged` line, no `launch-advance-capped` WARN on engaged loops, no secondary on aligned loops), `MissionsWindowPeriodicityDisplayTests.ComputeNextRelaunchUT_BoundaryOverlapEngaged_ReportsLNMinusRawDelta` (the engaged loop reports `L_N - rawDelta`, earlier than the old capped target), and in-game `BoundaryOverlapSecondary_IsMutedFlaggedAndUnwatched` / `_AtMostOnePerRecording` / `_MapInstanceMatchesSecondHead` (`GhostLifecycle` category). Pre-Segment ascent-icon fix: `BoundaryOverlapClockTests.SecondaryMarker_*` (the additive-marker gate: draws at the secondary head in the borrow window; never on a non-map surface / debris / null recording / aligned loop) + in-game `BoundaryOverlapSecondary_MarkerResolvesDuringAscentGap` (the resolver surfaces the secondary even when no map instance exists yet — the gap it covers).

**Review hardening (H1/H2/M1/L1, adversarial review of the boundary-overlap render):** four reachable items fixed (no criticals; clock / watch isolation / audio mute / map lifecycle / targeting byte-identity / persistence verified solid). H1: `forwardArcCache` was recording-id-keyed, so during the borrow window the primary + secondary forward passes (run for the SAME recording in one frame at disjoint heads) collided — the secondary overwrote the primary's cached arcs and the primary's forward conic vanished; fixed by namespacing the secondary under `ForwardArcDictKey` (the `WalkBoth` cell IS reached in the validated single-recording case — the old "not reached" comment was wrong). H2: the engine's boundary-secondary dispatch sat after the `decision != Render` early returns, so a two-recording CHAIN launch member (primary downstream, out of window) tore the secondary 3D mesh down before drawing it; fixed by hoisting the decision above the block and driving the secondary (hiding, not destroying, the primary) when the primary is hidden. M1: `GetGhostVesselPidForRecording` fell through to the secondary's pid for a launch member with a renderHidden primary (no `vesselsByRecordingIndex` entry); fixed with a `boundaryOverlapSecondaryPids` exclusion set on the fall-through readers (the polyline's direct call still gets the secondary pid). L1: corrected stale comments claiming the non-owned secondary leg's `ghostPid` hides its proto orbit line (it is inert metadata; `TryDrawLeg` ignores `ghostPid`). Tests: `GhostTrajectoryPolylineBuildTests.ForwardArcDictKey_*` (H1), in-game `BoundaryOverlapSecondary_EngineMeshSurvivesHiddenPrimary` (H2) / `_DoesNotShadowRecordingPid` (M1).

**Launch->escape near-meet gap (small-gap chord bridge):** with re-aim ENGAGED the launch alignment collapses the ascent->escape seam to a few degrees, but a small visible gap remained (widest at liftoff, closing as the icon climbs) because the forward-drawn ascent end LEADS the icon at the live rotation and lands short of the inertial conic, and the merge-slice bridge is muted below 5deg (its ~200-370km bulge dwarfs a small gap). Fixed by adding a STRAIGHT-CHORD band to the seam bridge: `ClassifySeamBridgeByAngle` routes `(0.5deg, 5deg]` to a zero-bulge chord (`TryBuildSeamBridgeChordLocalPoints`, leg end -> conic near endpoint, no conic clip), `(5deg, 45deg]` still the merge slice, `<=0.5deg`/`>45deg` still skip. Re-fits per frame; `src=chord` in the bridge-draw log. Tests: `GhostTrajectoryPolylineBuildTests.SeamBridgeChord_*` + `ClassifySeamBridgeByAngle_FourBands`. (NOTE: stale-log trap — an investigation agent first mis-read a June-15 log where this mission was still faithful-fallback at ~162deg/45deg-MAX-rejected; the live build engages alignment and the real gap is the sub-5deg one. The deeper "correct" fix — de-rotate the forward ascent / extend re-aim alignment to faithful loops — stays deferred; the chord is the minimal render-only close.)
