- **Design note SHIPPED (2026-06-10, branch `design-mission-phasing-alignment`):** `docs/dev/design-mission-phasing-alignment.md` records the nine decisions (D1-D9): anchor must EXIST in the save, live orbit only, no recorded-orbit derivation fallback, vanished anchors fail closed (resolves the period-cell-vs-retired-member UX incoherence); loops keep the live-PID anchor contract; the phasing-loiter knob is FULLY AUTOMATIC (kept revs derived from the solved relaunch schedule; no toggle, an opt-out is added only on playtest demand), first play always faithful; per-cycle k_N is a NEW small (pad window x kept revs) enumeration on top of the existing zero-drift primitives (no new solver math), k_N in [1, recorded+10], cuts restricted to BEFORE the first rendezvous (a timeline-rigidity guard that also auto-aligns undock/redock events); honest window math recorded: without the knob a 1-degree station tolerance admits ~0.5% of pad windows (tens of Kerbin days between aligned launches), so the knob is load-bearing for routes, not an optimization; Tier 1 = `VesselOrbital` constraint + extraction flip for exactly-one same-parent closed-orbit anchor; Tier 2 = arrival hold with T_station, dual-constraint destinations stay fail-closed with `SolveArrivalWindow` wiring as a post-M4c follow-up. Build order: M4a Tier 1 -> M4b knob (own plan doc; the per-launch-cuts span-clock seam; shared with M-MIS-2 P4's keepRevs API) -> M4c Tier 2.
- **M4a SHIPPED (2026-06-10, branch `mission-vesselorbital-tier1`):** Tier 1 `VesselOrbital` end-to-end per `docs/dev/plans/mission-vesselorbital-tier1.md`. EMITTED shape: exactly ONE same-parent closed-orbit vessel anchor across the included window -> `VesselOrbital(pid@Body)` (live period via the new `IBodyInfo.TryGetVesselOrbit`, resolved through `FlightRecorder.FindVesselByPid` so ghost map proto vessels never count; offset = first rendezvous UT - UT0; same-pid sections collapse to the earliest UT); tolerance = period * 1deg/360 (`StationPhaseToleranceDegrees`, branched BEFORE the SOI formula); solver ranks the kind with Orbital (lone-constraint method label `single-vessel-orbital`); period cell reads "(station window)". REJECTED shapes (fail closed, `UnsupportedRendezvous` + logged reason): pid-unrecorded anchors, 2+ distinct pids, unresolvable / non-closed anchors, cross-parent stations (M4c), null launch body. D3 drift amber: live vs recorded anchor period (covering non-predicted OrbitSegment of the section's `anchorRecordingId`) past 2% rel tolerance tints the T- cell amber with the reason as tooltip; display-only, logged once per transition. `DestinationConstraintExtractor` defensively skips the kind (M4c comment). Alignment stays RARE until M4b supplies the loiter knob (design 5.3).
- **M4a playtest fix (2026-06-11, same branch):** the first in-game run (orbital docking save, logs `2026-06-11_0009_m4a-station-playtest`) hit the pid==0 reject on the HEADLINE scenario: the recorder zeroes `anchorVesselId` whenever it stamps `anchorRecordingId`, so anchor-recording-only is the NORMAL recorded rendezvous shape. Fixed: the classifier resolves the pid through the committed anchor recording (recorded pid + launch guid), `TryGetVesselOrbit` gained the guid identity gate (craft-baked pid of a different launch fails closed), and both recorded shapes of the same anchor merge to the earliest rendezvous. The observed 810s vessel pile-up was the pre-existing faithful-path self-overlap (Auto overlap cadence = span/20), resolved by the mission now phase-locking. **Second retest fix (2026-06-11):** the dock merge makes anchoring MUTUAL (partner segments in-tree anchor the craft; craft anchors the partner), which read as two distinct anchors (multi-rendezvous reject). The classifier now partitions anchors against the mission's SELF launch line (earliest member pid+guid), reattributes self-anchored sections to their owning member (the partner), merges both directions to one target at the FIRST rendezvous UT, and treats all-self anchoring as no-constraint (not a reject); `ClassifyVesselOrbitalConstraint` returns Emitted / NoForeignAnchor / Rejected.
- **M4b SHIPPED (2026-06-11, branch `mission-loiter-knob`; plan `docs/dev/plans/mission-loiter-knob.md`):** the per-cycle phasing-loiter knob. `ReaimLoiterCompressor.DetectRuns` exposes run metadata (ComputeCuts is now a thin wrapper); `TryFindNextScheduleK` gained a shiftable-group overload (per pad window k, enumerate the rev shift d in [1-R, +10] by |d| ascending with cuts preferred on ties; residual = CircularPhaseError(k*T_anchor + d*T_park, P_j)); `TryBuildRelaunchSchedule` partitions constraints into shiftable (reference event after the phasing run end) vs unshiftable on the post-Drop effective list, with engagement rules (anchor event before the run, at least one shiftable, UT0==spanStart, owner-detected launch-body run ending before the rendezvous/SOI guard) all failing closed to today's schedule; `MissionRelaunchSchedule` materializes per-launch `LaunchTimingEntry` (kept revs, cuts for d<0, last-rev wrap extension for d>0, per-launch effective span) in its lazy walk and enforces next-launch spacing >= max(minSpacing, effSpan_last); the span clock's schedule branch consumes the entries (cut skip + `ApplyLoiterExtensionToPhase` whole-rev sawtooth + per-launch tail), knob-less schedules byte-identical. RouteLoopClock audited: `IsDockCrossing` is sawtooth-safe (dock after the guard, dockCycleIndex holds during the wrap). Earlier pre-guard runs get static keepRevs=1 cuts. Re-aim consumption of the keepRevs API stays M-MIS-2 P4; uniform-cadence (non-scheduled) compression deliberately out of scope. Post-review fix: runs not entirely inside [spanStart, guard] (trimmed missions opening mid-loiter) never produce cuts; the knob fails closed instead. **Retest fixes (2026-06-11, logs `2026-06-11_2127_m4b-knob-retest`):** two findings. (1) The knob aligned only 2-3 consecutive pad windows before slipping out of the 1-degree station tolerance (the d=k rev ladder drifts ~2.5s/window vs a 6.76s budget; gaps of ~40-60 days followed, and the Missions window's 19-day AVERAGE interval read as conflicting with the 6h T- countdown - reproduced exactly by simulating the schedule from the logged parameters). `StationPhaseToleranceDegrees` widened 1 -> 3 (sustains ~8 consecutive windows per family; cost: the recorded ABSOLUTE final approach can visually miss the live station by up to ~40km at the tolerance edge - the craft-side approach in this save has NO Relative sections; the dock loop-clock marker is unaffected). (2) The map icon teleported ~46 degrees during the rendezvous burns: a knob rev shift replays post-loiter events off the pad-rotation-aligned grid, and Absolute BODY-FIXED point sections (burn arcs recorded as lat/lon/alt) resolve against the live body rotation, so they rendered rotated by shift*360/T_rot while orbital checkpoint sections stayed inertially correct - the icon snapped between the two at every section toggle. Fix: per-frame body-fixed DEROTATION, shift = (currentUT - launchUT) - (loopUT - spanStart) (exact in every clock phase incl. the wrap sawtooth; identically 0 for knob-less schedules), applied as a longitude shift + spin-axis attitude rotation (`TrajectoryMath.FrameTransform.ShiftLongitudeDegrees`/`ShiftSurfaceRelativeRotation`) at the flight positioner (ambient per-call channel via `GhostPlaybackState.bodyFixedShiftSeconds`), the flight-map marker resolver, and the TS marker resolver; the map polyline needs nothing (its conic-seam anchor already rotates body-fixed legs onto the bracketing conics geometrically). KSC-scene point legs keep the old behavior (no orbital-rendezvous visual concern there; revisit on evidence). **MapRender high-warp residuals (2026-06-12, logs `2026-06-12_1756_m4b-icon-retest2`, tracer ON; filed after the endpoint-tail gate fix verified clean):** three remaining artifact classes, none a knob clock/solver defect. (1) ~~Creation-frame icon blip~~ FIXED on the branch: the proto loads at the raw recorded-epoch orbit and the effUT icon drive only repositions it on the next OrbitDriver tick, so the first rendered frame sat up to 143 deg off its line (tracer: creation-frame icon-off-orbit + icon-teleport); `ForceImmediateIconDrive` now issues one explicit `updateFromParameters` (routes through `GhostOrbitIconDrivePatch`) after the orbit + loop epoch shift are registered on the Segment/EndpointTail create branches. (2) Reseed-lag icon jumps at extreme warp (344x-1000x): the 0.5s real-time map-orbit reseed spans ~170-500s of game time per tick at those rates, so the icon rides a stale segment orbit and snaps ~1 Mm along-orbit on reseed (4 tracer events, all mid-cycle, fromOrbit==toOrbit). Fix direction: warp-scaled reseed cadence or head-left-segment eager reseed extended to the icon drive. (3) Anchored-leg/bridge curvature morph: the conic-seam anchor's rotation angle drifts at EXACTLY the body rotation rate (tracer: rotAngle 136.9->133.6 over ~200s game on the post-loiter burn leg) because body-fixed leg points rotate with the planet while the bracketing conics are inertial - the per-frame re-anchor reshapes the cached bridge arcs visibly at warp. Pre-existing (re-aim era); knob extensions anchor legs across ~134+ deg making it prominent. Fix direction: pin the anchor angle per loop cycle (recompute only on cycle/segment change) or draw anchored legs in the inertial frame outright. **Map-icon retest fix (2026-06-12, logs `2026-06-12_1731_m4b-derotation-retest`, tracer ON):** the loop member's map icon circled a WRONG orbit and teleported at 1x->2x warp (proto re-created at the mesh->proto handoff). Tracer evidence: GhostCreated with `orbitSource=endpoint-tail` and a garbage orbit (sma=809331 ecc=0.936 retrograde, epoch=recorded end - the recording ends DOCKED, so its endpoint is not a valid free orbit) while the LINE drew the correct covering segment; `icon-off-orbit angleIconVsOrbitEff=126.7`. Root cause: `ShouldOverrideVisibleSegmentWithEndpointTail` (the covering-segment endpoint-tail override, the documented "181 Mm cross-body bug class") had NO loop gate on the create-resolver path - the comment claimed loop members were "unconditionally suppressed" but only the TS update pass enforced it (`EndpointTailAllowedInTrackingStationUpdate`). PRE-EXISTING for any loop member whose recording ends with an eligible terminal state + fresh tail seed (not knob-specific; exposed by frequent knob cycles). Fix: `loopMemberInWindow` threaded into the pure predicate (first check, never override a covering segment for an in-window loop replay), the create-resolver's first endpoint-tail branch passes it, pinned by `ShouldOverrideVisibleSegmentWithEndpointTail_LoopMemberInWindow_NeverOverrides`. Also confirmed from this session: the Missions window period (~6d) vs T- (~1d) measure DIFFERENT things by design - the cell is the schedule's AVERAGE interval (burst gaps of 1-2d punctuated by ~38d lattice gaps; simulated exactly 6.0d from the logged parameters at the 3-degree tolerance), T- is the next launch. **Playtest fix (2026-06-11, station-save logs `2026-06-11_2111_m4b-knob-playtest`):** the knob silently disengaged on the real docking mission because the unit OWNER is the chain ROOT segment, which carries NO OrbitSegments - the parking loiter (a 3-rev run at sma 886553, T=2790.9s, ending 2268s before the rendezvous) lives in the same-launch chain CONTINUATION member. `BuildPhasingKnobInput` now gathers segments from every member sharing the owner's launch identity (`VesselLaunchIdentity.RecordingsShareLaunch`; chain segments are one vessel's sequential timeline so flattening them is safe), which also formally excludes the dock-merged partner and debris from ever driving cuts. With the fix the save's geometry aligns at nearly every pad window (d=+1 per window, ~2.5s residual vs the 6.8s tolerance) instead of one window per ~150 Kerbin days.
- **M4b destination-body fix SHIPPED (2026-06-13, branch `fix-loiter-knob-destination-body`):** the M4b phasing-loiter knob silently disengaged for a SAME-PARENT destination-body station dock (a Mun-station resupply: pad Rotation(Kerbin) + Orbital(Mun) intercept + VesselOrbital(station@Mun)). `BuildPhasingKnobInput` rule 2 only accepted a phasing parking loiter on the LAUNCH body and clamped guardUT at the first body-change segment start (the Mun SOI entry), so the Mun parking orbit (the designed phase absorber, AFTER the SOI entry) was structurally excluded; the cadence read ~1.6 Kerbin years (min ~90d / mean ~820d) instead of ~weeks. KSP.log signature: `phasing knob disengaged: ... none lie in-span before guardUT=... on body 'Kerbin'` with `runs=1`. Fix (guard GAP, not a deferral - same-parent destination dock is NOT in the M4c out-of-scope list, and the M4c emit comment already names a same-parent destination depot as Supported + knob-aligned): the guardUT body-change loop now SKIPS the launch body AND any RENDEZVOUS body (the body each VesselOrbital station orbits, read from `extraction.Constraints[i].BodyName`), clamping only at a genuine THIRD body (e.g. Minmus on a Kerbin->Mun->Minmus hop); the phasing-run candidate predicate + static-cut loop accept runs on the launch body OR a rendezvous body (`MissionLoopUnitBuilder.IsPhasingRunBodyAccepted`). Rule 3/4 partition (`TryBuildRelaunchSchedule`) is UNCHANGED and works for the Mun geometry by UT comparison alone: the Mun intercept reference event (SOI entry) lies BEFORE the parking loiter so Orbital(Mun) stays UNSHIFTABLE (pinned at the pad+Mun lattice), and the station rendezvous lies AFTER the run end so VesselOrbital(station@Mun) goes SHIFTABLE - that is what collapses the cadence. Launch-body cases (LKO-wait-for-Mun-window, Kerbin-station dock) stay byte-identical. A Verbose `phasing knob rendezvous-body loiter` line logs the destination-body selection. UI: the Missions period cell for a zero-drift scheduled unit now shows a min-max RANGE (`MissionRelaunchSchedule.MaxIntervalSeconds` + `BuildScheduledPeriodCellDisplay`/`FormatScheduledIntervalRange`, collapsing to one value within ~5%) instead of a single mean. Covered by `MissionLoiterKnobTests` (destination-body engage, launch-body regression, third-body Minmus exclusion, `IsPhasingRunBodyAccepted`), `MissionsWindowPeriodicityDisplayTests` (range + collapse), and `MissionZeroDriftScheduleTests.Schedule_MaxIntervalSeconds_*`.
  - **Diagnostic-log clarity follow-up (2026-06-14, branch `fix-phaselock-log-clarity`):** validated this fix in-game on the Mun supply route (logs `2026-06-14_1642_mun-loop-investigation`): the knob engages (`phasing knob rendezvous-body loiter ... body='Mun'`, keptRevs 6->9, d=+3, well under the +10 cap) and the schedule's launches read `within=True`. But the `PhaseLock APPLIED` headline and the `Solve` WARN reported the UNUSED fixed-cadence fallback (`residual=1402s withinTol=no`, "best-effort until the Phase-2 joint best-fit lands"), reading as if the window were inaccurate when the zero-drift schedule actually flies within tolerance. Fix (log-only, no behavior change): `PhaseLock APPLIED` now relabels the fallback verdict `fixedCadenceResidual`/`fixedCadenceWithinTol` and, when a schedule is attached, appends the schedule's OWN aggregate `scheduleWithinTol` + `scheduleWorstResidual` (`MissionRelaunchSchedule.AllLaunchesWithinTolerance` / `WorstResidualSeconds`); the `Solve` WARN drops the stale "until Phase-2 lands" tail and points to the schedule line. Covered by an extended assertion in `MissionPeriodicityTests.Build_SupportedSameParentMun_AttachesZeroDriftSchedule`. Note (unchanged, tuning not bug): the relaunch cadence for this geometry stays irregular (~3-18d gaps) because the three-constraint lattice coincides sparsely; the loiter is not the limiter (d=+3 has headroom). The lever is `StationPhaseToleranceDegrees` (already 1->3) vs approach accuracy.
- **M4c SHIPPED (2026-06-12, branch `mission-station-arrival-hold`; plan `docs/dev/plans/mission-station-arrival-hold.md`):** Tier 2 cross-parent station alignment. The classifier's rule-3 reject splits: a station orbiting a TRANSITED body (any body with an emitted Orbital constraint) now EMITS the VesselOrbital constraint, and emission never touches Support - so a same-parent destination depot (Mun/Minmus) stays Supported and rides the zero-drift schedule + M4b knob with zero new scheduling code, while a cross-parent destination depot (Duna) stays UnsupportedCrossParent and the re-aim ARRIVAL HOLD substitutes T_station for T_rot (`DestinationConstraintExtractor` gained HasStation/StationPeriodSeconds; `ArrivalHoldPlanner` picks the align period, renamed result field to `AlignPeriodSeconds`, `LoopUnit.DestRotationPeriodSeconds` -> `ArrivalAlignPeriodSeconds`). Stations around never-transited bodies still reject (reason names the no-Orbital-constraint basis). D8 fail-closed shapes (landing+station, station+constrained-moon - a deliberate widening on the same one-hold-one-period rationale - moon-orbiting stations, station-bearing Jool-class) return no hold and carry an `AmberReason` through the unit into the Missions T- cell (tint + tooltip, bypassing the phase-lock tint gate since re-aim is never phase-locked; drift amber also tints on re-aim units now). The Drop mode gates only the ROTATION hold (the setting is the transited-rotation A/B; station holds are automatic per D4), but does NOT rescue the dual case. One alignment-LOSING flip: a landing+station destination previously got the rotation hold (the station was rejected upstream, so the extractor saw landing-only); under D8 it now gets no hold + amber until SolveArrivalWindow lands. Also closed the M4a design debt: `BuildSignature` gains a station-anchor digest (resolved anchor pid -> live found/period-quantized-1s/body), so a boosted or vanished station rebuilds the cached unit instead of keeping a stale T_station. `SolveArrivalWindow` stays unwired (post-M4c follow-up). Known accepted residual: body-fixed burn arcs inside the destination SOI render rotated under a station hold (the hold aligns the station, not the rotation; landings are excluded by D8) - playtest watch item, candidate follow-up is extending the M4b derotation channel to hold-shifted re-aim units. NEEDS PLAYTEST: a cross-parent save (station in Mun or Duna orbit + recorded Kerbin resupply that transfers, rendezvouses, docks).
- **Viability:** high for Tier 1 (a third constraint in an existing solver); moderate for Tier 2. Priority is HIGH because logistics (the M1-M6 roadmap, PR #1113) is the active downstream consumer and station resupply is its headline profile.

### M-MIS-5 - Dock as an interval boundary + docked composition counts [GATED: after logistics v0 integration]

- **Investigated 2026-06-10:** confirmed still unimplemented - `MissionCompositionBuilder` interval edges come only from structural-peel UTs (MissionComposition.cs:132-143), never Dock/Board merge UTs, so a docked "AB" stretch cannot be looped in isolation and docked labels undercount (controllers gained at dock are never added). FEASIBLE with data already present: every leg carries `OriginBranchPointType` (set at MissionStructure.cs:378, includes Dock/Board), so the builder can emit a merge-UT edge on the continuing line when a leg begins via Dock/Board (+ add the joining vessel's controllers to the interval label).
- **Requirements:** keep the recorded decision (no auto Mission lifecycle on dock; topology-only). Do the boundary + the label undercount TOGETHER (they are one model change). Stays deferred until logistics/supply-routes v0 integration settles what a "docked stretch loop" must mean for routes - do not fix piecemeal (see the "docking/undocking effect on mission structure" entry below).
- **Logistics cross-link (2026-06-10, PR #1113 section 19 review):** logistics M4 ships multi-stop with mid-recording START-trims (the undock->undock shuttle runs of scenario family 3) as a DOCUMENTED LIMITATION surfaced in the rejection reason - explicitly NOT a Missions edit on their side. THIS milestone is the Missions-side fix that later lifts that limitation; schedule it after logistics M4 so the rejection text and the lift land coherently.
- **Viability:** high mechanically; gated on logistics sequencing, not on missing data.

### M-MIS-6 - Multi-moon destinations: the looped "Jool-5" mission, window-alignment cut [needs a short design note first]

- **Investigated 2026-06-10 (answers the open uncertainty):** today a Jool-5 recording loops on the FAITHFUL path only: `ReaimClassifier` supports the Kerbin->Jool transfer (Jool is a direct Sun child) but `DestinationConstraintExtractor` fails closed at 2+ SOI-entered moons, so nothing aligns the moons; each moon-relative block self-anchors to the LIVE moon while the Jool-centric inter-moon arcs replay inertially, so every encounter seam renders disconnected (the Mun-desync mechanism, once per moon). What makes it tractable WITHOUT new math: (a) all encounters shift TOGETHER under one arrival hold, so alignment needs the moons' joint CONFIGURATION to recur, not each moon independently; (b) stock Laythe:Vall:Tylo are a near-exact 1:2:4 resonance (period ratios off by ~1e-5 from rounded SMAs), so the inner-three configuration recurs every Tylo period (~211,926 s) to well within SOI tolerance - a per-loop hold in `[0, T_config)` aligns an inner-three tour exactly like the shipped `W_N` destination-rotation hold (substitute T_config for T_rot); (c) the stock major moons are tidally locked, so landing-rotation constraints collapse into orbital phase (the tidal-lock collapse `MissionPeriodicity` already implements); (d) Bop/Pol are incommensurate with the inner three - a full 5-moon tight alignment is effectively non-recurring, so those legs get Loose tolerance via the near-coincidence search or the mission fails closed to faithful (a VALID outcome, surfaced in the UI, never silent).
- **Requirements:** (1) short design note first (this is the "2+-moon mini star systems" deferred item, design doc sect. 14.4); (2) REUSE: wire the existing unwired `DestinationArrivalSolver.SolveArrivalWindow` (multi-constraint window pick over k*synodic) + generalize the per-loop hold from T_rot to a joint configuration period; (3) build the failing synthetic multi-moon test BEFORE any knob math (re-aim seam guidance); (4) intra-SOI re-aim (per-leg Lambert re-solves inside the destination system) is explicitly the SECOND cut, tracked as M-MIS-7 - only justified if this hold-based model proves insufficient in playtest.
- **Viability:** moderate - the resonant-inner-three + tidally-locked case maps onto shipped primitives; the general (Bop/Pol, non-resonant packs) case intentionally degrades to loose/faithful.

### M-MIS-7 - Intra-SOI re-aim and multi-hop targets (Jool-like systems second cut; Ike-class targets) [GATED: on M-MIS-6 playtest evidence]

- **What it is:** the recursive "mini star system" model - re-solving transfer legs INSIDE a destination system instead of only the heliocentric leg. Two consumers: (a) **moon-to-moon legs of a multi-moon tour** when the M-MIS-6 hold-based joint-configuration model is insufficient (non-resonant moon packs, Bop/Pol legs, long inter-moon loiters): per-leg Lambert re-solves in the gas giant's frame + per-leg holds at each moon-SOI seam; (b) **multi-hop TARGETS** - a target that is not a direct child of the common ancestor (Ike via Duna; rejected today by the `ReaimClassifier` single-hop guard, ReaimClassifier.cs:124-130): re-aim the heliocentric leg to the parent, then the in-SOI hop to the moon is the same intra-SOI machinery.
- **Requirements:** REUSE everything - `UvLambert` is body-agnostic (mu is a parameter), so the same `ITransferSolver` seam serves Jool-centric solves; the per-loop hold clock primitives generalize per leg. This is a genuine new subsystem (per-leg seams, recursive window scheduling): budget a full design note + the failing-test-first discipline, and do NOT build it speculatively - M-MIS-6's playtest decides whether it is needed at all.
- **Viability:** hard; deliberately last among the solver milestones.

### M-MIS-8 - Cross-tree foreign dock: loop a shared docked journey from the partner's side

- **Investigated 2026-06-10:** playback ALREADY follows cross-tree dock links via PID matching - `GhostChainWalker.MergeCrossTreeLinks` (GhostChainWalker.cs:487-574) merges chains across trees. The Missions side is single-tree by construction (`Mission.TreeId`; `MissionStructureBuilder.BuildBranchLinks` walks one tree's BranchPoints, MissionStructure.cs:331-392). The gap is a Missions-view + selection-model change (a selection spanning two trees), not a data problem.
- **Requirements:** follow the same PID dock-link pattern `GhostChainWalker` uses; decide the persistence shape (multi-tree mission vs linked-mission pairing) before building - it touches `Mission` serialization. Lowest functional urgency (UX nicety; the controller-side loop already works).
- **Viability:** moderate; bounded but touches persistence + UI.

### ~~M-MIS-9 - New-branch inclusion policy (re-fly supersede splits default to INCLUDED)~~ [DONE 2026-06-11, route-side freeze]

- **Investigated 2026-06-10:** confirmed by design - `Mission` persists only the EXCLUDED sets (Mission.cs), there is no definition-time head-id snapshot, and `MissionStore.ReconcileSelections` (MissionStore.cs:101-162) only drops stale excluded ids (one-way). A genuinely new branch silently joins every Mission on the tree.
- **Verdict (2026-06-11 investigation, `docs/dev/plan-mmis9-route-branch-freeze.md`):** the framing was overturned. Routes were ALREADY protected on their member path (`RouteStore.RevalidateSources` flips them non-ghost-driving on any SourceRef supersede/change); the real, delivery-affecting gap was branches landing OUTSIDE the member path (a re-fly fork rooted in the excluded post-undock subtree, or a switch-fly continuation merging onto the same tree with no supersede bump): the new branch silently joined the synthesized backing mission, extending the loop-unit span and inflating the dispatch cadence. For player missions the new-branch join is mostly the INTENDED replace semantics (playback suppresses the superseded subtree per-recording); the residual curated-exclusion gap is render-only/cosmetic and stays parked.
- **Fix (route-side, no Mission/MissionStore/codec change):** `RouteBackingMission.ComputeAutoExcludedNewIntervalKeys` derives, at the single synthesis chokepoint (`BuildMission`, gated behind a topology signature of BranchPoints/Recordings counts plus rolling ordinal id hashes, cached on two non-serialized Route fields), the keys to auto-exclude from the synthesized backing mission. Two prongs: (1) base-id rule - keys whose BASE recording id (the `/segN` marker stripped) was not known at creation (`SourceRefs` UNION the excluded keys' base ids); (2) UT end-trim - composition keys are POSITIONAL, so growth that adds a peel edge on a member/excluded through-line renumbers/mints base-KNOWN tail keys past the creation-time index range; the creation-time trim is therefore re-derived against the CURRENT tree from the persisted `RecordedDockUT`, excluding any selectable interval starting at/after the dock regardless of its key string. A pre-dock `/segN` re-peel of a known member stays included; an empty creation-time excluded set keeps the honest whole-segment fallback (no freeze); empty `SourceRefs` fails open (no freeze); the auto-excluded set Info-logs on any change (growth and shrink alike). A route without a persisted `RecordedDockUT` keeps base-id protection only (effectively empty population - the dock UT shipped in the same codec change as the excluded keys). The freeze RELIES on `RevalidateSources` for the inverse direction: pre-dock member-path renumbering (a stale creation key string coming to denote a pre-dock member window, which the union would over-exclude) is unreachable because any pre-dock member mutation changes a SourceRef fingerprint and flips the route off ghost-driving first (re-review finding 1, caveat-commented on the pure-method test). Residual: the recovery-credit whole-tree sum is NOT covered by this chokepoint - closed separately by M-MIS-9-R1 below (creation-time tree snapshot, 2026-06-12).

### ~~M-MIS-9-R1 - Route recovery credit sums the WHOLE source tree; a post-creation recovered branch inflates it~~ [DONE 2026-06-12, creation-time tree snapshot]

- **What it was (found in the 2026-06-11 M-MIS-9 review, finding 4; pre-existing):** `RouteOrchestrator.EmitPendingRecoveryCredit` sized the per-cycle KSC recovery credit via `RouteRunCostCalculator.SumRecoveredCredits` scoped to `ResolveTreeRecordingIds(route)` = EVERY recording id currently in the route's source tree. That whole-tree scope was deliberate (gotcha G1: the fly-home-and-recover leg is post-undock and outside the route member set, so member-scoping would silently return zero credit), but a branch added to the tree AFTER route creation that ends in a vessel recovery added its recovery rows to the sum and inflated the route's recurring credit (and the displayed run cost, which reads the same resolver). The M-MIS-9 freeze could not cover this - it operates at the backing-mission synthesis chokepoint and never touches the ledger-sum contract.
- **Fix (shape (a) of the two candidates; plan: `docs/dev/plan-mmis9-r1-recovery-credit-scope.md`):** new persisted `Route.CreationTreeRecordingIds` snapshot (every recording id in the source tree at creation, captured by `RouteBuilder.BuildRoute`; sparse `CREATION_TREE_RECORDINGS` node in `RouteCodec`; the defensive null-tree path leaves the snapshot empty / fail-open - a member-id fallback would exclude the recover leg, the G1 regression). `ResolveTreeRecordingIds(Route)` intersects the CURRENT tree's ids with the snapshot, so post-creation branches (re-fly forks, switch-fly continuations, and post-creation forks of creation-time descendants - all of which mint NEW recording ids) drop out of both the emitted credit and the run-cost display, while the post-undock recover leg stays in scope (it was in the tree at creation, so G1 holds). An empty snapshot FAILS OPEN to the whole current tree (degenerate / pre-field route; preserves G1's never-silently-zero contract, logged). Shape (b) cycle attribution was rejected: route cycles do not produce recovery `FundsEarning` rows (the recorded flight authored them once), so there is nothing to tag without inventing a new ledger row semantic the rewind cutoff walk and the re-fly tombstone path would both have to learn. Revert safety unchanged: the amount is still recomputed fresh from ELS at every flush (no cached amounts, T-CRASH-WINDOW-TOMBSTONE intact), row semantics are untouched, and the failure direction is conservative (a post-creation re-fly of the recover leg tombstones the old rows and mints excluded ids, so the credit drops to zero rather than ever over-crediting). Tests: `RouteRunCostCalculatorTests` (snapshot filter, fail-open, stale-id intersection), `RouteRecoveryCreditTests.PostCreationRecoveredBranch_DoesNotInflateCredit` (T-POSTCREATION-BRANCH), `RouteBuilderTests` (whole-tree capture incl. the post-undock leg; null-tree fail-open), `RouteCodecTests` (round-trip + sparse omission).

### M-MIS-10 - Scenario verification sweep: believed-supported archetypes, never explicitly verified [not sequenced - run incrementally alongside any milestone]

A 2026-06-10 online sweep of what KSP players actually fly (stock career contract types: satellite/relay, rescue, tourism, asteroid redirect, station resupply / crew rotation; the classic community challenges: Jool 5, Elcano, K-Prize, grand tours, Eve return; and the automation prior art Parsek overlaps with: Routine Mission Manager, KSTS, FMRS, MKS supply chains) found NO missing alignment subsystem beyond M-MIS-1..9 - but it surfaced a set of archetypes the recorder/missions stack should support TODAY that have no explicit test or playtest. Each needs a cheap in-game verify (file a todo entry where it breaks):

- **Constellation deployment** (resonant-orbit carrier releasing N relay sats, the CommNet career staple): an N-fork controlled-decouple tree where every branch ends in a perpetual-orbit terminal. Verify the fork-tree records, the Missions window renders N branches, selection/trim behaves, and N real satellites materialize at recording end.
- **Reusable booster flyback** (FMRS-class profile - the recorder's home turf): booster = controlled-decoupled child flown back to a landing. Verify the branch loops with the main mission and the booster's landed terminal spawns/recovers correctly.
- **Launch from a NON-Kerbin body** (Eve return ascent, Mun surface -> orbit, Laythe spaceplane): `Rotation(B)` / `launchBodyName` handling is generic by construction through the zero-drift scheduler, but every test and playtest to date launches from Kerbin. Verify phase-lock + pad anchoring for an off-Kerbin launch site (also exercises rewind-from-surface there).
- **Claw couples** (asteroid / derelict grabs): verify a claw `OnPartCouple` records as a Dock-equivalent branch point, and that a claw-coupled asteroid (PotatoRoid part) survives ghost-visual building and the snapshot part-name path.
- **Long surface expeditions** (Elcano-class rover circumnavigation, days of driving): no alignment problem (surface sections are rotation-locked and render correctly at any UT) but a recording-size / optimizer / polyline-budget STRESS case; measure before declaring supported.
- **Round-trip resupply with vehicle reuse** (the Routine Mission Manager marquee profile: outbound dock, return, recover): the Missions side (whole-tree span loop incl. the return leg) should already work; the delivery-AND-recovery-per-cycle economics are logistics-roadmap territory - verify the rendering half here, leave the ledger half to logistics M1-M6.
- **Suborbital tourist hop** (career tourism staple): atmospheric-only -> unconstrained free loop; should be the trivial case - one verify run.

### M-MIS-11 - Missions -> Logistics loop-unit API hardening [schedule alongside logistics M3-M5; nothing here blocks logistics M1/M2]

- **Investigated 2026-06-10 (PR #1113 section 19 + seam code review).** The route-on-Missions consumption WORKS and the locked-layer doctrine held: a route synthesizes a PRIVATE `Mission` via `RouteBackingMission.BuildMission` (never stored in `MissionStore`), feeds it through the unchanged `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.Build`, and reads the span clock through `RouteLoopClock` -> `GhostPlaybackLogic.TryComputeSpanLoopUT`; delivery fires once per dock-phase crossing with warp-skip handled fire-once-snap-forward, and `cycle-N` ids stamp all three ledger rows. Verified NON-needs: logistics does not need multi-loop-per-tree (one route binds one tree via `RouteTreeGuard`, so the design-doc sect. 12 "one ghost of one recording on several Mission clocks" deferral stays moot), and round-trip-in-one-recording is logistics M4's widened render window, not a Missions change. The friction an API pass should target, in value order:
  1. **First-class loop-unit build seam:** `RouteOrchestrator.ResolveLoopUnit` (RouteOrchestrator.cs:766) re-synthesizes the throwaway Mission and re-runs the FULL builder pipeline on every orchestrator tick and again per eligibility check, and `RouteBackingMission.ComputeExcludedIntervalKeys` re-walks the composition with its own trim logic (a second walker of the same tree). Provide a `BuildLoopUnitForSelection(treeId, trimWindow)` entry point + build-signature caching so consumers stop paying for (and duplicating) the Mission-pipeline shape.
  2. **Loop milestones as events, not polling:** expose span-clock cycle events (cycle started / UT-marker crossed / cycle completed) carrying the cycle index, with the warp-skip semantics (fire once, snap forward) centralized in the emitter instead of re-implemented per consumer. Serves the route dock crossing today, logistics M3's N loading-window markers per cycle tomorrow, and the Missions-window TTL display.
  3. **Cycle-index semantic typing (CORRECTED 2026-06-10 - NOT a logistics M5 blocker):** the scheduled-launch index IS already exposed - on the schedule path `TryComputeSpanLoopUT` returns it as the out `cycleIndex` (`cycleIndex = sIdx` from `MissionRelaunchSchedule.TryResolveActiveLaunch`, GhostPlaybackLogic.cs:7258-7262) and `RouteLoopClock.TryGetRouteLoopState` surfaces it, so M5's "`CadenceMultiplier` as a modulo on the scheduled-launch index" is route-side-only work. The real (minor) gap is SEMANTIC: `cycleIndex` means flat-cadence index on a null-schedule unit and scheduled-launch index on a scheduled unit, distinguished only by `unit.RelaunchSchedule != null`. The hardening item is a typed exposure (an enum/flag or distinct fields) so consumers cannot misread one as the other - a nice-to-have, not a prerequisite.
  4. **Span-clock parameter object:** `TryComputeSpanLoopUT` (GhostPlaybackLogic.cs:7198) has grown to 13 parameters (5 in + 3 out + 5 optional), reached directly by the flight engine, `RouteLoopClock`, and `ReaimPlaybackResolver`, and through the 15-parameter `DecideUnitMemberRender` wrapper (GhostPlaybackLogic.cs:7478) by the KSC / TS / map-marker surfaces; fold the unit-derived inputs into one context struct built off the `LoopUnit` so a consumer cannot mis-thread schedule / cuts / hold fields.
  5. **Member identity contract:** loop-unit members are POSITIONAL indices into the raw `RecordingStore.CommittedRecordings` (supersede/ERS-blind by design; the orchestrator carries an [ERS-exempt] comment re-stating the alignment invariant). Either formalize the invariant as a tested contract for all unit consumers, or move membership to recording-id keys with one positional resolve at the engine boundary.
  6. **Phase-anchor read-back:** the builder floors the anchor to spanEnd and overrides the route's `LoopAnchorUT`, so routes (and the TTL UI) re-derive the effective anchor; expose the EFFECTIVE anchor on the built unit.
  7. **(Stretch, gameplay) Parallel shipments / fleets:** route loops are single-instance today (cadence raised to >= span). A fleet profile (dispatch interval < route duration, several cycles in flight at once) maps onto the EXISTING per-instance overlap rendering (Integration 2) but needs per-INSTANCE marker crossings, per-instance cycle ids, and per-instance cargo escrow before logistics could adopt it. Park until a player route profile demands it.
- **Cross-note for logistics M2 (harvest provenance, PR #1113):** the harvest-attribution capture plan names `ModuleResourceHarvester` / `ModuleResourceConverter`; stock asteroid/comet mining uses the SEPARATE `ModuleAsteroidDrill` / `ModuleCometDrill` modules. Include them in the M2 capture surface or asteroid-mining routes (the asteroid variant of scenario family 4) will fail flow closure with an untracked-gain rejection. **RESOLVED by M2 (2026-06-12, branch `logistics-m2-resource-generality`):** the converter cache keys on the `BaseConverter` BASE CLASS (the `TimeJumpManager` precedent), which covers both asteroid/comet drill modules and modded derivatives with no module name list (M2 Phase 3, plan D4), and the M2 Phase 4 gain check consumes the windows end to end - an asteroid/comet drill run on an ALREADY-GRAPPLED asteroid records its harvest and analyzes Eligible. Mid-run GRAPPLE runs (the claw grab itself) are a merge boundary / second-window shape and stay M4 territory (plan finding 15).
- **Logistics M2 capture limitation (discovered building Phase 3): mid-leg quickload loses recorder-side harvest windows.** Harvest windows live on the RECORDER side until an active-stop capture forwards them (plan D3 rule 2 - deliberate, the false-alarm reopen unwind relies on it), and the OnSave mid-flight flush does not serialize them. A quickload back into a leg therefore resumes with the persisted run-manifest START half (adopted, correct) but WITHOUT windows witnessed before the quicksave: drill gains from before the quicksave become unaccounted and the Phase 4 gain check will reject the run with the named quantity (honest fail-closed per D12, not silent wrongness; remedy = re-record the leg without the mid-drill quickload). If playtests hit this often, M3 could persist open windows through the serialization flush and re-adopt them on quickload resume alongside the manifest start half.

### Logistics M2 deferred scope + manual playtest items (2026-06-12, branch `logistics-m2-resource-generality`)

Harvest provenance shipped (design doc 19.4 M2 / 19.2.2 item 3); these are the stated deferrals and the open verification work.

- **BG-leg harvest capture deferred (plan D12):** a transport leg that transits BACKGROUND (the player switches away from a loaded drilling transport) has its run cargo manifest VOIDED (Warn-logged at the transition) and its recorder-side harvest windows discarded; the lineage then lacks complete manifests and the gain check DEGRADES TO LEGACY analysis for that tree. The stated fail mode is degrade-to-legacy, NOT a named-quantity rejection. Same degrade for ForceStop / scene-change legs (the END half never completes). Workflow rule, mirroring the M1 undocked-start rule: stay with the mining vessel.
- **Drilling while docked at the origin is outside the gain check until M3:** pre-anchor gains (the depot run drilling BEFORE the undock split) sit outside the checked anchor-to-dock span (plan D6 span limit - a fail-open mask, deliberately not credited), and in-window docked harvest admission needs M3 flow accounting. Drilling while docked at the DESTINATION still rejects (`HasResourcePickup` / `MixedPickupDelivery` unchanged). Documented limitation, lifted by M3.
- **Manual playtest pending (the D4/D5 empirical risks; plan risk 4):** (1) live Minmus drill run - activate the drill, record, fly to a depot, dock, create the route; confirm in KSP.log that the load-time catch-up burst attributes inside the open-at-start window or a bridged boundary (`Harvest window opened ... atStart=1`, analysis Eligible, no `UntrackedCargoGain`). (2) The warp case - activate drill, rails-warp while drilling, exit warp, dock; confirm the rails-entry breadcrumb (`Harvest window stays open across rails entry`) and that a warp-period toggle closes with `trigger=rails-exit`. In-game twins exist (`InGameTests/LogisticsHarvestRuntimeTests.cs`, Logistics category, isolated-run), but the design-doc D5 claim should be confirmed once on a real drill save.

### Logistics M4 Phase A1 - analysis: accept + order N windows, widen the result, run-level closure (done, branch `logistics-m4-multistop`)

Plan `docs/dev/plan-logistics-m4-shape-generality.md` Phase A1 (D1/D2/D3, analysis layer ONLY). The route-shape N-stop build (A2), per-window firing (A3), no-spawn / end-trim / mid-recording-start rejection (A4), and in-game validation (A5) are later phases; multi-stop does NOT work end-to-end yet (RouteBuilder still consumes the scalar fields and builds a single-stop route this phase), so there is NO user-facing CHANGELOG line and the design-doc 19.4 M4 bullet is NOT yet flipped to SHIPPED.

- **Accept + order N windows at BOTH entry points (D1).** `RouteAnalysisEngine.AnalyzeTree` and `AnalyzeRecording` no longer return `MultipleConnectionWindows` on the second completed window. Each collects EVERY `IsComplete` window across the source-path recordings into a `WindowOnRecording` list, then `TryOrderWindows` sorts ascending by `RouteConnectionWindow.DockUT` (mandatory because `AnalyzeTree` iterates an unordered `HashSet`). `MultipleConnectionWindows` (value 2, enum unchanged) is RE-PURPOSED to fire ONLY on genuinely-unorderable windows - a NaN/Inf DockUT (no sort key) or two windows sharing an identical DockUT (two transfers at the same recorded time). The formatter text changed from "multi-stop routes are not yet supported in v1" to "Two transfers happened at the same recorded time and cannot be ordered." Both `RouteCandidateFinder` ineligible counters renamed `multiWindow` -> `unorderableWindows` (the batch-summary token follows). The accept+order summary logs the count + the sorted DockUT order; the unorderable reject logs the duplicate/NaN DockUT.
- **Per-stop collection on `RouteAnalysisResult` (D2).** New `RouteAnalysisStop` (per-window ConnectionWindow + the four manifests + the resolved `EndpointAtDock` + `DockUT` + `SourceRecording`) and `List<RouteAnalysisStop> Stops`, ordered ascending by DockUT. The existing singular scalar fields (`ConnectionWindow`, `ResourceDeliveryManifest`, etc.) are KEPT and populated from the FIRST/anchor stop, so every existing consumer (`RouteBuilder`, `RouteCreationFormatters`, `RouteCandidateFinder`, `UI/LogisticsWindowUI`) keeps compiling against the scalars and a single-window run is byte-identical (one stop mirroring the scalars). `AnalyzeWindow` was restructured into `AnalyzeWindows`: per-window gates (endpoint-proof, manifest build, unwitnessed-inventory-gain, no-delivery-AND-no-load) run per window in DockUT order; the run-level gates (harvest gain check, undocked-start workflow gate, untracked-gain verdict, flow closure, refined undocked-start) run once. Run-level singletons (`HarvestedManifest` / `IsHarvestOrigin` / `FirstHarvestWindow`) stay run-level. NOTE: A1 widens the result only - consuming `Stops` to build N RouteStops is A2; a multi-window run still builds a single-stop route this phase (acceptable on the dev branch).
- **Run-level flow closure (D3).** The harvest gain check and `ComputeFlowClosure` are now fed ALL N windows. `ComputeFlowClosure` (unchanged - it already sums over a window LIST) receives the full per-window loaded + delivered lists; `residual` = the LAST (max-DockUT) window's `UndockTransportResources` (NOT a sum, which would double-count cargo still aboard), `launched` = the anchor leg's `StartTransportResources`. The harvest "covered" term in the gain check (`RouteHarvestAnalysis.CheckTransportGains`) now sums ALL N windows' loaded terms via the new `SumManifestList` (today it folded one), so a legit multi-pickup run whose accumulated dock cargo exceeds any single window's load does not false-reject `UntrackedCargoGain`. The harvest check + closure anchor on the LAST (max-DockUT) window (its dock holds the maximally-accumulated cargo, its source resolves the deepest lineage); the scalar result fields mirror the FIRST window. For a single window first == last, so the analysis is byte-identical. Reject `FlowDoesNotClose` (value 8) only on pre-clamp slack `< -GainEpsilon` (unchanged).
- **Tests (in `RouteAnalysisEngineTests.cs`):** `AnalyzeRecording_TwoDeliveryWindows_AcceptsAndOrdersByDockUT` (D1: a distinct-DockUT multi-window run accepts + orders the stops ascending, scalars mirror the anchor), `AnalyzeRecording_ReversedDockUTInput_StillOrdersAscending` (D1: the sort is not input-order-dependent), `AnalyzeTree_TwoDeliveryWindows_OverDeliveryAcrossWindows_RejectsFlowDoesNotClose` (D3: over-delivery SUMMED across two windows rejects naming the 50-Ore quantity - a single-window fold would close and slip through), `AnalyzeRecording_DuplicateDockUT_RejectsMultipleConnectionWindows` (D1: two windows at the same DockUT are unorderable and still reject; re-purposed from the old V0-multi-stop test), `AnalyzeTree_MultiPickup_CompleteManifest_NoFalseUntrackedCargoGain` (D3: a three-pickup run on a complete run manifest, accumulated dock gain 100 covered only by the summed 150 load, does NOT false-reject UntrackedCargoGain), `AnalyzeRecording_SingleWindow_ByteIdenticalScalarsPlusOneStop` (D2 no-regression: a single-window run's scalar fields are unchanged and Stops carries exactly one entry mirroring them).
- **Pending (later phases):** RouteBuilder N-stop build + per-stop `SegmentIndexBefore`/`DeliveryOffsetSeconds` + single-stop byte-identity (A2); per-window firing - windowed replay key, `Sequence` uniquification, per-stop fire state (A3); no-spawn pin + last-dock end-trim + `MidRecordingStartTrimUnsupported = 9` rejection (A4); in-game `LogisticsMultiStopRuntimeTests` + synthetic multi-stop recording (A5).

### Logistics M4 Phase A2 - route shape: build N stops, per-stop timing, byte-identity (done, branch `logistics-m4-multistop`)

Plan `docs/dev/plan-logistics-m4-shape-generality.md` Phase A2 (D4, route-shape build + codec ONLY). Per-window firing (A3), no-spawn / end-trim / mid-recording-start rejection (A4), and in-game validation (A5) are later phases; a multi-stop route now BUILDS N stops but the orchestrator still fires only stop 0 (`ResolveCycleStop` defaults `PendingStopIndex` to 0 - that is A3), so multi-stop does NOT fire end-to-end yet. There is NO user-facing CHANGELOG line and the design-doc 19.4 M4 bullet is NOT yet flipped to SHIPPED.

- **Per-stop fire-state fields on `RouteStop` (OQ3 shape; serialized here, firing is A3).** `RouteStop` gains `double RecordedDockUT = -1.0` (the per-stop dock-phase UT, the per-window analogue of route-level `Route.RecordedDockUT`, read at fire time in A3) and `long LastFiredCycleIndex = -1` (the per-window firing sub-gate, left at default this phase - A3 wires it). `RouteCodec.SerializeStop`/`DeserializeStop` write BOTH sparsely on the `STOP` node (omitted when `== -1.0` / `-1`, empty->default on load), mirroring the route-level `lastObservedLoopCycleIndex` sparse convention (NOT the non-sparse `segmentIndexBefore`/`deliveryOffsetSeconds` pattern). A single-stop / pre-M4 route leaves both at default, so the codec writes NEITHER key and the STOP node is byte-identical to pre-A2.
- **RouteBuilder builds N ordered stops (D4).** RouteBuilder now loops `analysis.Stops` (ordered ascending by DockUT in A1) instead of reading the scalar fields, building one `RouteStop` per analysis stop: `Endpoint` / `ConnectionKind` / delivery + pickup manifests (resource + inventory, defensive copies as before) from the per-stop analysis, plus `RecordedDockUT = stop.DockUT`. `ResolveAnalysisStops` synthesizes a single stop from the scalar `ConnectionWindow` + manifests when `analysis.Stops` is null/empty (the shape the pure-logic RouteBuilder tests construct), so a single-window analysis builds the same single-stop route as pre-A2. The route span (`RecordedDockUT` / `TransitDuration` / `DockMemberRecordingId`) keys on the LAST (max-DockUT) stop; for a single-stop route this is the same window as pre-A2 (byte-identical). **A2 review fold:** the initial A2 commit keyed `DockMemberRecordingId` on the ANCHOR (first) stop's source while `RecordedDockUT` keyed on the last stop, producing an incoherent `(last-UT, first-recording)` pair on a CROSS-recording multi-stop route (which A4's end-trim + `MissionRouteStructureList` resolve through `DockMemberRecordingId`); fixed to `(lastAnalysisStop.SourceRecording ?? source).RecordingId` so the pair references the same run-end leaf (byte-identical for single-stop, where anchor == last). Pinned by `BuildRoute_CrossRecordingMultiStop_DockMemberRecordingIdCoherentWithLastStop` + a length-1-`Stops` equivalence test + a Verbose trace on the `ResolveAnalysisStops` scalar-fallback collapse.
- **`SegmentIndexBefore` derivation (D4).** For N>1, `SegmentIndexBefore` = `ResolveSegmentIndexBefore` (best-effort index of the stop's `SourceRecording` id in `route.RecordingIds`; -1 when not resolvable). A single-stop route keeps the byte-identical placeholder `0`.
- **Byte-identity gate (D4 / RANK-8, critical).** `DeliveryOffsetSeconds` is consumed ONLY by the codec - it is NOT read at fire time (`ResolveCycleStop` / `PendingDeliveryUT` do not read it; the loop fires on the recorded dock PHASE via the loop clock), so its derivation is GATED to `analysis.Stops.Count > 1`. A SINGLE-stop route keeps `DeliveryOffsetSeconds = 0.0` AND `SegmentIndexBefore = 0` exactly as the pre-A2 build set them, AND leaves the new `RecordedDockUT`/`LastFiredCycleIndex` at default (sparse-omitted), so its serialized bytes are identical. For N>1, `DeliveryOffsetSeconds = stop.DockUT - rootLaunchUT` (the scheduler/display projection per design 6.2; the actual per-window firing keys on each window's DockUT through the loop clock, A3). No `RouteConnectionWindow` field and no `RouteProofHasher` change, so the recording proof hash is trivially unaffected (`Hash_PreM4Recording_ByteStable` untouched).
- **Logging.** RouteBuilder logs a one-line `Built multi-stop route` summary (stop count + per-stop dock UT / segment index / offset / endpoint pid+body / deliver+pickup counts) ONLY for a multi-stop route; the headline `Built route` line carries a new `stops=N` token and keeps the anchor (first) stop's `stop-*` counts. A single-stop route logs no summary line, so the common-case log is unchanged.
- **Tests (in `RouteBuilderTests.cs` + `RouteCodecTests.cs`):** `BuildRoute_TwoStopAnalysis_BuildsTwoStopsInDockUtOrder` (D4: 2 stops in DockUT order, each with its own endpoint + delivery manifest + RecordedDockUT), `BuildRoute_TwoStopAnalysis_DeliveryOffsetsSetForMultiStop_AscendingByDock` (D4: offsets set for N>1, stop0 < stop1, both positive, + the multi-stop summary log), `BuildRoute_TwoStopAnalysis_RouteSpanUsesLastStopDock` (D4: route span keys on the last stop's dock), `BuildRoute_SingleStopScalarOnlyAnalysis_StillBuildsOneStop` (D4/RANK-8: the scalar-only fallback builds one stop at the single-stop sentinels, no summary line); `RoundTrip_TwoStops_PerStopRecordedDockUtPreserved` (N stops + per-stop fire state round-trip incl. a non-default `LastFiredCycleIndex`), `RoundTrip_SingleStop_PerStopFireStateSparseOmitted` (the new per-stop keys are sparse-omitted on a single-stop STOP node), `Serialize_SingleStop_ByteIdenticalToBaseline` (RANK-8: the full serialized single-stop route ConfigNode string is byte-identical to a known-good baseline; STOP node carries `segmentIndexBefore`+`deliveryOffsetSeconds=0` and NO new per-stop keys). Full xUnit suite green (15874).
- **Pending (later phases):** per-window firing - re-key BOTH replay guards to `(RouteId, cycleId, stopIndex)`, `Sequence` uniquification, per-stop fire state reads, drive `PendingStopIndex` per crossing, `CompletedCycles` once-per-cycle (A3); no-spawn pin + last-dock end-trim + `MidRecordingStartTrimUnsupported = 9` rejection (A4); in-game `LogisticsMultiStopRuntimeTests` + synthetic multi-stop recording (A5).

### Logistics M4 Phase A3 - per-window firing: replay key, Sequence, per-stop fire state (done, branch `logistics-m4-multistop`)

Plan `docs/dev/plan-logistics-m4-shape-generality.md` Phase A3 (D5, OQ2 Horn A + OQ3 + OQ4, the BLOCKER phase: the firing/idempotency restructure). A multi-stop DELIVERY route now fires N delivery windows end-to-end, each at its OWN recorded dock phase under ONE cycleId, idempotent across save/reload, with `CompletedCycles` bumping exactly once per completed cycle. No-spawn pin + last-dock end-trim + the mid-recording-start rejection (A4) and in-game validation (A5) are later phases, so there is NO user-facing CHANGELOG line yet and the design-doc 19.4 M4 bullet is NOT yet flipped.

- **ProcessLoopRoute drives N per-window crossings (Horn A restructure).** `ProcessLoopRoute` branches on `route.Stops.Count`: a single-stop route keeps the byte-identical scalar path (`EmitLoopCycle` - the single-window full-cycle emitter, untouched), and a multi-stop route routes to the new `ProcessMultiStopCrossings`. The multi-stop helper resolves, in DockUT order, which windows are DUE this tick (per-stop `IsDockCrossing(unit, loopUT, cycleIndex, stop.RecordedDockUT, stop.LastFiredCycleIndex)`), fires the dispatch half ONCE per cycle (cycle open), fires each due window's pickup (+ delivery) via `EmitMultiStopWindow`, and snaps each fired stop's `LastFiredCycleIndex` forward. The dispatch + every window of one cycle run under ONE `cycleId = cycle-{Completed+Skipped}` (stable because neither Completed nor Skipped moves until the cycle completes / is skipped).
- **BLOCKER-1 fix - one dock-cycle per pass + catch-up loop (cross-cycle gap-tick desync).** An adversarial review reproduced a warp-reachable economic-correctness bug through the REAL Tick path: when a tick lands in the `(dockA, dockB)` gap of cycle K+1 while cycle K's later window is still owed, the per-stop due pass derives a DIFFERENT `sDockCycle` per stop (the earlier dock -> cycleIndex, the later dock -> cycleIndex-1) but the FIRST draft fired BOTH under the SAME frozen `cycleId = cycle-{Completed+Skipped}`; the deferred bump never fired (loopUT in the gap), so the cycleId never advanced. A later tick then found the gap-tick's row under the frozen cycleId and SILENTLY DROPPED a whole cycle's dispatch (KSC funds charge) + at least one delivery, and `CompletedCycles` under-counted. The fix processes EXACTLY ONE dock-cycle per `ProcessMultiStopCrossings` pass - the LOWEST owed cycle `cMin` - firing only the windows whose `sDockCycle == cMin`, the dispatch half ONCE for `cMin`, and bumping Completed (or Skipped on a block) exactly once when `cMin`'s last dock is reached. `ProcessLoopRoute` wraps the helper in a bounded catch-up loop (`MaxCatchUpCyclesPerTick`) that re-invokes while the route reports `stillDue=true` (a LATER owed cycle remains after `cMin` completed this pass). The SAFETY PROPERTY is that `cycleId` is unique per FIRED cycle: `Completed+Skipped` is strictly monotonic (bumped once per cycle as each completes / is skipped) and a partially-fired cycle resumes under its EXISTING count-id, so the per-window `(RouteId, cycleId, stopIndex)` replay-guard keys never collide across cycles. (The stronger equality `Completed+Skipped == cMin` holds only for same-tick NON-warp ascending catch-up passes; across a warp that SKIPS span cycles, `cMin` - a loop-cycle index - runs ahead of the fired-cycle COUNT. The fix does not rely on the equality, only on per-fired-cycle id uniqueness + correct partial-bucket resume, both of which hold under warp - A3-fix re-review wording correction.) A tick that lands in `cMin`'s OWN (dockA, dockB) gap (no later owed cycle) leaves `cMin` open with `stillDue=false`; its remaining windows fire on a future TICK (the deferred-snap resume, unchanged). Warp-once semantics are preserved (a tick that warps past a cycle without an intervening gap tick fires that cycle once and snaps forward; missed earlier cycles are not replayed).
- **CompletedCycles bumps ONCE per cycle, after the last window (OQ4).** The per-window `CompletedCycles += 1` was moved OUT of `ApplyDeliveryFromPlan` (STEP 9, now gated on a new `ApplyDeliveryContext.BumpCompletedCycle`) and the `ApplyDelivery` replay branch (same gate). For the SINGLE-stop loop + the legacy self-timer path the 3-arg `ApplyDelivery` forwards `bumpCompletedCycle: true` (byte-identical to pre-A3: one bump per cycle, the P2-1 replay-bump preserved). For a MULTI-stop cycle every window passes `false`; `ProcessMultiStopCrossings` owns the single bump, fired when `loopUT >= max(stop.RecordedDockUT)` (the cycle's last dock). So the cycleId the LATER windows recompute inside `ApplyDelivery` stays in sync with the tick-start computation. `EmitLoopCycle`'s replay-branch + pure-pickup bumps are unchanged (single-stop = one-window cycle = cycle complete).
- **BOTH replay guards re-keyed to `(RouteId, cycleId, stopIndex)`.** `IsDeliveryAlreadyInLedger` and `IsDispatchAlreadyInLedger` both gained a `stopIndex` parameter that matches the row's already-serialized `RouteStopIndex`. The DELIVERY guard keys per-window so window 0's `RouteCargoDelivered` row does NOT suppress windows 1..N (the RANK-1 hole). The DISPATCH half fires once per cycle and its rows carry a CYCLE-STABLE carrier stop index (stop 0, the first stop in DockUT order) - stable across the whole cycle so a partial-cycle resume (window 0 fired + saved; the resume tick has only window 1 due) does NOT re-dispatch under a drifting stop index. The single-stop / legacy dispatch rows keep the v0 sentinel `-1` (`EmitDispatchDebit` gained a `dispatchStopIndex = -1` default), so `EmitLoopCycle` checks the guard against `-1` and the rows are byte-identical.
- **Per-stop fire state + deferred route-level snap (OQ3).** The A2-added `RouteStop.LastFiredCycleIndex` is now the per-window sub-gate; the route-level `LastObservedLoopCycleIndex` snap is DEFERRED until the cycle's last dock is reached, so a tick landing between dock A and dock B fires only window A and leaves the route marker un-snapped (window B fires on a later tick). On a BLOCKED multi-stop cycle EVERY stop not yet fired through `cMin` (unconditional `< cMin` snap) + the route marker snap forward so the whole blocked cycle is skipped ATOMICALLY and does not re-fire; `SkippedCycles` bumps once. (A3-fix re-review: the first cut narrowed this snap to only the windows dock-crossed THIS tick, which left dock B un-snapped when the block tick landed in the cycle's own (dockA, dockB) gap; if the block then cleared before the ghost reached dock B, dock B fired next tick as a SEPARATELY-dispatched delivery under a fresh cycleId - splitting one logically-skipped cycle into "dock A skipped" + "dock B dispatched + delivered", an unaffordable cycle the player never supported. Reverted to the unconditional snap; pinned by `InGapBlockedThenUnblocked_WholeCycleSkipped_NoSplitDispatch`.) The new `RouteOrchestrator.ResetStopFireState(route)` resets EVERY stop's `LastFiredCycleIndex` to `-1` at the two reset sites alongside the route-level cursor: `RouteOrchestrator.TryActivate` (Paused->Active) and `RouteCadence.ApplyMultiplier` (cadence rebase, C1) - else a multi-stop route's later windows would stall (N raised) or jump (N lowered) after a rebase. The third site, `RouteBuilder`, already builds every stop at the `-1` default. OnSave/OnLoad round-trip for both per-stop fields was wired in A2 (sparse codec).
- **Sequence uniquified per window (RANK-3); single-stop is BEHAVIOUR-identical (C-1).** New `SeqStride = 8` constant; each window's rows are `stopIndex * SEQ_STRIDE + intraSeq` (dispatch +0, debit +1, pickup +2, delivery +3), so `(UT, Sequence)` is a TOTAL order across windows (replay-stability + the ledger dedup equality). A single-stop route fires only stop 0, so its dispatch/debit/pickup sequences stay 0/1/2 - byte-identical - but the single-stop `RouteCargoDelivered.Sequence` changes 0 -> 3 (the stride-0 delivery offset). This is BEHAVIOUR-identical, not byte-identical (C-1 wording correction): verified recalc-walk-order-equivalent because route rows are non-earning, `FundsModule` ignores `RouteCargoDelivered` entirely, the ledger walkers do NOT assume a contiguous 0..N (`RecalculationEngine.SortActions` = OrderBy UT, ThenBy IsEarning, ThenBy Sequence; the dedup equality keys on ActionId / type-specific fields, NOT Sequence), and the dispatch-before-delivery guard still holds (dispatch seq 0/1 < delivery seq 3). The `RouteModule.ProcessCargoDelivered` `DispatchedCycles==0` out-of-order guard is satisfied by primary UT order (A1 guarantees accepted multi-window runs have DISTINCT DockUTs).
- **PendingStopIndex driven per crossing (C5).** `ProcessMultiStopCrossings` sets `route.PendingStopIndex` to each firing window's index before `EmitMultiStopWindow`, so `ResolveCycleStop` + `RouteHasDeliveryManifest` / `RouteHasPickupManifest` resolve THAT window's stop (the helpers need no rewrite), then clears it to `-1` after the tick so a later non-loop read never sees a stale value.
- **C-2 pickup replay backstop (defense-in-depth).** `EmitPickupHalf` PHYSICALLY debits the source but previously had NO ledger-level idempotency guard of its own (it relied on the per-stop `LastFiredCycleIndex` cursor + the dispatch-keyed backstop). The BLOCKER-1 class of cursor/ledger desync showed a cursor-only guard can be out-flanked, so the new `IsPickupAlreadyInLedger(routeId, cycleId, stopIndex)` (structural mirror of `IsDeliveryAlreadyInLedger`, keyed on the `RouteCargoPickedUp` row) is checked at the top of `EmitPickupHalf`: if THIS window's pickup row is already in the ELS, emit NOTHING (no second physical debit, no second row). Single-stop / legacy never double-fires (the dispatch backstop), so it never trips for them - byte-identical there.
- **C-4 / C-5 doc-comment fixes.** Corrected a stale `EmitMultiStopCycle` reference in the `EmitLoopCycle` dispatch-guard comment (the actual path is `ProcessMultiStopCrossings` / `EmitMultiStopWindow`) and removed a duplicated/garbled XML-doc line in the `TryComputeSecondsToNextDockCrossing` H1 accessor.
- **Tests (in `RouteMultiStopFireTests.cs`, NEW):** the plain `DeliveryApplierForTesting` fake short-circuits BEFORE the per-window guard (false-green risk the plan flags), so these tests instead leave it null and use the new `RouteOrchestrator.DeliveryRowEmitterForTesting` seam that the REAL `ApplyDelivery` consults AFTER its STEP-1 `IsDeliveryAlreadyInLedger` guard but before the live-Vessel resolution (xUnit cannot build a Vessel) - so the dispatch-debit half + both replay guards run for real and a window-2-suppressed regression goes RED. Tests hitting the REAL Tick/ApplyDelivery path: `Blocker1_GapTickWithPriorOwedWindow_NoDroppedCycleOrDelivery` (THE BLOCKER-1 regression - the 3-tick gap sequence; verified RED on pre-fix code: dispatched.Count Actual 1 vs Expected 2), `Blocker1_SingleGapTickTwoOwedCycles_CatchUpProcessesBoth` (catch-up loop processes cMin=0 then cMin=1 in ONE tick under unique cycleIds; verified RED pre-fix: cycle-0 dock B delivery empty), `TwoWindowCycle_BothDeliveriesFire_Window2NotSuppressed` (RANK-1 hole), `PartialCycleResume_Window0Skips_Window1Fires` (OQ3 idempotent resume), `TwoWindowCycle_UtSequence_IsTotalOrder` (RANK-3), `CompletedCycles_BumpsOncePerCycle_NotPerWindow` (two full cycles -> 2 not 4), `WarpPastCyclesAndWindows_FiresEachDueWindowOnce_BumpsOnce`, `BlockedMultiStopCycle_EmitsNothing_SnapsAllStops`, `PreDockA_Tick_FiresNothing`, `PickupBackstop_NoDoubleDebitAcrossReload` (C-2: re-presented pickup window does NOT re-debit the source). Direct-guard tests: `DeliveryGuard_IsPerWindow_NotPerCycle`, `PickupBackstop_IsPerWindow_NotPerCycle` (C-2). Cadence/activate resets: `CadenceRebase_ResetsPerStopFireIndices` + `Activate_ResetsPerStopFireIndices` (C1). C-3 direct-core stride test in `RouteOrchestratorDeliveryTests.cs`: `ApplyDeliveryFromPlan_StopIndex1_EmitsStopIndex1AndSequence11` (runs the REAL production stride, not the test-mirror seam). All existing single-stop loop-fire + delivery + pickup + codec tests pass unchanged. Full xUnit suite green.
- **Pending (later phases):** no-spawn pin + last-dock end-trim + `MidRecordingStartTrimUnsupported = 9` rejection (A4); in-game `LogisticsMultiStopRuntimeTests` + synthetic multi-stop recording + design-doc 19.4 M4 bullet flip (A5). A multi-window run with >1 source-debiting (pickup) window stays M4b territory; A3 scope is N DELIVERY windows.

### Logistics M4 Phase A4 - no-spawn pin + last-dock end-trim + mid-recording-start rejection (done, branch `logistics-m4-multistop`)

Plan `docs/dev/plan-logistics-m4-shape-generality.md` Phase A4 (D7/D8/D9). In-game `LogisticsMultiStopRuntimeTests` + the synthetic multi-stop recording + the design-doc 19.4 M4 bullet flip are A5, so there is NO user-facing CHANGELOG line yet and the 19.4 M4 bullet is NOT yet flipped to SHIPPED. The Missions locked layer was consumed READ-ONLY (no Missions file touched; the Missions git diff is EMPTY).

- **D7 - last-dock end-trim (VERIFY-ONLY, no route-side code change).** A2 set `Route.RecordedDockUT` = the LAST (max-DockUT) stop and `RouteBuilder` (line ~161) already derives the local `recordedDockUT` from `lastAnalysisStop.ConnectionWindow.DockUT` (the stops are ordered ascending by DockUT in A1), then passes THAT (line ~311) to `ComputeExcludedIntervalKeys`. So the walk already receives `max(stop.DockUT)`; the single-UT `StartUT >= segmentEndUT - epsilon` exclusion correctly drops everything at/after the last dock, and `CollectTerminalUndockChildLegIds` already scopes the undock-child trim to the undock branch point CLOSEST to `segmentEndUT` (the terminal undock), so an intermediate-stop undock does NOT trim the continuing survivor. The M-MIS-9 freeze prong-2 (`ComputeAutoExcludedNewIntervalKeys`) re-derives against the persisted `route.RecordedDockUT` (= the last dock) and its result is cached on the route behind the topology-signature gate (`BuildMission` does not recompute per frame). NONE of these assume a single dock in a way that breaks N stops, so D7 required NO code change - it is a VERIFY + regression test. NOTE (Missions-composition reality, pinned by the test): composition folds a vessel's whole dock/undock/dock path into ONE through-line and splits it ONLY at undocks (peels), so an N-stop DELIVERY route's rendered window end-trims at the TERMINAL structural boundary (the last dock's undock / the last stop's `RouteConnectionWindow.DockUT`, which production aligns with that boundary, exactly as the single-stop fixtures pass `UndockUT` as `segmentEndUT`); the intermediate-undock survivor leg (the transport that undocked from depot A and flew to depot B, StartUT < the boundary) and the depot-B docked-combined leg both fold into the kept through-line and STAY rendered.
- **D8 - no-spawn regression pin (the main deliverable; pure, no new production code).** The no-spawn guarantee is ARCHITECTURAL: the engine intercepts any loop-unit member at `GhostPlaybackEngine.cs:1141` (`currentLoopUnits.TryGetUnitForMember(i, out unit)` -> `UpdateUnitMemberPlayback`, which never emits `needsSpawn`) BEFORE the past-end / `ShouldSpawnAtRecordingEnd` path, and route-excluded recordings never become unit members. Multi-stop WIDENS the rendered window past the FIRST dock (to the last dock), so the pin guards that the widening neither started spawning the kept members NOR started rendering the post-last-dock tail. `NoSpawnPin_MultiStopLoopUnit_KeptMembersLoop_PostLastDockNonMembers` (`RouteBackingMissionLoopUnitTests.cs`) drives the production `ComputeExcludedIntervalKeys` -> `BuildMission` -> the UNCHANGED `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.Build` and asserts at the `LoopUnitSet.IsMember` seam: (a) every kept member (launch through-line up to the last dock, INCLUDING the intermediate-undock survivor + the depot-B docked combined leg) `IsMember == true` (loops, never reaches the spawn path); (b) every recording at/after the last dock (the post-last-dock tail continuation + the terminal peel) `IsMember == false` (excluded entirely -> never a unit member -> never spawns); the unit span end-trims at the last dock. `Compute_MultiStop_ExcludesAtAndAfterLastDock_KeepsIntermediateSurvivor` pins the same shape at the pure `ComputeExcludedIntervalKeys` + `MissionIntervalSelection.ComputeRenderWindows` layer (excluded set covers the post-terminal tail interval + the peel; the intermediate survivor's `launch/seg1` interval is KEPT). Both use a verified multi-stop tree topology (launch -> dock A -> intermediate undock from depot A peeling payloadA, continue -> dock B -> terminal undock from depot B peeling payloadB). In-game extension: `LogisticsRouteOnMissionsRuntimeTests.RouteOnMissions_MultiStop_KeptMembersLoop_PostLastDockNonMembers` runs the union through `RouteGhostDriverSelector.SelectGhostDrivingBackingMissions` + the locked builder under live KSP statics and asserts the same members / non-members / span (read-only: no route committed past teardown, no resource mutated).
- **D9 - mid-recording-start rejection (NO Missions edit; RESERVED documented-limitation reason).** Appended `RouteAnalysisStatus.MidRecordingStartTrimUnsupported = 9` (after `FlowDoesNotClose = 8`, append-only, parses forward-compatibly) + `RouteCreationFormatters.FormatRejectMessage` text "This run starts between two docks. Routes must begin at launch or while docked to the origin; mid-flight start points are not supported yet." (ASCII, no em-dash); `LogisticsRejectPresentation.DescribeNearMiss` already delegates verbatim to `FormatRejectMessage(status, detail)` so status 9 surfaces through with no change there. **INVESTIGATION outcome: NOT cleanly detectable in M4a, so it is a RESERVED reason NOT emitted by any detector.** An undock -> undock shuttle whose run BEGINS inside a pre-dock recording (between two docks) is the locked Missions layer's gap 1: a dock MID-recording is not a selectable interval boundary (`MissionIntervalSelection` renders a contiguous `[min-start, max-end]` window per vessel), so it cannot be START-trimmed; the lift is M-MIS-5 (gated after this milestone). In M4a the analysis resolves the ORIGIN recording and such a run already rejects as `UndockedStartOrigin = 6` (it starts undocked with cargo aboard, no KSC launch / docked-origin proof), and the "begins mid-recording between two docks" shape is NOT distinguishable from the general undocked-start case WITHOUT the Missions-side dock-as-interval-boundary detection (locked). Per plan D9 a fragile detector was NOT forced; the enum value + formatter text are added now as the player-facing SURFACE, to be wired to a real detector only when M-MIS-5 lands. Tests: `LogisticsRejectPresentationTests` gained a `MidRecordingStartTrimUnsupported` InlineData on `DescribeNearMiss_Sealed_DelegatesToRejectMessage` (status 9 delegates verbatim) + `DescribeNearMiss_MidRecordingStartTrimUnsupported_PassesThrough` (asserts the "starts between two docks" / "not supported yet" text). The two `RouteCandidateFinder` ineligible-counter switches have no `default`/throw and simply do not bucket status 9 (never produced by a detector), so they are unaffected.
- **Tests + result.** 4 new pure xUnit tests (D7 + D8 in `RouteBackingMissionLoopUnitTests.cs`, 2 D9 in `LogisticsRejectPresentationTests.cs`) + 1 in-game `LogisticsRouteOnMissionsRuntimeTests` extension. Full xUnit suite green (15896, up from the A3 baseline 15892).
- ~~**Pending (later phase):** in-game `LogisticsMultiStopRuntimeTests` ... (A5 closes M4a end-to-end).~~ DONE in A5 (see the A5 section below).

### Logistics M4b Phase B1 - N-source dispatch gating derived from pickup stops (done, branch `logistics-m4-multistop`)

Plan `docs/dev/plan-logistics-m4-shape-generality.md` Phase B1 (D10, OQ5: derive the source set from the pickup `Stops`, NO new persisted `Route` field). The escrow map + lifecycle (B2), per-window source debit firing (B3), and in-game validation (B4) are later phases; multi-origin does NOT work end-to-end yet (the firing path still defers a >1 source-debiting pickup window per M4a A3), so there is NO user-facing CHANGELOG line and the design-doc 19.4 M4 multi-origin bullet is NOT yet flipped to SHIPPED.

- **INVESTIGATION (stated for the record).** (1) A multi-pickup-window route (>=2 pickup stops, each with a non-empty `PickupManifest`, resolving to two source vessels) IS buildable today: the A1 analysis accepts + orders N windows, and `RouteBuilder` (`:510-540`) builds one `RouteStop` per window carrying that window's `PickupManifest` / `InventoryPickupManifest` from `RouteAnalysisStop.ResourceLoadManifest` / `.InventoryLoadManifest`. So the SHAPE B1 gates is exercisable by a synthetic fixture. (2) The firing-defer is NOT at analysis/build - it is at FIRING: `RouteOrchestrator.EmitMultiStopWindow` (`:1185-1215`) already calls `EmitPickupHalf` per window, but the M4a A3 comment scopes a multi-window run with >1 source-debiting pickup window to M4b (a single bidirectional M3a window still fires through the path). B3 lifts that; B1 only adds the GATE. (3) The source = each pickup stop's `Endpoint`; `Route.Origin` (the docked-origin / KSC provenance) is gated INDEPENDENTLY (launched cargo vs loaded-en-route cargo are distinct units - no double-count).
- **No `IRouteRuntimeEnvironment` change; ZERO test fakes updated (RANK-10 avoided).** `OriginHasCargo(Route, out string)` already takes the full `Route` and resolves endpoints itself via `RouteEndpointResolver`, so the per-pickup-source gate fits ENTIRELY inside the production `LiveRouteRuntimeEnvironment` using statics it already touches (`RouteEndpointResolver` + `LiveOriginCargoProbe` + `LiveInventoryPickupWriter`). The interface signature is unchanged, so none of the ~14 `: IRouteRuntimeEnvironment` test fakes needed a new member. The failure flows through the existing `out string lackingResource` -> `CheckEligibility` -> `OriginLacksCargo` kind unchanged.
- **`OriginHasCargo` split into two INDEPENDENT provenance gates.** Extracted the pre-B1 body into `OriginProvenanceHasCargo` (the single docked-origin gate: KSC/harvest early-returns + `CostManifest` / `InventoryCostManifest` all-or-nothing, byte-behaviour unchanged), then ALWAYS run the new `PickupSourcesHaveCargo` after it (a KSC-origin or harvest-origin route can still load cargo from a refinery/depot). The two gate distinct units, so they do not double-count.
- **`PickupSourcesHaveCargo` + the pure `RoutePickupSourceGate` (new file `Source/Parsek/Logistics/RoutePickupSourceGate.cs`).** The live env resolves each pickup stop's endpoint to a live vessel (cached per endpoint-pid so a same-pid vessel resolves + captures the loaded-gate ONCE - never hoisted across vessels) and builds a `PickupSourceResolution` carrying the loaded-gate-baked `ProbeResourceStored` / `CountStored` readers. The pure `RoutePickupSourceGate.TryBuildSourceGroups` GROUPS the pickup stops by RESOLVED pid and SUMS the per-pid resource + inventory manifests (OQ5/OQ6 under-gate guard: a same-pid window checked independently sees the full tank); `Evaluate` runs `RouteOriginCargoCheck.HasRequired` / `HasRequiredInventory` per source in ASCENDING earliest-dock-UT order (then ordinal pid tie-break), returning the FIRST short source. A pure-delivery stop contributes no source; zero groups returns eligible (delivery-only byte-behaviour-identical).
- **B2 escrow-net seam (explicit, NOT wired in B1; WIRED in B2 - see the B2 section below).** The per-pid stored-amount reader reads LIVE stored amounts only in B1. B2 wraps the reader to subtract the sum of reservations held by EVERY OTHER route on that `(pid, resource)` from the reader's return value in PURE RAM (never via ELS, so the ERS/ELS grep gate stays green) so a competing higher-priority route in the same / a later tick (before the reserving route's physical debit) sees the reservation. NOTE the correct NET semantics: a route does NOT subtract its OWN reservation - it owns what it reserved; only OTHER routes' reservations reduce the amount this route sees (the original B1 wording "subtract the amount THIS route reserved" was imprecise and is corrected here). The grouping / summing / first-short logic is unchanged by that net; only the reader's value shifts. The seam is documented at the reader-build site + the gate class summary.
- **Hold reason names the SOURCE (M6 surface).** A short pickup source emits the `OriginLacksCargo` detail token `source:<pid>:<name>:<resource-or-inventory-token>` (name sanitized of `:` at the emit site `RoutePickupSourceGate.BuildHoldToken`); an unresolved source emits `pickup-source-unresolved:<reason>`. `LogisticsHoldPresentation.DescribeHold` gained a `DescribePickupSourceShort` branch (+ the unresolved branch) under the existing `OriginLacksCargo` case: "Depot A is out of Ore - delivers when it has the full amount" / "Cargo Bay is missing a required stored part ..." / "a pickup source vessel could not be found ...". Plain-ASCII, never blank, degrades through the generic origin text on an unexpected shape.
- **Logging.** `PickupSourcesHaveCargo` logs a per-gate summary: one `VerboseRateLimited` line per resolved source (pid + name + summed resource/inventory counts + cover/short decision; sources are bounded so per-source lines are OK), plus a single first-short-source-named FAIL line or an all-cover OK line, plus a pickup-source-unresolved line on a resolution miss.
