**Root cause (HIGH confidence; SYSTEMATIC + design-deferred, NOT inherent):** re-aim substitutes ONLY the heliocentric coast with a FRESH center-to-center Lambert (`Reaim/ReaimTransferSynthesizer.cs`: r1 = launch-body center, r2 = target-body center, recorded tof reused) and replays the recorded Kerbin-escape + Duna-capture hyperbolae VERBATIM at their original asymptotes. Two superimposed sources:
1. ENDPOINT (dominant, ~96% of the jump): Lambert endpoints are at planet CENTERS but the transfer renders FULL-SPAN (`Reaim/ReaimPlaybackResolver.cs:232-247` passes NaN render bounds). At the seam UT the synth arc is at the body center while the recorded leg ends at the SOI boundary, so each jump is ~1 SOI radius. (An earlier pass that DID trim the launch side to the SOI-exit UT was REVERTED - it opened a gap right after launch SOI exit where the orbit ghost was destroyed and the transfer line restarted displaced by the launch body's own motion. See the comment at `ReaimPlaybackResolver.cs:232-243`.)
2. ORIENTATION / SHAPE (~4% + a 2.5% sma / different ecc gap): the fresh Lambert has zero v-infinity awareness of the recorded asymptotes and reuses the recorded tof (geom tof differs by ~330,610 s here, `devFromGeom` in the `re-aimed transfer ready` line), so over a fractional 0.5835 synodic the asymptote directions and orbit shape differ from the verbatim recorded legs.

The original design (`docs/dev/done/plans/reaim-interplanetary-transfers.md:252-279, 359-361`) accepted the orientation residual as "the accepted small seam" and shipped only PadAlignLaunch; SOI-handoff continuity ("option 3: re-plan the whole patched-conic chain") was explicitly DEFERRED. The same-body 45 deg / 120 s seam-bridge (`GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer.cs` `IsBridgeAdjacentConic`) cannot cover a cross-SOI body-change seam by construction.

**Fix direction (the ONLY geometrically sound one; large effort):** the design's deferred "option 3" - synthesize the WHOLE patched-conic chain from one solve so the escape hyperbola's SOI-exit STATE matches the heliocentric departure v1 and the capture hyperbola's SOI-entry STATE matches the arrival v2, instead of splicing a fresh heliocentric arc onto verbatim recorded SOI legs. All three legs then meet at the same SOI-sphere position with continuous velocity, giving a real encounter into the SOI. Immutability-safe (in-memory loop-only on copied structs) and MIT-clean (reuses the already-solved v1/v2; no new solver). SEQUENCE AFTER the in-flight reaim branches land (`reaim-lambert-reliability`, `reaim-eccentric-tof`, `reaim-dest-loiter-retimer` / PR #1155, `fix-soi-trajectory-seam-coverage`) to avoid stacked re-aim rewrites.

**Rejected shortcuts (adversarially verified 2026-06-15, workflow wf_2ead60c5-a19; all NOT VIABLE except E as a stopgap):**
- (A) rigid-rotate the recorded transfer to the new epoch: geometrically false (escape is Kerbin-frame, capture is Duna-frame, only the middle leg is heliocentric; one Sun rotation cannot rotate all three) and misses the dominant endpoint gap.
- (B) anchored / shooting solve to SOI-boundary endpoints + recorded asymptotes: over-determined (a single-rev Lambert has only tof free once r1, r2 are fixed; one scalar cannot match two 3D asymptote directions) and reopens the reverted trim regression.
- (C) render-only rotate the recorded legs onto the solved asymptotes: corrects only the ~4% angular residual, leaves the ~1-SOI-radius endpoint gap, and needs the reverted trim.
- (D) cross-SOI render-only seam bridge: cannot move the ICON / proto-orbit (they ride the ghost transform, not the polyline), and a 62 deg cross-body connector is the wild-spiral / planet-intersection case the bridge was gated against.
- (E) accept the gap + clip the line / suppress the icon across the handoff: VIABLE only as a labeled STOPGAP - it does NOT make the line accurate (a tidy gap is still no encounter, the user's actual complaint) and re-litigates the reverted trim.

**Do NOT do (regression guards):** do not rewrite / finalize / load-time-modify recorded data (.prec / OrbitSegments) on any path - re-aim stays in-memory loop-only; do not vendor a GPL solver (Parsek is MIT); do not auto-extend the heliocentric draw / icon window over the SOI escape / capture window (tried + reverted, puts the ghost behind the planet); do not trim the full-span render without also fixing the capture leg (the reverted gap regression); revert-on-regression - prior re-aim rewrites went net-negative, the current single honest kink is a known baseline; pin the requirement against this one concrete case before writing code.

**Validation must be the ENCOUNTER, not the seam number:** re-run the looped Duna One re-aim playtest, collect a fresh log, and confirm the LINE visibly enters Duna's SOI in-game (a real encounter) and the ICON follows it through both handoffs - NOT merely that the `[ReaimSeam]` jump dropped below one SOI radius. Also confirm: re-aim still ENGAGED, the synth geometry is still a sane ellipse, and no new "gap-between-orbit-segments" / orbit-ghost-destroyed warnings appear at the launch SOI exit (the reverted-trim regression must not return).

**References:** full investigation + ranked options doc at the umbrella root `reaim-seam-investigation.md`; log snapshot `logs/2026-06-15_1906_duna-mission-investigation/`; engaged params `KSP.log:13201` (`ENGAGED re-aim Kerbin->Duna via Sun; D0=142619013 synodic=19653075 tof=6854613`).

**ATTEMPTED + REVERTED (2026-06-17) - option 3 (whole-chain synthesis). STILL OPEN; do not re-attempt without the preconditions below.** The deferred "option 3" was built behind a default-OFF flag (P0/P1 foundation #1169, P2-P4 chain synthesis #1170) and then REVERTED (#1171 reverts #1169; #1170 closed). Plan/design docs at the umbrella root: `reaim-fix-plan.md`. Why it was abandoned:
- **It regressed the flag-ON render and never solved the bug.** First playtest (Kerbal X #2): synth escape/capture legs were garbage hyperbolae (`[ReaimSeam] chain legs: escape ecc=12.9, capture ecc=7.77`; sane is ~1.05-1.3), so departure+arrival misaligned, Duna-SOI arrival render broke, icon teleported. Log `logs/2026-06-16_2351_reaim-chain-kerbalx2-regression/`.
- **Root cause (confirmed):** `ReaimTransferSynthesizer.BuildBodyRelativeLeg` paired the transfer POSITION at the SOI crossing with the Lambert ENDPOINT velocity v1/v2 (at the planet center), an inconsistent state vector. Fixed (use `transfer.getOrbitalVelocityAtUT(crossingUT)`) + added the plan's never-built periapsis/ecc fail-closed gate (`IsSaneLegConic`), so flag-ON fails closed to baseline instead of rendering garbage.
- **But it still could not be validated:** every available test mission is a fail-closed case. Duna One threads Ike (capture fails closed). Kerbal X #2 is a heliocentric-parking (two-burn) departure (escape fails closed) AND its re-aim render is independently broken by the #1166-engages-but-#1167-Increment-2-not-built span-greater-than-synodic gap, not by this work. Validating option 3 needs a CLEAN DIRECT Kerbin->Duna recording: no parking-orbit loiter, no moon (Ike) encounter. No such mission exists in the test save.
- **Structural doubt:** a center-to-center Lambert solve carries no information about the real ejection/capture periapsis, so the synth body-relative legs inherit whatever periapsis the SOI-crossing sample implies; the gate fails the bad ones closed, but a "consistent but wrong-altitude" leg can still pass. The premise may need rework (e.g. SOI-edge-to-SOI-edge solve, or seed the ejection from the recorded parking periapsis) rather than center-to-center.

**Do NOT re-attempt option 3 without (a) a clean direct no-park no-moon Kerbin->Duna looped recording to validate against, and (b) resolving the center-to-center-periapsis structural doubt.** Confirm a validatable test case exists BEFORE building (this arc was built end-to-end before that check, which was the core process mistake).

## ~~In progress 2026-06-16~~ SUPERSEDED + RETIRED 2026-06-19 by the synodic-multiple-cadence fix (see the "Fixed - looped re-aim span>synodic mission" entry at the top) - Re-aim SELF-OVERLAP scheduling milestone: heliocentric-park departure renders wrong because span > synodic (branch `reaim-self-overlap-scheduling`, stacks on #1166)

**SUPERSEDED:** Increment 1 (park LAN re-phasing on the cadence clock) and the F2 park-end-anchor work below SHIPPED and remain in effect. The DEFERRED Increment 2 / Approach A (self-overlap, cadence == synodic) was RETIRED: the every-window transfer-aim gap it existed to close is now closed by making the relaunch cadence the smallest synodic MULTIPLE >= span and stepping the departure clock by that same cadence, so the clocks coincide and the F2 override fires every window with NO overlap (single instance). The sub-PR 1-3 scaffolding (`ShouldFlipToSelfOverlapCadence` + flip block, `ReaimSelfOverlapEnabled` flag, the dead `TryResolveWindowSegmentsForWindow` overload) was deleted. The historical Increment-1 / F2 / clock-gate notes below are kept for provenance.

**Bug (found after #1166's classifier-engage, `logs/2026-06-15_2220_reaim-helio-park-render`):** s15 "Kerbal X #2" now ENGAGES re-aim (#1166) but the departure RENDERS broken: the verbatim heliocentric park draws ~239 deg off live Kerbin, and the re-aimed transfer drifts ~142 deg*k off live Kerbin for window k>=1. Root cause (confirmed in `ReaimWindowPlanner.cs` + the log): the recorded loop SPAN (~270 d = 23,285,417 s) EXCEEDS the Kerbin-Duna SYNODIC (~227 d = 19,645,697 s). Re-aim's scheduler assumes synodic >> span: `Plan` sets `cadence = max(span, synodic) = span` and the engine relaunches every SPAN, so the transfer renders at `D0 + k*span`, which is not any synodic window `D_k = D0 + k*synodic` for k>=1; `PadAlignLaunch` also skips on the `cadence != synodic` guard. Every real heliocentric-park Kerbin->Duna mission is span > synodic (the park alone is ~67% of the synodic), so #1166's engage fires every such mission into this broken render.

**Approach (design `docs/dev/plans/reaim-self-overlap-scheduling-design.md`, two clean-context adversarial reviews):** A = SELF-OVERLAP. To render the transfer at synodic windows the engine must relaunch every synodic; since span > synodic, ~2 instances overlap (inherent). Approaches B (compress the park: `effectiveCadence = max(span,...)` uses the RAW span loiter cuts never shrink) and C (decouple the resolver window clock: the ENGINE span clock governs WHEN it renders, not the resolver pick) were proven wrong. KEY: the per-instance overlap map/TS presence (`overlapInstanceVessels`) ALREADY exists and engages on `UnitMemberOverlaps`, AND overlap-cycle index == synodic-window index is a clean identity when `overlapCadence = synodic`. BLOCKER found in review: that per-instance presence has NO per-frame body-transition refresh (`EnsureOverlapInstances` only creates/destroys; `GhostOrbitIconDrivePatch` can't change `referenceBody`), so it renders SAME-BODY loops only (logistics/stations) and cannot render a body-changing interplanetary ghost (Kerbin->Sun->Duna) per cycle. Building that refresh is the bulk of Increment 2.

**Increment 1 (this branch, SHIPPED + headless-tested, in-game pending):** park LAN re-phasing on the EXISTING single-instance per-index path - does NOT set the overlap gate, so the broken per-instance path is not triggered. `ReaimPlaybackResolver.BuildWindowSegments` rotates the recorded heliocentric park's LAN by `Delta_lon(window) = omega_parent * (D_k - RecordedDepartureUT)` (`omega_parent = 360 / OrbitPeriod(launchBody)`, deg/s) via `ReaimSegmentAssembler.ReplaceHeliocentricLeg`'s new `parkDeltaLonDeg` param (else-branch park pass-through, rotates only the non-predicted common-ancestor coast ending at/before the burn). Gated on `plan.DepartedFromHeliocentricPark` + a near-equatorial guard (`ParkRephaseMaxInclinationDeg = 15`); FAILS CLOSED (declines the window to faithful, never the verbatim 239 deg park) on a non-equatorial / degenerate-omega park. Net effect: the 239 deg park teleport is removed (park connects to the escape + transfer) and the FIRST synodic window renders fully correct; later windows stay internally consistent but drift off live Kerbin by the span-vs-synodic error (the `D_k`/`DepartureUTForWindow` synodic clock used for the park angle here is SUPERSEDED for the park by the cadence-clock follow-up below: re-phasing the park on `RelaunchUTForWindow` = `D0 + k*cadence` pins the loiter to live Kerbin at every window; only the transfer-aim drift remains for Increment 2). Pure helpers `RotateLanForParkRephase` / `ComputeParkDeltaLonDegrees` / `FindHeliocentricParkInclination` / `TryComputeParkRephase`. Byte-identical when off (`parkDeltaLonDeg = 0` / direct transfer). Tests: `ReaimSegmentAssemblerTests` (+6); full headless suite green (15,702; InjectAllRecordings env-flake excluded). **In-game VALIDATED 2026-06-16 (`logs/2026-06-16_1912_reaim-park-rephase`):** the park icon initialized near live Kerbin after Kerbin SOI exit (Delta_lon sign+magnitude correct: `ReaimPlayback parkDeltaLon=2305.35deg` w0 -> `3073.79` w1 -> `3842.24` w2, +768.45deg/window = omega_Kerbin*synodic). Every window solves a valid transfer (`encounter=Duna devFromRecorded=0s`; synth `xfer-vs-Duna@arrival=0`). The maintainer's "transfer did not accurately reach Duna" is the EXPECTED span>synodic drift (Increment 2, NOT a bug): the single instance renders at span cadence (D0+k*span) while geometry targets synodic windows (D_k=D0+k*synodic), gap k*(span-synodic)~k*42d, so live Duna has moved ~20deg*k from the aim - window 0 accurate, windows 1+ drift (the maintainer warped through w0->w1->w2). Layered on even at w0: the #1165 center-to-center cross-SOI seam. CONCLUSION: Increment 1's scope (park re-phasing + window-0 correctness) is DONE + validated; the transfer touching live Duna at EVERY window needs Increment 2; a clean SOI encounter needs #1165.

**Park-placement follow-up (2026-06-17, branch `fix-reaim-teleport1-loiter`, SHIPPED + headless-tested, in-game pending):** Increment 1 re-phased the park on the SYNODIC clock (`Delta_lon = omega_parent * (D_k - RecordedDepartureUT)`, `D_k = DepartureUTForWindow = D0 + k*synodic`), which kept the park internally consistent with the transfer but, in the span>synodic case, drifted BOTH off live Kerbin by ~142 deg*k for windows k>=1. That is the maintainer's "after Kerbin SOI exit the icon appears at a distant point on the heliocentric loiter orbit instead of next to live Kerbin" report (the FIRST of the two reported teleports; the transfer-aim teleport is the second). Increment 1's in-game validation only checked window 0 (warped w0->w1->w2 but read the park as correct at w0), so the k>=1 park drift slipped through. First-principles root cause: the loop ENGINE relaunches on the CADENCE clock (`D0 + k*cadence`, `cadence = max(span,synodic) = span` here), and the body-relative escape leg follows the LIVE launch body at that relaunch time (KSP `Orbit.getPositionAtUT` adds the live `referenceBody.position`), so a launch-body-co-orbital park must re-phase to the CADENCE relaunch time, NOT the synodic departure. Fix: new `ReaimWindowPlanner.ReaimWindowSchedule.RelaunchUTForWindow(k) = D0 + k*cadence`, and `ReaimPlaybackResolver.BuildWindowSegments` feeds THAT to the park re-phase (the transfer synthesis stays on the synodic `DepartureUTForWindow`). Net: the loiter sits next to the live launch body at EVERY window, not just window 0; byte-identical when `cadence == synodic` (synodic > span) and at window 0. This DECOUPLES the park from the transfer in the span>synodic case, so a park->transfer kink remains for k>=1 - that is the SAME transfer-aim drift Increment 2 owns (the transfer touching live Duna at every window). Tests: `ReaimWindowPlannerTests` (+4, incl. the cadence-vs-synodic divergence + end-to-end park-angle assertions); full headless suite green (15,733). Does NOT need the full overlap build; corrects the Increment-1 clock choice only.

**Departure-seam fix (2026-06-17, branch `reaim-park-departure-anchor`, SHIPPED + headless-tested, in-game pending):** the prior two fixes placed the rendered PARK leg correctly (re-phased onto live Kerbin) but the synthesized TRANSFER still solved its Lambert CENTER-TO-CENTER from the launch body's center (`r1 = launchBody.orbit.getRelativePositionAtUT(departureUT)` in `ReaimTransferSynthesizer`), so for a parking departure (where the icon is coasting on the heliocentric park at the burn, not at Kerbin's center) the transfer did NOT emanate from where the icon is - it could not traverse park -> transfer -> Duna continuously. Fix (gated to the parking-departure path ONLY; direct transfers stay byte-identical): anchor the synthesized transfer's r1 (and the near-180 handedness-axis velocity) at the vessel's re-phased heliocentric PARK-END state. **LOAD-BEARING detail:** the park-end r1/vel are evaluated on the LAN-rotated park at the RECORDED burn UT (`== plan.RecordedDepartureUT`), NOT at the future synodic departure D0 - the assembler renders the park by ONLY LAN-rotating it (keeps its recorded epoch/UTs, NOT ShiftInTime'd), so the rendered park-end the icon abuts is `LANrotatedPark.getRelativePositionAtUT(RecordedDepartureUT)`; the transfer is built at absolute D0 then ShiftInTime'd into recorded-span time, so the rendered transfer-start at recorded-span RecordedDepartureUT equals r1, closing the seam exactly at WINDOW 0. Frame: `getRelativePositionAtUT/getOrbitalVelocityAtUT().xzy` everywhere (matching the existing r1/r2 swizzle contract; NEVER `getPositionAtUT`, which would add the Sun world offset and break the round-trip with `UpdateFromStateVectors`). New pure `ReaimSegmentAssembler.FindHeliocentricParkSegment` (the SINGLE source of both the inc guard - `FindHeliocentricParkInclination` now delegates - and the r1 reconstruction) + `DecideDepartureAnchor` (the pure override-vs-decline-vs-launch-center DECISION: parking + rephase-ok => ParkEndOverride at evalUT=RecordedDepartureUT; parking + rephase-declined => DeclineToFaithful, NEVER a launch-center fallback for a parking departure; direct => LaunchCenter). `TrySynthesizeTransfer` gained optional `departureOverridePos/Vel/hasDepartureOverride` params (default => byte-identical direct conic; all four fail-closed guards - sane-conic / retrograde / near-180 / proximity - unchanged). The resolver reconstructs the LAN-rotated park Orbit at the call site (Unity-bound) and feeds the override; fails closed BEFORE synthesis when a parking departure's rephase declines. Tests: `ReaimSegmentAssemblerTests` (+5: FindHeliocentricParkSegment, the delegation, the RotateLan shape-identity, the three DecideDepartureAnchor modes) + `ReaimWindowPlannerTests` (+1: window-0 D0==R0 clock-coincidence + k>=1 divergence) + in-game `ReaimEndToEndInGameTest` parking-departure fixture (window-0 r1==park-end geometry gate, compile-only here). Full headless suite green (15,740). **OUT OF SCOPE (still open):** the windows-1+ arrival clock-drift (cadence=max(span,synodic) != synodic; the transfer aims on the synodic clock while the capture renders on the cadence clock; drifts k*(cadence-synodic)) is the SEPARATE Increment 2 self-overlap work below - this fix ONLY closes the DEPARTURE seam at window 0 (k=0), where the clocks coincide.

**F2 tof + render-span + capture re-time follow-up (2026-06-17, same branch, SHIPPED + headless-tested, in-game pending):** the anchor fix above (r1 at the park-end) was necessary but not sufficient - the in-game playtest showed a WEIRD conic, because the synthesizer still searched the band centered on the RECORDED tof (~9.38 Ms = 1.438x the Hohmann time ~6.5 Ms for the s15 mission), and forcing a 1.44x-Hohmann tof FROM the re-phased park-end makes a degenerate transfer. A design pass chose formulation F2 (keep the synodic departureUT unchanged - it already aims at Duna, baseline logged `xfer-vs-Duna@arrival=0m` - and fix ONLY the tof + render-span + capture; no schedule / engine-clock change, the #1173 anchor block stays byte-identical). Three coupled changes, ALL gated on the existing parking-path flag `hasDepartureOverride` (direct transfers byte-identical: helper not called, render bounds stay NaN, capture re-time a no-op): **(i)** new pure `ReaimTofSearch.BuildParkingCandidateTofs(geomTof, eTarget)` - mirrors `BuildCandidateTofs` but STEP 0 = geomTof (the geometric Hohmann center, NOT the recorded tof) with the symmetric +-`HalfWidthFraction(eTarget)` band (same base +-6% widening law, capped); `ReaimPlaybackResolver.BuildWindowSegments` gates `hasDepartureOverride ? BuildParkingCandidateTofs(geomTof, eTarget) : BuildCandidateTofs(schedule.TofSeconds, geomTof, eTarget)`. **(ii)** render span = the TRUE transfer duration `[RecordedDepartureUT, RecordedDepartureUT + usedTof]` (no launch-side gap - the recorded escape ends at the burn UT; the arrival side trims to the new earlier arrival), passed as real render bounds instead of NaN,NaN; `ReplaceHeliocentricLeg` already clamps + falls back to full-leg on invalid bounds. **(iii)** a new `ReplaceHeliocentricLeg` overload (`captureRetimeShiftSeconds`, `targetBody`, defaults 0.0/null => byte-identical direct path) `ShiftInTime`s each non-predicted targetBody-bodied capture segment starting at/after the recorded arrival by `captureShift = newArrivalUT - RecordedArrivalUT` (NEGATIVE - the Hohmann transfer arrives EARLIER) before the sort/coalesce, so startUT/endUT/epoch move together (phase preserved) and the capture begins where the transfer ends (the seam closes). The departureUT / schedule / engine clock / parkDeltaLon / r1 anchor are UNCHANGED. Tests: `ReaimTofSearchTests` (+5: step0==geomTof, symmetric band, eccentric widens bounded, all-positive-distinct, degenerate geomTof => empty), `ReaimSegmentAssemblerTests` (+2: capture-retime shifts only the targetBody leg earlier with the seam closing + sorted, and the 0/null regression fence), in-game `ReaimEndToEndInGameTest` parking fixture (recorded tof inflated to 1.44x geomTof so the F2 work is real; asserts the resolved transfer endUT == capture startUT == RecordedDepartureUT+usedTof, the new arrival is earlier than the recorded arrival, and usedTof is within the parking band of geomTof). Full headless suite green (15,747).

**Review follow-up (2026-06-17, same branch, SHIPPED + headless-tested, in-game pending):** clean review of the F2 diff returned NO blockers; three changes landed. **FIX #1 (latent gap hardening):** the render-end trim and `captureShift` were computed independently from `newArrivalUT`, so a usedTof > recordedTof window (allowed up to the ~1.20*geomTof band cap for a near-Hohmann two-burn or a cap-binding eccentric target) would hit `ReplaceHeliocentricLeg`'s render clamp (renderEnd > recordedArrival => silent full-span fallback) while `captureShift` stayed POSITIVE and shifted the capture FORWARD, opening a real gap. Now `newArrivalUT` is CLAMPED to <= `RecordedArrivalUT` BEFORE computing BOTH `captureShift` and `renderEndUT`, so usedTof > recordedTof degrades cleanly to render-full-span + captureShift 0 (no gap, no forward shift); the s15 path (usedTof < recordedTof) is unchanged. Tests: `ReaimSegmentAssemblerTests` `ReplaceHeliocentricLeg_RenderEndPastArrival_FullSpanRender_NoGap` (+1) + an in-game NIT #4 assertion that no segment sits in the `(transferEnd, captureStart)` window. **FIX #2 (capture-phase PartEvents re-time):** INVESTIGATED - the re-aim flight path is NOT map-only: the flight engine consumes `ReaimedTrajectory.PartEvents` via `GhostPlaybackLogic.ApplyPartEvents` (zone/distance-gated, not map-only), so a watched capture-phase event (capture-burn / staging / decouple) fired at its recorded UT would desync `|captureShift|` from the now-earlier capture geometry. FIXED: new pure `ReaimSegmentAssembler.ShiftCapturePartEvents(events, recordedArrivalUT, captureShift)` re-times the in-capture events (ut >= recordedArrivalUT) by the SAME shift; the resolver caches the shift (`CacheEntry.CaptureShiftSeconds`) and `ResolveForFrame` builds the re-timed list, passed through a new `ReaimedTrajectory(inner, segments, retimedPartEvents)` overload (null => delegate, byte-identical direct path). Tests: `ReaimSegmentAssemblerTests` (+3: shifts only in-capture, zero-shift no-op, null/empty). **CONFIRM #3:** `ReaimedTrajectory.EndUT` now derives from the shifted (earlier) last-segment endUT, but the engine's loop/span clock uses the unit-supplied `SpanStartUT`/`SpanEndUT`/`CadenceSeconds` and the per-member render window uses `unit.MemberEndUT` (recorded-metadata trim, `traj.EndUT` only the untrimmed fallback) - the shifted EndUT is internally consistent with its shifted OrbitSegments (the ghost simply ends at its true earlier capture end), no terminal/last-frame handler depends on it matching the recorded arrival, so no guard needed. Full headless suite green (15,751).

**RESIDUAL (accepted):** the transfer->capture ORIENTATION seam - the capture is re-timed in UT (and its in-capture PartEvents re-timed with it per FIX #2), but the capture conic is NOT re-oriented to meet the re-aimed transfer's arrival vector - is an accepted residual; windows k>=1 and any schedule change remain the separate Increment 2 work below.

**Clock-coincidence gate on the F2 park-end bundle (2026-06-17, same branch, SHIPPED + headless-tested, in-game pending):** the F2 fix is correct at window 0 but a playtest at window 21 of a span>synodic mission rendered a WILD conic (ecc 0.82, park-end r1 192 deg around the Sun). ROOT CAUSE: the park-end r1 anchor is evaluated on the CADENCE clock (`parkReplayUT = RelaunchUTForWindow`, where the body-relative escape leg + the #1172 LAN-rotated park sit) while the transfer aims on the SYNODIC clock (`departureUT = DepartureUTForWindow`); they coincide ONLY at window 0 (and at every window when cadence == synodic, i.e. span <= synodic) and DIVERGE by k*(cadence - synodic) (>= ~3.6M s for stock Kerbin->Duna) at k>=1 of a span>synodic mission - the override then anchors r1 where the launch body is NOT at the aimed departure, producing the wild conic. THE BOUNDED FIX (this task): a new pure predicate `ReaimWindowPlanner.ParkEndOverrideClocksCoincide(parkReplayUT, departureUT)` (|diff| < 1.0 s) gates the F2 SYNTH BUNDLE (r1 override + `BuildParkingCandidateTofs` + true-duration render bounds + captureShift) in `ReaimPlaybackResolver.BuildWindowSegments`: `hasDepartureOverride = (anchor.Mode == ParkEndOverride) && ParkEndOverrideClocksCoincide(parkReplayUT, nominalDepartureUT)`. When the clocks diverge (k>=1, span>synodic) the EXISTING code falls back to the tested Increment-1 path (r1 = launch-body center, `BuildCandidateTofs` recorded-centered band, NaN render bounds, captureShift 0) - the pre-F2 #1166 behavior, a SANE Kerbin->Duna conic, NOT wild. CRITICAL - #1172 PRESERVED: `parkDeltaLonDeg` (the park LAN re-phase) is computed from the anchor decision and passed to `ReplaceHeliocentricLeg` at EVERY window regardless of the gate, and `ReplaceHeliocentricLeg` applies it purely on `parkDeltaLonDeg != 0.0` (no override-flag dependency), so the park render still re-phases onto live Kerbin at k>=1 (the distant-loiter teleport stays fixed). A Verbose log fires when gated off (parkReplayUT-departUT divergence, "-> Increment-1 Kerbin-center fallback (sane, not wild); every-window-correct needs Approach A (overlap)") and the "re-aimed transfer ready" line's `departAnchor` reads `launchCenter(gated:clocks-diverge,k>=1)`. Tests: `ReaimWindowPlannerTests` (+3: the pure predicate coincide/diverge/epsilon, window-0-coincides for both schedule shapes + k>=1-gated-off for the divergent one, and span<=synodic coincides at every window so F2 is unaffected for normal missions); the in-game `ReaimEndToEndInGameTest` parking fixture Case A + Case B both drive k=0 (parkReplayUT == departureUT == D0 => gate true => F2 applies => the seam asserts still hold, unweakened). Full headless suite green (15,754).

**DEFERRED every-window solution = Approach A (overlap instances, cadence == synodic).** To render the park-anchored transfer correctly at EVERY window the engine must relaunch on the SYNODIC clock so the cadence clock and the synodic clock coincide at all k; since span > synodic, ~2 instances overlap (inherent). Staged in 3 sub-PRs: (i) `MissionLoopUnitBuilder` sets `effectiveOverlapCadence = ComputeEffectiveLaunchCadence(synodic, span, MaxOverlapGhostsPerRecording)` gated on `span > synodic && DepartedFromHeliocentricPark`; (ii) `ReaimPlaybackResolver` re-key the cache to `(member, window)` + add an explicit-window overload + a cache bound; (iii) `GhostMapPresence` add a per-frame `RefreshOverlapInstanceOrbits` loop over `overlapInstanceVessels` reusing `ApplyOrbitToVessel` for the per-instance body transition. CONFIRMED BLOCKER: the overlap presence is create-only - there is NO per-frame body-transition refresh, so a body-changing interplanetary ghost (Kerbin->Sun->Duna) cannot currently render its per-cycle conic; building that refresh is the bulk of sub-PR (iii). The naive "move parkReplayUT to the synodic clock" (Approach C) was REJECTED in plan review: it is a literal revert of PR #1172 (re-opens the ~142 deg/loop distant-loiter park teleport).

**Increment 2 (deferred, the full overlap build):** builder gate `effectiveOverlapCadence = synodic` when `span > synodic && DepartedFromHeliocentricPark`; resolver cache re-key to `(member, window)` + an explicit-window overload; the NEW per-frame body-transition refresh for overlap map/TS instances routed through the windowed resolver (so each per-cycle instance renders its own window's transfer + park rotation across SOI changes); synodic-quantized pad-align; the loiter-cut/arrival-hold overlap-path remap decision; the forced KSC overlap behavior. This is where "the transfer touches live Kerbin at EVERY window + N per-cycle correct orbit lines/icons" is achieved. Do NOT modify PR #1155; the Kerbin-SOI warp-reseed icon-teleport + body-fixed launch seam are a separate session's scope.

  - **Sub-PR 1 (i) landed DARK (branch `reaim-overlap-builder-gate`):** `MissionLoopUnitBuilder` flips the unit's `effectiveOverlapCadence` to the synodic period (`GhostPlaybackLogic.ComputeEffectiveLaunchCadence(sched.SynodicPeriodSeconds, span, GhostPlayback.MaxOverlapMissionInstances)`, which resolves to synodic for the s15 shape where the cap floor span/20 << synodic), routing the unit OUT of the #1174 launch-hold-secondary (`!UnitMemberOverlaps`) branch and INTO the per-instance self-overlap path. `effectiveCadence` (the playback/span cadence) stays `max(span, synodic)`; only the overlap cadence (the sole `UnitMemberOverlaps` lever) drops. Behind the default-OFF compile-time flag `GhostPlayback.ReaimSelfOverlapEnabled` via the pure `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.ShouldFlipToSelfOverlapCadence(flag, !padApplied, planSupported, departedFromHeliocentricPark, span>synodic)`, inserted AFTER the PadAlignLaunch block (also excludes `pad.Applied` as defense-in-depth) and before the LoopUnit ctor. With the flag false (production default) the flip never runs and builder output is byte-identical, so the #1174 regime is untouched. The flag STAYS OFF until sub-PR 3 lands the per-frame Kerbin->Sun->Duna body-following overlap refresh AND ports #1174's launch-hold rotation alignment onto the self-overlap instances - flipping it without those re-opens the #1174 launch->escape seam for this unit. Tests: `MissionLoopUnitBuilderTests` (+8: the `ShouldFlipToSelfOverlapCadence` truth table, the synodic cadence math for the s15 shape, and the `UnitMemberOverlaps` lever for `OverlapCadenceSeconds == synodic` vs `== max(span,synodic)`). No gameplay change, no schema change.
  - **Sub-PR 2 (ii) landed DARK (branch `reaim-overlap-resolver-rekey`):** `ReaimPlaybackResolver` cache re-keyed from per-`member` to per-`(member, window)` so two consecutive windows (k and k+1) coexist for overlapping instances, the explicit-window overload `TryResolveWindowSegmentsForWindow(memberId, memberSegments, plan, schedule, window, out segments)` added (no caller yet; sub-PR 3 wires it), and a bounded per-member eviction band (`[k-1, k+1]`, `CacheWindowBandHalfWidth = 1`) added so the tuple dict cannot leak windows at high warp between `Clear()`s. The currentUT overload (`TryResolveWindowSegments`) and the explicit overload share a `TryResolveWindowSegmentsCore`; the live path is byte-identical (same window derivation, same segments, just tuple-keyed) - verified by reasoning + the full headless suite (15,764 green) + a new `ReaimPlaybackResolverTests` (10 tests via a Unity-free `BuilderOverrideForTesting` seam, null in production: two-window concurrency, explicit==currentUT-for-same-window, eviction band bounded + per-member). No gameplay change, no schema change.

## Fixed 2026-06-15 - Looped re-aimed Kerbin->Duna mission with a two-burn (heliocentric-parking) departure declined re-aim -> broken render + "not aligned" (branch `reaim-heliocentric-parking-departure`) [classify fix pinned by xUnit; render addressed by the self-overlap milestone above; P4 needs in-game playtest]

**Bug (2026-06-15 playtest, save s15, looped mission "Kerbal X #2" / tree `ced78481`):** a valid looped Kerbin->Duna landing rendered broken on the map (launch polyline drew, then no transfer continuation, the icon teleported, all lines vanished) and the Missions tab read "not aligned". One root cause for both facets: re-aim DECLINED the mission (`ReaimDiag ... transferMemberSegs=0 reason='no member yields a re-aim transfer'`), so it replayed faithfully at an arbitrary loop phase (transfer aimed where Duna was, arrival ghost at live Duna, lines retired). NOT a duplication bug (the `.prec.txt` readable mirror shows orbit segments twice - flat list + TrackSection checkpoints - but the binary load is 14, per KSP.log `postOrbitSegments=14`); NOT a #1149 / map-render-merge regression; NOT P4 (`reaim-dest-loiter-retimer` only affects re-aim-ENGAGED arrival hold, inert here).

**Root cause:** the transfer member (`aa48920e`) records a HELIOCENTRIC PARKING orbit (Sun coast `sma=1.407e10` ~ Kerbin's solar orbit, ecc 0.033, ~152 days) BEFORE the trans-Duna burn (`sma=1.791e10`). `ReaimClassifier.Classify`'s transfer-run walk-back breaks at the 21.4% SMA step (> `DefaultAStepRelThreshold=0.05`), leaving the run = the last Sun coast only, whose predecessor is the Sun parking segment -> the explicit `"transfer departs from a heliocentric parking orbit or mid-course correction (deferred); staying faithful"` decline (`ReaimClassifier.cs`). Duna One (a direct single-pass transfer, no heliocentric park) classifies; this second mission's two-burn departure was outside re-aim's v1 envelope (the design deferred "Lambert assumes r1 = launch body").

**Fix (design `docs/dev/design-reaim-heliocentric-parking-departure.md`; workflow-designed + adversarially reviewed):** new pure `ReaimClassifier.IsHeliocentricParkingDeparture` flips the decline to ENGAGE for an ADMISSIBLE two-burn departure, leaving the synthesizer / resolver / assembler / window planner UNTOUCHED (`r1 = launchBody` unchanged - the only behaviour change is one conjunct on the `:224` decline). Admissible = EVERY common-ancestor (solar) loiter run keeps `DefaultKeepRevs` whole revolutions (reuses `ReaimLoiterCompressor.DetectRuns`, scanning ALL solar runs not just the predecessor, so no heliocentric loiter cut fires; engaging therefore adds no park-driven anchor shift on top of the re-aim schedule's anchor - distinct from the DIRECT-transfer byte-identical claim, where the predicate is never reached - and a launch-body L2 cut is unaffected), near-circular at BOTH the run anchor and the burn point (`ecc <= 0.1`; DetectRuns merges on sma only, so ecc can drift), AND co-orbital with the launch body at the burn point (last park segment's sma within 10% of the launch body's heliocentric sma, derived from its orbit period via Kepler's 3rd law - pure, no Unity; NOTE the sma+ecc gate bounds the departure ORBIT, not the true-anomaly PHASE, an accepted fail-closed limitation). Every other Sun predecessor fails closed -> faithful: a sub-period MCC arc (< 1 rev), a multi-rev solar park anywhere before the transfer (`wholeRevs > keepRevs`, the cut composition is unvalidated on a heliocentric park - deferred), an eccentric (or eccentric-at-burn-point) park, or a wide-sma park. The verbatim park leg is NOT an "inertial-fixed miss": it renders from a live `Orbit(..., Sun)`; the Sun does not move, so it replays on its true track every loop like the shipped escape/capture legs, and the park does not aim at the target (only the transfer leg is re-aimed). Per-member classify-reason logging added to `MissionLoopUnitBuilder` (the gather only logged the chosen member; the per-member decline reason is now visible in KSP.log), plus a `parking=` token on the `ReaimDiag` Supported line.

**Scope (decided 2026-06-15):** departure-side render + Missions-UI readout only (the destination-SOI landing-rotation ~131 deg alignment stays the separate Phase-4 `DestinationArrivalSolver` work); empty-cut parks only (multi-rev parks deferred). Engaging re-aim here also UNBLOCKS P4 / PR #1155 (its destination-loiter trim cannot fire until re-aim engages; `aa48920e` records a Duna destination loiter `sma=495883` ~11.63 revs that is exactly P4's target). Do NOT modify #1155.

**Tests:** `ReaimClassifierTests` (+12): the s15 two-burn fixture engages with the correct departure UT / tof / `DepartedFromHeliocentricPark`; multi-rev / eccentric / wide-sma parks decline; a non-adjacent earlier multi-rev solar park declines (all-runs empty-cut scan); a same-sma park eccentric at the burn point declines (burn-point ecc check); the predicate's loiter / admissibility / fail-closed branches; the existing sub-period (`Classify_HeliocentricLoiterBeforeTransfer_Declined`) and same-sma >1-rev decline fences stay green. Full headless suite green (15696, InjectAllRecordings env-flake excluded). **Acceptance pending in-game:** load s15, loop "Kerbal X #2", confirm `ReaimDiag plan.Supported=true parking=True`, `ENGAGED re-aim Kerbin->Duna`, the Missions tab shows the synodic window (existing IsReaim path), the map renders the full transfer, and (bonus) P4 `dest-trim` fires on the Duna loiter.

## ~~Fixed 2026-06-15 - Looped transfer ghost's incoming SOI-approach orbit line drew one fragment at the crossing, the rest seconds later (branch `fix-loop-arc-segment-coalesce`)~~ DONE, in-game validated

**Observed:** a looping Kerbin -> Mun transfer GHOST on the FLIGHT-scene map draws only the FIRST piece of its incoming Mun trajectory at SOI crossing; the rest of the curve toward Mun appears ~27 s later. The stock ghost orbit line is ON and drawing the whole crossing (`reason=visible-body-frame lineActive=True`), but its drawn ARC SWEEP is geometrically clipped to one OrbitSegment at a time (Arc-clip log: `arc=11.8deg` then ~27 s later `arc=112.0deg`, the two pieces contiguous in eccentric anomaly).

**Root cause:** the Mun approach is stored as 2-3 ADJACENT OrbitSegments with IDENTICAL Kepler elements (the recorder closes + reopens a segment at every recording-mode transition; this split is BY DESIGN). For a LOOP-SHIFTED ghost, `GhostMapPresence.TryGetVisibleOrbitBoundsForGhostVessel` SHORT-CIRCUITS to the stored single applied-segment bounds (`ghostOrbitBounds[pid]`, written one segment per tick) and SKIPS the non-loop merge (`TrajectoryMath.TryGetOrbitWindowForMapDisplay` / `ExpandEquivalentOrbitWindow`) the non-loop path runs. So the arc clips to one same-orbit fragment; the next is revealed only when the playback head advances into it. The line on/off gate uses a SEPARATE wide body-frame window (`ghostBodyFrameOrbitBounds`) and keeps the line ON correctly, so the symptom is the arc sweep, not the line toggle.

**Fix (Option A, expand-on-read; the recording is immutable):** new pure helper `TrajectoryMath.TryExpandStoredSingleSegmentWindow` locates the RAW recorded segment matching the stored window and grows it across element-equivalent adjacent neighbours (same `AreOrbitSegmentsEquivalentForMapDisplay` predicate the non-loop merge uses, PLUS an `isPredicted`-match guard mirroring `CoalesceSameOrbitFragments`, so a captured ellipse or a predicted ballistic tail stops the grow and is not folded in). `GhostMapPresence.ExpandStoredBoundsAcrossEquivalentSegments` un-shifts the stored live-frame bounds to raw (`MapLiveUTToEffUT`), expands on the raw committed `OrbitSegments`, then re-applies the loop shift, writing back to the arc-clip window ONLY when more than one fragment coalesces. Applied in the loop-shifted AND endpoint-tail short-circuit branches of `TryGetVisibleOrbitBoundsForGhostVessel`. Read-only / shape-clip only: `ghostOrbitBounds` (which drives `SetOrbit` + the icon epoch) is never mutated, so the icon stays on the single applied segment and only the drawn arc sweep widens. The recorder / optimizer are unchanged.

**Tests:** +6 pure xUnit in `OrbitSegmentTests` (`TryExpandStoredSingleSegmentWindow_*`): merges seg3+seg4 hyperbola and STOPS before the captured ellipse seg5; single-segment no-equivalent-neighbour returns count 1 (no widening); no-seed-match returns false (caller keeps stored bounds); does-not-merge-across-predicted-boundary; null/empty returns false; startUT match within tolerance. Plus 1 wrapper test in `GhostMapEndpointTailTests` (`TryGetVisibleOrbitBoundsForGhostVessel_LoopShifted_CoalescesEquivalentArcWindowAcrossSegments`) driving `ExpandStoredBoundsAcrossEquivalentSegments` end to end: asserts the returned window is the un-shifted-expanded-then-re-shifted seg0+seg1 span (stopping before the non-equivalent ellipse) and asserts the `Loop arc-window coalesced ... fragments=2 segIndices=0-1` log line. Full suite green (15569 passed).

**Related:** this is the non-re-aim, loop-shifted follow-up anticipated by the 2026-06-02 Playtest-2 fix (`ReaimSegmentAssembler.CoalesceSameOrbitFragments`), which merged the same same-orbit fragments but was scoped to re-aim members only; this fix covers the ordinary loop-shifted ghost via the visible-bounds resolution.

**In-game VALIDATED 2026-06-15** (`logs/2026-06-15_1835_mun-soi-fix2-check`, merged-fix DLL): the coalesce fires on the Mun approach (`Loop arc-window coalesced reason=loop-shifted fragments=2 segIndices=3-4`, stopping before the non-equivalent captured ellipse), and the Arc clip now draws a single continuous `arc=123.9deg` on every occurrence across both loop members instead of the prior `arc=11.8deg` then `arc=112.0deg` two-piece reveal (both old values now absent). No regressions: 0 errors, 0 icon-off-orbit on the Mun ghosts, over-merge guard held. The few residual `icon-teleport`/`line-blink` anomalies are the separate known warp-reseed icon facet, not this arc-clip-window fix.

## Done 2026-06-14 - In-flight committed-restore-clone discard reverts cleanly (data-loss fix) + no-op auto-discard now covers committed missions (branch `autodiscard-noop-switch-segment`)

**Surfaced (2026-06-14, log `logs/2026-06-14_0043_refly-discard-dataloss`):** discarding an in-flight committed-restore clone stranded it, then a whole-tree discard wiped the committed mission (the "Kerbal X" 13-recording mission was deleted; recovered from a snapshot). Plan: `docs/dev/plans/committed-clone-noop-discard.md`.

**Chain:** `TryTakeCommittedTreeForSpawnedVesselRestore` deep-clones the committed tree into the live activeTree (copy-on-write; the committed ORIGINAL stays in `committedTrees` the whole in-flight session — verified `ParsekFlight.cs:14497-14521`). `TryDiscardActiveSwitchSegmentAttempt` on that clone IN-FLIGHT prunes the segment but reports `droppedPendingClone=False` (the clone is the active tree, not the pending slot), leaving the clone live. On the switch it is serialized `isActive`; OnLoad `TryRestoreActiveTreeNode` removes the committed original (`RemoveCommittedTreeById`) and stashes the clone to the Limbo slot; it strands; a later whole-tree merge-dialog Discard runs `DiscardPendingTree`, deleting the mission (the `IsCommittedRecordingId` guard defeated because the original was already removed).

**Fix (Goal 1):** new `ParsekFlight.DiscardActiveSwitchSegmentAttemptRevertingLiveClone` — captures the live committed-restore-clone tree id BEFORE the scoped discard clears the restore attempt, runs the scoped discard (prunes the fresh-GUID segment, clears session + restore attempt, deletes only segment sidecars), then if the captured clone is still the live activeTree tears it down via the proven `AutoDiscardActiveTreeCore` (in-memory only — deletes NO files, never touches `committedTrees`, verified). The clone is never serialized `isActive`, so OnLoad never removes the committed original, which survives untouched. Used by the in-flight pre-switch Discard handler (`DiscardPriorAndSwitchTo`, both manual + auto) and the scene-exit Hook 1 committed-clone path.

**Extension:** with the revert in place, the no-op auto-discard now covers committed missions: both hooks (scene exit + in-flight re-switch) auto-discard `CommittedRestoreClone` no-ops silently (revert to the committed original, no dialog), not just `Standalone`. Only `BgMemberOrMixed` defers (the rest of a live tree must commit). This makes "Fly to a tracked-mission vessel, do nothing, leave/switch" silent — the dominant use case.

**Follow-up 2026-06-14 (no-session committed-restore resume):** playtest (log `logs/2026-06-14_1147_noop-mainmenu-mapswitch`) found two gaps where auto-discard did not fire: exiting to MAIN MENU, and in-flight map Switch-To. Both are the SAME root cause — resuming a committed mission via the NO-SESSION path (`ResumeCommittedActiveRecording`, used when you Fly / Switch-To a far vessel and OnLoad re-resumes it in-place; it sets `liveResumeSessionStartUT`, not a `SwitchSegmentSession`). The session-gated no-op check never saw these. Fixed by `SwitchSegmentNoOpClassifier.IsNoOpResumeTail` (evaluates only the resume TAIL since `liveResumeSessionStartUT`, ignoring the committed history) + `ParsekFlight.TryEvaluateNoSessionCommittedResumeNoOp` / `AutoDiscardNoOpNoSessionCommittedResume` (revert the clone to the committed original — same safe teardown), wired into Hook 1 (scene exit, incl. MAINMENU) and the Case B/C pre-switch path (reusing `DiscardActiveRecordingAndSwitchTo`). +9 xUnit (`ResumeTail_*`).

**Follow-up 2026-06-14 #2 (background-member refinement):** a further playtest (log `logs/2026-06-14_1236_noop-edge-case-4`) found the in-flight map Switch-To STILL deferred to a dialog, because the first cut deferred whenever the clone had ANY tracked background member — and a committed mission almost always has one (e.g. a station coasting on-rails, `onRails=1 checkpointed=0`). That over-deferred: a tracked-but-coasting member accrued nothing. Refined: `TryEvaluateNoSessionCommittedResumeNoOp` now flushes the foreground recorder, calls `backgroundRecorder.CheckpointAllVessels` (closes open on-rails orbit segments into the tree recordings), DEFERS only when a LOADED/physics background member is present (`BackgroundRecorder.HasLoadedBackgroundMembers` — per-frame content CheckpointAllVessels can't flush), then runs `IsNoOpResumeTail` on EVERY recording in the clone tree (foreground + on-rails members). A coasting station passes (revert, no dialog); a background member that actually moved (e.g. an SOI crossing flushes a body-changed orbit segment) keeps (defer). Safe: revert still only drops content recomputable from the committed original.

**Edge-case audit (2026-06-14, multi-agent workflow + 2 follow-up Opus agents covering the rate-limited dimensions):** one DATA-LOSS gap found and FIXED — `SwitchSegmentNoOpClassifier` gated only on `Recording.VesselDestroyed`, but `ApplyDestroyedFallback` (the active-vessel-crash finalize path) set only `TerminalStateValue=Destroyed`, never the bool, so a destruction that does NOT also emit an `onPartDie` Destroyed PartEvent (NaN/Kraken `Vessel.Die` cleanup) could leave a destroyed resume looking like a boring no-op and get auto-discarded. Fix (defense-in-depth, both): `ApplyDestroyedFallback` now also sets `rec.VesselDestroyed = true`, AND `IsNoOpSegment`/`IsNoOpResumeTail` gained a `TerminalStateValue==Destroyed` gate next to the bool gate. +2 xUnit. The audit otherwise found NO new wrong-discard/data-loss bug (PartEventTypes all caught; un-flushed SegmentEvents harmless — the un-mirrored types have no producer; resume seeds inert; disposition can't drop a multi-recording tree; revert never deletes the committed original; orbit checks sound). Three LOW-severity, non-data-loss FAIL-TO-FIRE edges are ACCEPTED (a do-nothing resume shows a one-click dialog or commits a boring segment instead of silently discarding — never loses data): (a) in-bubble `[`/`]` vessel-cycle away from a no-op session segment (no intent marker -> no no-op hook -> backgrounded -> later BgMemberOrMixed dialog); (b) quickload while resumed into a committed mission loses the session-transient `liveResumeSessionStartUT` anchor -> `no-resume-anchor` keep; (c) an atmosphere-graze / surface-jitter blip emits a non-boring section that blocks the discard (intentional conservative-keep bias).

**Regression FIXED (2026-06-14, log `logs/2026-06-14_1350_scene-exit-regression`):** the audit's `TerminalStateValue==Destroyed` gate (added above) was UNSCOPED in `IsNoOpResumeTail`, which broke scene-exit auto-discard entirely for every real mission. The no-session path (`TryEvaluateNoSessionCommittedResumeNoOp`) runs the tail check over EVERY recording in the restored clone, and a committed mission tree always carries debris recordings (spent boosters / stages) with `TerminalStateValue=Destroyed` from their ORIGINAL flight — destroyed decades of UT before the resume anchor. The unscoped gate tripped on the first such member (`keep reason=member:...:terminal-destroyed`), so leaving to TS / Space Center / Main Menu after a do-nothing resume surfaced a Merge/Discard dialog instead of silently discarding. Fix: scope BOTH destroyed gates in `IsNoOpResumeTail` by `segment.EndUT >= sinceUT` (consistent with every other window-scoped gate in that method) — a member that ended before the resume anchor is committed history, not part of the resume. The SESSION path `IsNoOpSegment` is unaffected (it inspects only the single active segment recording, which IS the resume, so its destroyed gate stays unscoped and correct). An in-window destruction whose payload bounds end before the anchor is still caught by the scoped Destroyed part-event backstop. +2 xUnit (`ResumeTail_TerminalDestroyedBeforeAnchor_IsNoOp`, `ResumeTail_VesselDestroyedBoolBeforeAnchor_IsNoOp`; existing in-window keep test kept as `ResumeTail_TerminalDestroyedInWindow_IsKept`).

**Dropped / residual:** the originally-proposed Goal 2 (a `DiscardPendingTree` re-commit guard) was DROPPED — `MergeState.Immutable` is the default for every recording, so the guard could not distinguish a taken-clone-whose-original-was-removed from a genuinely-uncommitted pending tree, and would resurrect trees the user deliberately discarded. With Goal 1 the strand is unreachable. Residual: the consume-site `superseded-by-new-switch` clear (`ParsekFlight.cs:~8898`, the documented S1 minor gap) does not route through the revert helper; a second rapid switch to a different target clears the prior session without teardown (the subsequent branch selection usually overwrites activeTree). Not data loss in practice, tracked as S1. Test delta: +1 xUnit (`IsCommittedTreeRestoreAttemptTree`); the in-flight teardown is runtime-coupled (validated by playtest + the code-grounded plan review).

## Done 2026-06-13 - Auto-discard no-op resumed (Fly / Switch-To) recording segments (branch `autodiscard-noop-switch-segment`)

**Goal:** when you Fly (Tracking-Station / KSC marker) or Switch-To a vessel and then leave / switch away without changing anything, the resumed recording segment changed nothing and there is no point keeping it (it only prolongs the ghost state and delays the real vessel spawn). Same spirit as `RecordingOptimizer.TrimBoringTail` ("so the ghost finishes quickly and the real vessel spawns promptly") and the idle-on-pad whole-tree auto-discard. Plan: `docs/dev/plans/autodiscard-noop-switch-segment.md`.

**Definition (locked with maintainer):** a segment is KEPT if it changed orbit elements, moved its landing/surface position (any non-boring track section: Atmospheric / ExoPropulsive / SurfaceMobile / Approach), docked / undocked, decoupled / staged, spawned debris / EVA children, fired an engine or RCS at positive throttle, or planted a flag. Idle EC drain, light / thermal-animation toggles, engine/RCS "off" seeds, and pure time-warp coasting are NOT meaningful, so a coast-or-sit-still segment is discarded. Science is recorded by the action/ledger recorder (not flight recordings), so it is irrelevant here.

**Implementation:** pure `SwitchSegmentNoOpClassifier.IsNoOpSegment` (gates: descendants, meaningful part event via `IsMeaningfulPartEvent`, non-TimeJump segment event, flag, dock target, all-boring sections, orbit-element delta) + `RecordingStore.TryClassifyActiveSwitchSegmentNoOp` (resolves the session tree / segment, verifies it is the live active recording, computes the descendant count + `SwitchSegmentDisposition`) + `ParsekFlight.TryEvaluateActiveSwitchSegmentNoOp` (restoring / Re-Fly / merge-journal guards, then flushes the recorder into the tree so the segment carries its in-flight payload before reading it, mirroring `IsActiveTreeIdleOnPad`). Two hooks, BOTH gated to the **Standalone disposition only**: scene exit (`SceneExitInterceptor.TryAutoDiscardNoOpSwitchSegment`, reuses the proven `AutoDiscardActiveTreeCore` whole-tree teardown) and in-flight map re-switch (`MapFocusObjectOnSelectPatch` Case A, Standalone-only after the 2026-06-14 data-loss fix, reuses the existing `DiscardPriorAndSwitchTo` Discard handler instead of prompting). No schema change. Test delta: +41 xUnit (`SwitchSegmentNoOpClassifierTests` pure + `SwitchSegmentNoOpEvaluatorTests` resolver/disposition).

**Data-loss fix (2026-06-14 playtest, log `logs/2026-06-14_0043_refly-discard-dataloss`):** the in-flight hook originally auto-discarded a `CommittedRestoreClone` no-op via a path that left the clone tree (carrying the whole committed mission) live (`droppedPendingClone=False`), which then stranded in the Limbo pending slot and was later whole-tree-discarded, deleting the entire 13-recording "Kerbal X" mission (recovered losslessly from the `logs/2026-06-13_2043_zoom-cull-repro` snapshot). Fully fixed: see the "Done 2026-06-14 - In-flight committed-restore-clone discard reverts cleanly" entry above — the in-flight discard now tears down the clone and reverts to the committed original, and the no-op auto-discard now safely covers committed missions in both hooks.

**Known limitations (intentional, documented):**
- **Pure internal-state changes with no recorded surface are not detectable** and so a coasting segment whose ONLY activity was one is discarded. Two cases: a **tank-to-tank fuel transfer** (no recorded event, per-vessel resource totals unchanged, end manifest not captured at the decision point) and an **intra-vessel crew transfer** between parts (no `onCrewTransferred` recording surface; the `SegmentEventType.CrewTransfer` enum value is never emitted, and the scene-exit flush does not move segment events into the tree recording anyway). Both change only internal state with no visual ghost representation, so discarding the segment loses no replayable content (consistent with the project's Visual & Recording Design Principle). Honoring "keep on crew/fuel transfer" would need a new internal-state recording surface - a separate feature. (The classifier keeps a non-TimeJump segment event defensively, but that gate is not reached at the live decision point; nothing meaningful is missed because breakage / part-destruction events ride flushed part events.)
- **Auto-discard covers Standalone AND CommittedRestoreClone (both hooks); only BgMemberOrMixed defers.** A no-op resume of a fresh vessel (Standalone) tears down the throwaway tree; a no-op resume of a committed mission (CommittedRestoreClone) reverts to the committed original (no dialog, mission preserved) via the 2026-06-14 revert-clone fix. BgMemberOrMixed (a live tree with other content beyond the segment) still defers to the dialog because the rest of the tree must commit.
- **Consume-site supersede minor gap:** if the in-flight pre-switch dialog fails to spawn or hits the re-entry guard, the prior session is cleared with `superseded-by-new-switch` without commit/discard, so a no-op segment can leak as plain tree data on those rare paths. The scene-exit hook still catches any armed no-op session on the next exit.
## Done 2026-06-13 - Looped route delivery ghost docked against a recorded station copy ~20 km away, plus a duplicate station ghost (branch `fix-loop-relative-live-anchor`)

**Observed (2026-06-13 playtest, log `logs/2026-06-13_1350_depot-ghost-double-d24`, "orbital supply route" save):** the player controls the live "Depot" station (Mun orbit, live pid 4277041026) and watches a looped ghost of "Deliverer Mun 1" dock with it. Instead, a ghost DOUBLE of the Depot plus the Deliverer ghost render ~20,821 m away at the Depot's recorded absolute Mun position, and the docking animation plays out there, not relative to the live Depot.

**Root cause:** mission-loop / route members persist the NON-loop recorded-anchor contract - `TrackSection.anchorRecordingId` set (Deliverer `b9f08d0f` -> Depot `7e0d79b5`), `anchorVesselId=0`, `Recording.LoopAnchorVesselId=0`, `LoopPlayback=False` (looping is driven at Mission/periodicity level via loopShift, not per-recording LoopPlayback). The documented live-PID loop path is doubly gated on `LoopAnchorVesselId!=0` AND `LoopPlayback` (`GhostPlaybackLogic.ShouldUseLoopAnchor` / `ShouldSpawnLoopedGhost`), so it is never entered for these recordings. Both flight and map/KSC playback therefore resolve the anchor through `RelativeAnchorResolver` to the recorded Depot lat/lon/alt (`body.GetWorldSurfacePosition`, ~20.8 km from the live Depot) and apply the ~3 m anchor-local docking offset there. Separately the Depot's OWN loop ghost is drawn alongside the loaded live Depot via the flight `IsVesselRecordedByTree` carve-out and the map `loopMemberInWindow` carve-out (`GhostMapPresence.ResolveMapPresenceGhostSource`).

**Fix (playback-side, the offending recording is immutable):** Step 1 binds the anchor pose to the live launch-matched vessel inside `RelativeAnchorResolver.TryResolveAnchorPose` (between the re-fly resolution and `TryResolveRecordingPose`): a new host delegate `ParsekFlight.TryResolveLiveLaunchMatchedAnchorPoseForResolver` returns the live vessel's `transform.position`/`rotation` (via `TryResolveLoopLiveAnchorPose`, the recorder's vesselTransform frame, so docking attitude is correct) when the anchor recording's own launch-matched live craft is loaded, else null -> recorded-anchor fallback unchanged. Wired from both context builders (flight `BuildFlightRelativeAnchorResolverContext` + map/KSC `RecordedRelativeAnchorPoseResolver.TryBuildContext`), so flight, map-presence, and KSC all converge on the one resolver site. Guid-gated via `GhostPlaybackLogic.RealVesselExistsForRecording` (`VesselLaunchIdentity`): persistentId is craft-baked, three same-craft Depot launches exist on disk, so a different-launch live vessel never binds. Step 2 suppresses a LOOP MEMBER's OWN ghost only while it is the LIVE docking anchor of an in-window relative member this-or-last frame (the Step-1 live-bind event), NOT for the whole loop (see the 2026-06-14 over-suppression follow-up below: the whole-loop generalization was the over-broad cut). The suppression term is the guid-gated `GhostPlaybackLogic.IsLiveAnchorDoubleSuppressed(rec, loopingLike)` = `loopingLike && RealVesselExistsForRecording(rec) && RelativeAnchorResolver.WasLiveBoundThisOrLastFrame(rec.RecordingId)` at all five sites, AND-scoped to loop membership so flight and map agree on scope: flight in `ParsekFlight.ComputePlaybackFlags` gates the OR into `externalVesselSuppressed` on `loopingLike` (`rec.LoopPlayback || chainLooping || cachedLoopUnits.IsMember(i)`, the same term the BUG-B dormancy block uses), with a dedicated `[Anchor]` Verbose line at the decision; map tightens the `loopMemberInWindow` carve-out in `ResolveMapPresenceGhostSource` via `liveLaunchMatchedAnchorOfActiveMember` (threaded from the TS lifecycle, TS startup, flight pending-create, and overlap-instance create sites, each reusing the guid-gated `realVesselExists` term AND the new live-bind conjunct, never the pid-only `IsMaterializedForMapPresence` that feeds `alreadyMaterialized`). The loop gate keeps the suppression off the player's own active recording, an active re-fly history ghost, and the tree-history carve-outs in `ShouldSkipExternalVesselGhost` (`isActiveRecording` / `IsGhostedByChain` / `IsVesselRecordedByTree`); only a looping anchor being docked right now is hidden. A Depot watched looping from afar with no live vessel loaded fails the existence check, so its ghost still draws. (The 2026-06-14 follow-up re-converged with the earlier `LiveAnchorBindTracker.WasLiveBoundRecently` recency idea - which the original #1136 cut had removed in favor of the whole-loop existence check - but sources the bind from the engine's own `RelativeAnchorResolver` Step-1 live-bind, NOT a re-derived `ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT` membership mapping, which is the documented drift dead-end.)

**Doc-accuracy note:** the header metadata (loopAnchorPid / loopPlayback / recordedVesselGuid) lives in `persistent.sfs` RECORDING blocks and the live VESSEL guid in the save, NOT in the `.prec`/`.prec.txt` trajectory sidecar (the original diagnosis wording "verified in the .prec.txt" was imprecise; the `.prec.txt` carries the `anchorRecordingId` and the anchor-local offset point, the SFS carries the loop/guid metadata). Recorder-side population of `LoopAnchorVesselId` for route members is explicitly NOT pursued: it cannot fix the immutable on-disk recording, and these are `LoopPlayback=False` mission-periodicity members so populating it would not engage `ShouldSpawnLoopedGhost` without also flipping the `LoopPlayback` gate (which would alter unrelated loop semantics).

**Tests:** +3 `RelativeAnchorResolverTests` (live-bind / recorded fallback / inert-when-unwired; the live-bind test now also asserts the bound `AnchorPose.WorldRotation` carries the live anchor rotation, locking docking-attitude propagation in a headless test) + `RouteLiveAnchorTests` covering the whole-loop suppression headlessly: the guid gate at the predicate level (`RealVesselExistsForRecording` same-launch suppresses / different-launch does NOT / no-live-vessel does NOT) plus the map-surface decision gate (`ResolveMapPresenceGhostSource` returns `None` with the live-anchor-double skip reason when the whole-loop term is set, and does NOT take the live-anchor branch when it is clear) + `FlightPlaybackExplainabilityTests` driving `ComputePlaybackFlags` through the vessel-exists / guid overrides on a loop-member anchor (anchor ghost skipped via `ExternalVesselSuppressed` when the same-launch live vessel is loaded, still spawnable, spawn-suppressed head total not inflated; NOT skipped for a same-craft different launch; NOT skipped when the live vessel is absent; and a scope test confirming a NON-loop recording is NOT suppressed even with its launch-matched live vessel loaded) + an in-game `RuntimeTests.LoopedRelativeMemberDocksWithLiveAnchor` (RouteLiveAnchor category) asserting the resolved anchor pose binds within metres of the live anchor transform (position + attitude) with no ~20 km ghost double; skips when no live route anchor is present. The former `LiveAnchorBindTracker` recency tests were removed with the tracker. Deferred: the two flight-scene map-presence state-vector UPDATE branches (`map-presence-soi-gap-state-vector-update`) refresh an existing ghost's orbit only, so they cannot create the double (the create paths are all suppressed); left unmodified.

**Known limitation / playtest-verify (review major finding, 2026-06-13):** the live-anchor bind in `RelativeAnchorResolver.TryResolveAnchorPose` is NOT gated to Logistics route members - it fires for ANY top-level Relative-anchored recording (any rendezvous / station-approach capture carrying `TrackSection.anchorRecordingId`) whenever that anchor's launch-matched live vessel is loaded. This is the intended Relative-frame contract and is correct for the steady-station route case (the live anchor barely moves between recorded window and replay), but it embeds a UT-alignment assumption: `TryResolveLiveLaunchMatchedAnchorPoseForResolver` resolves the live anchor's CURRENT transform and ignores `targetUT`, so a NON-looped relative ghost replaying its recorded pass while the player keeps flying the live anchor (which has since moved/rotated) snaps to `liveAnchorNow + recordedOffset` and can displace from the recorded scene. NOT a regression for ordinary parent-anchored debris / controlled-children (steered to the `bodyFixedFrames` surface by the `ShouldRetire` / `ShouldSkipRecordedRelativeResolver` gates before the bind). Watch this specifically in the upcoming in-game playtest (run `RuntimeTests.LoopedRelativeMemberDocksWithLiveAnchor` in the "orbital supply route" save AND eyeball a non-looped rendezvous ghost whose live anchor is loaded and moving). If displacement is observed there, scope the bind (e.g. only when the focus member's replay UT is within the live anchor's currently-replaying loop window, or only for mission-periodicity loop members) rather than broadening it to every `anchorRecordingId`-carrying section. Per-finding guidance: do not over-scope pre-emptively, which would regress legitimate non-route relative cases.

## Done 2026-06-14 - #1136 Step-2 over-suppressed ALL route meshes while watching the looped route from a fresh launch (branch `fix-flight-anchor-oversuppress`)

**Observed (2026-06-14 playtest, log `logs/2026-06-14_1220_mun-depot-dock-relative-ghost`, "orbital supply route" save):** a fresh new-mission launch (`#autoLOC_501224`) watches the looped supply route replay. The relative-member delivery ghost ("Kerbal X") approached the live Depot correctly in MAP view (icon + path), but its in-bubble FLIGHT MESH never appeared. The #1136 Step-2 cut suppressed the in-flight mesh of EVERY loop member: 11 distinct recordings (4 "Depot", 5 "Kerbal X"/"Kerbal X Probe", 1 "Deliverer Mun 1", 1 "Transporter") each logged `Step-2 suppressed live-anchor double (whole loop)` 82x. The scene had 18 live vessels loaded (the real route craft parked at the station), so `RealVesselExistsForRecording(rec)` was true for all of them and the whole-loop gate hid the entire route. The map survived only because the 4 map sites additionally AND on `alreadyMaterialized`, which was false this session.

**Root cause:** the #1136 Step-2 gate `loopingLike && RealVesselExistsForRecording(rec)` keyed on bare guid-gated live-vessel existence, which is true for any loaded route craft regardless of whether it is the station being docked. The static `anchorRecordingId` graph does NOT discriminate either: it cross-cuts vessel role - `56298d83 "Kerbal X"` is a PURE anchor (7 members dock it; an anchor-only predicate would keep suppressing the wanted delivery mesh), and `0c8ec58d "Depot"` is itself a relative MEMBER (`anchorRecordingId=44129e52`; an anchor-only predicate would un-suppress its duplicate, the #1136 regression). "Is an anchor in the graph" is not "is a station the player is docking against".

**Fix (playback-side, narrows the existing 5-site gate by one conjunct):** gate Step-2 on the ACTUAL Step-1 live-bind event, not the static graph and not a re-derived UT mapping. `RelativeAnchorResolver.TryBindLiveLaunchMatchedAnchorPose`, on its `source=live` branch, stamps the bound anchor's `RecordingId` into a process-static, frame-scoped `HashSet<string>` (`liveBoundAnchorRecIds`) stamped with the current frame (`Time.frameCount` via an injectable `FrameProviderForTesting`; the set Clears once per frame on the first bind, so it is allocation-free in steady state). `WasLiveBoundThisOrLastFrame(recId)` returns `set.Contains(recId) && currentFrame - stampFrame <= 1`. The shared predicate `GhostPlaybackLogic.IsLiveAnchorDoubleSuppressed(rec, loopingLike)` = `loopingLike && RealVesselExistsForRecording(rec) && WasLiveBoundThisOrLastFrame(rec.RecordingId)` replaces the flight gate (`ParsekFlight.ComputePlaybackFlags`) and is AND-ed into the 4 map sites (TS lifecycle, TS startup, flight pending-create, overlap-instance create) on top of their existing `realVesselExists` term. The inbound delivery member is the resolver FOCUS, never the resolved anchor, so its own id is never in the bind set - its mesh always draws; only the station BEING docked right now is hidden, scoped to the actual docking overlap. **One-frame lag:** `ComputePlaybackFlags` runs before `engine.UpdatePlayback` (where positioning fires the binds), so the flight predicate reads the previous frame's set; a continuously-docking anchor re-stamps every frame, so the `<=1` tolerance keeps it suppressed continuously, and a docking that just started/ended flashes the duplicate at most ~1 frame (sub-perceptual at the ~20 km standoff). In the reported scene ZERO live-binds fire (the looped ghosts are loop-shifted ~76.3M s out of any docking window), so all 11 meshes draw and the bug is fixed; a Depot duplicate is suppressed only on frames carrying a live bind to its id, preserving #1136 intent.

**Tests:** `RouteLiveAnchorTests` gains the live-bind ledger contract (false before any bind; true at the bind frame and N+1, false at N+2; only the bound id; set clears when the frame advances) and the `IsLiveAnchorDoubleSuppressed` predicate (anchor live-vessel + loopingLike + live-bound suppresses; same but NOT live-bound does NOT - the scene fix; the inbound relative member is NOT suppressed because its own id never enters the bind set - the regression, using the real `b9f08d0f -> 7e0d79b5` Deliverer/Depot edge and the `56298d83` pure-anchor id as fixtures; no-live-vessel and not-loopingLike do NOT). `FlightPlaybackExplainabilityTests` drives `ComputePlaybackFlags` through the live-bind ledger: the anchor is skipped via `ExternalVesselSuppressed` only when live-bound (still spawnable, head total not inflated, plus the batched `Step-2 live-anchor-double: suppressed=N` summary line); a live-vessel-loaded-but-not-live-bound anchor is NOT suppressed (pins the scene fix); a relative member whose anchor target is live-bound is NOT suppressed (pins the regression); the different-launch / no-live-vessel / non-loop cases stamp the bind set to isolate the OTHER gate term. The in-game `RuntimeTests.LoopedRelativeMemberDocksWithLiveAnchor` additionally asserts the inbound member's own ghost is never live-anchor-suppressed while the anchor it just docked through the resolver IS (with its live vessel loaded). The headless tests stamp the ledger by driving a real resolve through the public `TryResolveAnchorPose` path with a live-anchor delegate (the exact stamp site), so the stamp is proven not assumed.

## Done 2026-06-13 - Tracking Station "Fly" loaded the WRONG vessel when ghost trajectories were on the map (branch `fix-tsfly-ghost-index`)

**Observed (2026-06-13 playtest, log `logs/2026-06-13_1742_switch-depot-merge-bug`):** the player clicked Fly on the "Depot" station (pid 4277041026) in the Tracking Station but was placed in control of "Kerbal X Probe" (pid 575069177). KSP.log: `TS Fly intent armed ... targetPid=4277041026`, then `Vessel switch detected: '' -> 'Kerbal X Probe'`, then `SwitchIntent refused reason=stale-target-mismatch markerTargetPid=4277041026 newVesselPid=575069177` (the FLIGHT-side consume correctly declined to record on the wrong vessel - a symptom, not the cause).

**Root cause:** stock `SpaceTracking.FlyVessel(Vessel v)` does `GamePersistence.SaveGame("persistent")` then `FlightDriver.StartAndFocusVessel("persistent", FlightGlobals.Vessels.IndexOf(v))` - it identifies the target purely by its INDEX in the live `FlightGlobals.Vessels` list, then focuses that index in the loaded file. `GhostTrackingStationInitPatch` pre-creates ghost map ProtoVessels in the `SpaceTracking.Awake` prefix BEFORE the real vessels load, so the ghosts sit at the FRONT of the live list; `GhostMapPresence.StripFromSave` then removes them from the saved persistent.sfs. So `IndexOf(v)` counts the leading ghosts while the loaded file has none, landing the player (number-of-ghosts-before-the-target) slots away from the intended vessel (5 ghosts in the reproduced session).

**Fix:** `SwitchIntentTrackingStationFlyPatch.Prefix` (the real-vessel Fly Prefix, after its ghost-guard mirror early-return and before stock IndexOf/SaveGame) now calls the new `GhostMapPresence.RemoveAllGhostVesselsBeforeStockFly(targetPid)`, which strips all ghost map vessels from the LIVE list so the live index and the ghost-free saved file are consistent and stock focuses the intended vessel first time. It first captures the would-be drift via the pure unit-tested `GhostMapPresence.ComputeFlyIndexDrift(livePids, ghostPids, targetPid)` (count of ghost pids at a live index strictly below the target; -1 sentinel when the target is absent) and logs an Info `[SwitchIntentPatch] TS Fly pre-stock ghost strip` line with the drift it prevented (Warn on the -1 sentinel, Verbose no-op when there are no ghosts). Removal reuses the existing `RemoveAllGhostVessels` (per-ghost `Die()` in try/catch) and fires only on a real-vessel Fly (the ghost-block path keeps its ghosts and stays in the TS). The missed-switch safety net in `TryConsumeStockActionIntent` was deliberately NOT added: the root-cause strip makes the index correct first-time, so the existing stale-target-mismatch refusal stays as the residual guard. Test delta: +13 xUnit (`FlyIndexDriftTests`: 10 drift facts + 3 log-capture) plus in-game `TrackingStationFlyStrip_RemovesGhostsFromLiveList`.

## Done 2026-06-13 - Pre-switch Merge/Discard dialog showed the whole resumed tree's multi-year span, not the short new segment (branch `fix-tsfly-ghost-index`)

**Observed (2026-06-13 playtest, same log):** after switching onto an existing committed vessel and flying it ~17s, switching away popped the Merge/Discard dialog reading "Kerbal X - 8 years" (the whole resumed mission) instead of the few-second segment just flown.

**Root cause:** `MergeDialog.ResolveDialogBodyDuration` shows the segment duration ONLY when a `SwitchSegmentSession` is armed. The player landed on the committed vessel via the OnLoad committed-tree restore (`ParsekFlight.TryTakeCommittedTreeForSpawnedVesselRestore` -> `ResumeCommittedActiveRecording`), which resumes the committed tree and re-attaches the recorder to the EXISTING committed recording WITHOUT arming a session, so the dialog fell back to `ComputeTreeDurationRange(tree)` = the full span. Crucially the resumed recording's Points are appended in place, so its `StartUT` is the original (multi-year-ago) launch UT - `currentUT - StartUT` would STILL render ~8 years, not the segment.

**Fix:** capture a per-session live-resume anchor. `ParsekFlight.liveResumeSessionStartUT` (transient, not serialized) is reset to NaN in `PrepareSessionStateForRecorderStart` (the single recorder-start funnel, so a prior craft's anchor cannot leak) and re-armed to the current UT only on the no-session resume/promote paths (`ResumeCommittedActiveRecording`, `PromoteRecordingFromBackground`). `MergeDialog.ResolveNoSessionDialogBodyDuration` (the no-session branch) now shows `currentUT - resumeStartUT` when this dialog's tree carries the currently-live recording, gated by `tree.Recordings.ContainsKey(liveId)` (cross-tree safety), a finite anchor, and `currentUT > resumeStartUT` (reusing the session-armed clamp); otherwise it falls back to tree-wide exactly as before. Case A (session-armed) is untouched and takes precedence over the new branch. A new `LiveResumedSegmentProviderForTesting` seam plus `ParsekFlight.GetLiveResumedRecordingIdForDialog` / `GetLiveResumeSessionStartUT` accessors (null/NaN off-Unity) make the branch headlessly testable; every return path logs a `[SwitchSegment] ... duration source=` line (live-resumed-segment / tree-wide). The anchor is best-effort across a save/reload (resets to NaN, falls back to tree-wide until the next resume re-captures it). Test delta: +10 xUnit (`MergeDialogLiveResumedSegmentDurationTests` 6 + `ParsekFlightLiveResumeAccessorTests` 4).

## Done 2026-06-12 - Dock/undock wrote up to three identical-UT structural snapshot points (branch `fix-structural-snapshot-dup`)

**Observed (2026-06-12 audit, log `logs/2026-06-12_1915_m4c-save-recording-crew-audit`):** the docked-interval recording `4759c914` ends with THREE points at the identical undock UT 6738307.0211730218, and the older mission's docked composite `70667ab4` shows the same triple at its undock UT - a long-standing artifact reproduced on every dock/undock cycle. One `Part.Undock()` call fires `onPartUndock` plus one `onPartJointBreak` per docking port at the same physics-clock UT; each handler appended its own `StructuralEventSnapshot`-flagged point of the same live vessel state (KSP.log 19:12:51.684: `Undock` + `JointBreak` + `JointBreak`, identical lat/lon/alt/flags). The equal-UT appends pass the #419 monotonicity tolerance ("boundary seeds"), but the strictly-increasing Catmull-Rom section fit fails on them (`Catmull-Rom fit failed ... reason=non-monotonic UT at sample 25`), leaving the section unsmoothed, and the duplicates waste storage against the minimal-recording principle.

**Fix:** new pure `FlightRecorder.HasStructuralEventSnapshotAtTail(points, eventUT)` - true when the tail point is already structural-flagged at the event UT (1e-6 tolerance, matching `TryFindStructuralEventSnapshotPointForUT`). Both producers guard on it before committing: `FlightRecorder.AppendStructuralEventSnapshot` (foreground) skips with a Verbose dedup log, and `BackgroundRecorder.AppendStructuralEventSnapshot` mirrors it with a `deduped` counter in its skip summary. Tail-only is sufficient because the duplicate events fire within one physics tick (no regular sample can interleave). A regular unflagged sample at the same UT does NOT suppress the snapshot (the flag carries boundary info), and distinct-UT structural events are unaffected. Existing recordings keep their duplicates (recorded data is immutable); the next dock/undock playtest should show no `Catmull-Rom fit failed` warning for the docked segment. Test delta: +8 xUnit cases in `FlightRecorderStructuralEventTests` (15161 -> 15169, all green).

## Done 2026-06-12 - Stand-in kerbal duplicated across multiple live vessels (branch `fix-standin-duplication`)

**Observed (2026-06-12 playtest, log `logs/2026-06-12_1915_m4c-save-recording-crew-audit`):** the same stand-in, Barton Kerman, was crew on BOTH vessels in the scene after a Mun rendezvous; the collected save has him aboard FOUR vessels (Depot x2, Transporter, Deliverer Mun 1), Lagerpont aboard three, Adlo aboard two. The roster holds ONE entry per kerbal, so recovery/EVA/status handling of any one copy corrupts the others (the 18:45:11 `Assigned -> Available` / "found inside a part but status is set as missing" tug-of-war at save load).

**Root cause:** `crewReplacements` maps each reserved kerbal to ONE stand-in by design (`KerbalsModule.ApplyToRoster` Step 3 bridges `GetActiveOccupant` per slot), and every placement site applied that map blindly, without checking the stand-in's `rosterStatus`.
