Once the stand-in was Assigned (aboard any live vessel), each further application seated the same `ProtoCrewMember` on another vessel: (1) `CrewAutoAssignPatch.ApplyCrewAssignmentSwaps` swapped the stand-in into every new VAB/launch-dialog manifest (the 18:55:24 launch armed this playtest's duplicate while Barton sat in Mun orbit aboard the previous mission's vessel); (2) `PlaceOrphanedReplacements` only checked the ACTIVE vessel's crew before placing, so at 19:13:30 it injected Lagerpont and Adlo into the Depot while both were aboard other persisted vessels; (3) `SwapReservedCrewInFlight` Pass 1 had the same blind `AddCrewmemberAt`; (4) `SwapReservedCrewInSnapshot` (KSC spawn, bug #167) wrote the stand-in name into spawn snapshots blindly (`RemoveDuplicateCrewFromSnapshot` only sees `FlightGlobals.Vessels`, which is empty at KSC).

**Intended contract** (from the `CrewAutoAssignPatch` header and the `CleanUpReplacement` doc "If the replacement is Assigned (on a mission), leave them as a 'real' kerbal"): an Assigned stand-in is busy and not reusable; the seat is left empty.

**Fix:** new pure `CrewReservationManager.ClassifyStandInForPlacement` (plus `IsStandInPlaceable`) enforced at all four sites: Assigned and Dead stand-ins are never placed, Missing stand-ins keep the established rescue-to-Available-then-place convention (`ReserveCrewIn` / `PlaceOrphanedReplacements` / `RescueReservedMissingCrewInSnapshot` agreement; the manifest swap and Pass 1 rescue inline, the KSC snapshot path writes Missing through for the downstream spawn-route rescue). The manifest swap routes through the new pure `CrewAutoAssignPatch.DecideStandInPlacement` (clears the seat, logs the placement verdict + status), Pass 1 skips with a fail log, orphan placement gets a roster-wide Assigned check + `skippedAssignedToOtherVessel` summary counter (checked after the active-vessel skip so that bucket keeps its meaning), and `SwapReservedCrewInSnapshot` takes an optional roster-status resolver + `out seatsCleared` (KSC spawn passes the live roster, falls back to the legacy blind swap on a null roster, and logs swapped vs cleared distinctly). Existing multi-residence copies in old saves are NOT repaired (live vessel state, not Parsek data); they drain as those vessels are recovered or destroyed, and the new guards stop fresh duplication. Test delta: +20 xUnit cases (15141 -> 15161, all green) + in-game `OrphanPlacement_AssignedStandIn_SkippedToAvoidDuplicate` (CrewReservation category) pinning the orphan-pass skip end to end.

## Done 2026-06-11 - Logistics M6 slice: live route hold-reason legibility (branch `logistics-m6-hold-reasons`)

**M6 first bullet, live-hold half** (design `docs/parsek-logistics-supply-routes-design.md` 19.4 M6 / 19.6 rule 9; plan `docs/dev/plan-logistics-m6-hold-reasons.md`). A live route that cannot dispatch now explains itself in the Logistics window instead of only in the KSP.log BLOCKED line:

- **Capture:** four sparse additive `Route` fields (`LastHoldKind` enum-by-name, `LastHoldDetail` raw evaluator token verbatim, `LastHoldShortfall`, `LastHoldUT`) written by `Route.RecordHold` (Verbose on kind/detail change only) at four orchestrator sites: the loop-path BLOCKED branch (zero new computation - reuses the eligibility verdict), `ApplyWait` (now takes `currentUT`; kind via the pure `RouteOrchestrator.HoldKindForOutcome` map), `ApplyEndpointLost`, and `ApplyDelivery`'s endpoint-lost-at-delivery branch.
- **Clear semantics:** `Route.ClearHold` on an eligible loop crossing (placed BEFORE `EmitLoopCycle` so the endpoint-lost-at-delivery hold recorded INSIDE that call survives - plan-review BLOCKER 1, pinned by `EndpointLostAtDelivery_HoldSurvivesEligibleCrossing`), on legacy `ApplyDispatch`, and on player Activate only (`TryActivate`; Pause deliberately keeps the hold so it answers "why wasn't this delivering"). Persisted across save/load; pre-M6 saves load the None/null/0/-1 defaults.
- **Display:** new pure `LogisticsHoldPresentation` (`DescribeHold` total over loop bare tokens + legacy prefixed tokens + an unknown-kind/token fallback that never blanks; `FormatHoldDetailLine` appends the mandatory "checked {age} ago" suffix) feeds a yellow detail-panel line plus the status-cell tooltip, built as `HoldText`/`HoldShort` in the ~1 Hz legibility cache (draw path reads only; detail line conditions ONLY on the cached `HoldText` for IMGUI control-count stability). Display gate (plan-review MAJOR 2): `MissingSourceRecording`/`SourceChanged` rows suppress the still-persisted hold. Accepted degradation: legacy-path funds holds render the generic no-number text (the shortfall lives only inside the legacy `funds-shortfall-N` token, deliberately not parsed; the legacy path is dead for v0 loop routes).

Test delta: +32 xUnit cases (14988 -> 15020 local, all green).

## Done 2026-06-12 - ReStock / ReStock+ support: patch-authored ghost FX recovery + RS+ showcases (branch `restock-ghost-fx`)

ONE feature covers both mods. ReStock core re-models stock parts and writes a FRESH full EFFECTS per covered engine/RCS part (MODEL_MULTI_PARTICLE -> `ReStock/FX` models + PREFAB_PARTICLE `fx_smokeTrail_light`); alone, the normal post-MM scan reads it and ghosts work. Under Waterfall config packs (SWE base configs are NOT ReStock-gated and `!EFFECTS {}` on top of ReStock; the 8-engine `WaterfallRestock_overrides` folder re-kills the rest of the way) the existing pristine-disk recovery restored the STOCK look on ReStock-modeled parts. ReStock+ adds NEW parts whose own cfgs carry full EFFECTS referencing core FX models: normal scan alone, zero SWE coverage (no ModuleWaterfallFX, gate never opens), pristine-disk recovery as the safety net if a pack ever patches them; RS+ needed zero new FX code.

**Fix:** `ReStockPatchFxIndex` parses ReStock's MM patch FILES on disk (`GameData/ReStock/Patches/**/*.cfg`; MM strips patch nodes from GameDatabase post-patch) into a lazy per-session index: decorated `@PART[x]:HAS[~RestockIgnore[*]]:FOR[000_ReStock]` node names are matched by prefix, the target token is between the FIRST `[` and `]` (wildcard check on the TOKEN only; the `:HAS` suffix wildcard would otherwise skip 100% of patches), fresh `EFFECTS` matched by EXACT name (never the `!EFFECTS` delete node), per-ordinal engine effect names read through MM value prefixes (`%`/`@`/`&` accepted, `!`/`-`/`#` skipped), absent directory = permanently empty index (the stock-install no-op guarantee). Recovery pre-stages: engine empty-scan (`TryApplyPristineEngineFxFallback`) and SWE-remnant replacement (`TryReplaceSweRemnantsWithPristine`) try the ReStock-authored EFFECTS BEFORE the stock pristine definitions; RCS fallback same. Group filter chain per engine-module ordinal: patch-authored names -> pristine per-ordinal names (RAPIER authors EFFECTS but no module nodes; verified stock names `power_open`/`running_open`/`running_closed` match ReStock's fresh groups exactly) -> all-groups for single-module parts -> skip for multi-module (anti-bleed). **Stock tuning standdown:** the hardcoded per-part FX tunings (Ant/Spider, Kickback, Puff, Rhino, heavy white-flame, Vector, RAPIER forcing, LES skip) all target ReStock-covered parts and would stomp the correct ReStock look even WITHOUT Waterfall; they now stand down on `HasAuthoredEffectsFor(part)` (ReStock presence, not the Waterfall gate), each with a rate-limited standdown log line.

**Known limitations (accepted):** RestockIgnore'd parts keep stock models but the index still reports ReStock-authored EFFECTS, so their ghosts get ReStock-style plumes AND the tunings stand down (rare, cosmetic, diagnosable from the standdown log lines). Wildcard `@PART` targets are skipped (none exist in ReStock). Other model-replacing mods with the same kill pattern are out of scope (directory-specific stage). Per-part FX size boosts still apply (uniform across configs).

**Showroom:** install-conditional ReStock+ showcases (36 rows: 17 engines incl. the Soyuz tank motors, 12 RCS blocks, 3 deployable antennas, service bay, 3 fairing bases) on a dedicated line band 60 m behind the stock lines (extending stock row indices would wrap RS+ rows onto stock rows' latitudes via `ShowcaseEntriesPerLine`; `ShowcaseRowCount` untouched). `InjectAllRecordings` includes them only when `GameData/ReStockPlus` exists in the target install (probe override seam for tests). Remaining RS+ categories (wheels, science/airlock/claw animations, decouplers, color changers) deliberately not showcased yet, same coverage rule as stock (parts with showcase-able behaviors).

**Validation:** +41 xUnit cases (index parsing fixtures verbatim from real patch shapes incl. the `:HAS` wildcard suffix, merge rules, filter chains, scanner composition, showcase well-formedness/band placement/probe seam; 15143 green, the only full-suite failure is the known environmental `InjectAllRecordings` skip-on-live-KSP). New `ReStockCompat` in-game category (skip-gated on ReStock and Waterfall presence): index content, ReStock-alone non-empty scan contract, Swivel + RCS recovery yields `ReStock/FX` models, RAPIER both-ordinal distinct groups, standdown engages for all covered tuned parts, `AllReStockPatchFxResolveExactly` sweep. POST-CKAN (user): WaterfallCompat + ReStockCompat in the four configs, fingerprint A/B (baseline = ReStock WITHOUT Waterfall vs WITH; target zero divergences like the proven stock-vs-Waterfall A/B), showroom playtest (ReStock plumes on Swivel/Mainsail/Rhino/Kickback ghosts, RCS puffs, RS+ rows, LES standdown particle density).

**ReStock-alone playtest round 1 (2026-06-12, `../logs/2026-06-12_2020_restock-alone-validation/`):** index built clean (64 files, 244 part nodes, 40 EFFECTS-bearing, zero failures/conflicts), all 12 standdowns fired incl. LES (user: LES FX now visible and OK), all runnable ReStockCompat tests PASSED, RS+ rows injected. ONE real bug: **SRB ghost smoke gathered at a single point instead of flowing** (user report). Root cause via .mu decode + Assembly-CSharp decompile: ReStock's `restock-fx-srb-smoke-1/2/3` are world-space TRAIL assets whose plume look comes from the EMITTER (flying vessel) moving away from emitted particles; baked particle velocity is 0-1 m/s (smoke-3 exactly zero), and in modern KSP `damping`/`emitterVelocityScale` are dead fields while the cfg `speed` curve maxes at 1.0, so a STATIC showcase ghost pools every particle at the nozzle. Flame cores bake -13..-17 m/s, hence flames looked right. Fix: `GhostVisualBuilder.TryComputeWorldSpaceEmitterVelocityFloor` gives cloned world-space emitters below 4 m/s a 6 m/s exhaust-ward flow at ghost build time (applied in `ProcessEngineModelFxEntries` after `StripKspFxControllers`). Provably a no-op on non-ReStock installs: a scan of all 252 Squad/SquadExpansion/ReStock/ReStockPlus `.mu` assets found ZERO stock world-space emitters (only ReStock's 3 srb-smoke models + 4 drill FX outside the engine path). Accepted deviation: moving ghosts' smoke columns drift a few m/s exhaust-ward on top of the motion-painted trail. Floor speed is a single constant (`WorldSpaceEmitterFloorSpeed`), tunable on playtest feedback. **Round-2 playtest correction:** the first cut aimed the floor along the ASSET's authored axis (else -Y), which squirted sideways on Clydesdale/Thoroughbred because ReStock orients `fxTransformSmoke` differently per SRB rig (all three smoke .mu transforms are identity; the rig rotation differs). The floor now follows the ENGINE'S EXHAUST AXIS (first thrust transform's forward, the same thrust-anchor-local lesson as commit 99dc81798) converted into the emitter's local frame (undoing the cfg localRotation and the FX transform's prefab-space rotation).

**Round-3 playtest (smoke orientation CONFIRMED fixed; three new findings, all fixed, `../logs/2026-06-12_2139_restock-round3/`):**
- **Jets rendered NO FX under ReStock-alone**: their only running visual is PREFAB `fx_smokeTrail_light`, and ReStock deletes the legacy `fx_*` keys on every covered engine, emptying the legacy donor cache install-wide; `prefab not found` hit 19 parts (jets totally dark; ReStock-authored liquids silently lost their smoke trails; the v1 deprecated engines too). The builtin `Effects/{name}` resolution existed for exactly this but was Waterfall-gated. Fix: `ShouldProbeBuiltinEffectsOnPrefabMiss` = Waterfall-part OR `ReStockPatchFxIndex.IsReStockInstalled()`; stock installs unchanged (donor cache resolves there, gate stays closed). NOTE: the `AllReStockPatchFxResolveExactly` sweep had used builtin-inclusive resolution while the runtime path did not, which is why it passed while jets were dark; runtime and sweep now use the same gate.
- **Mite/Shrimp ghost smoke oversized vs Flea/Hammer**: they got the default 1.5x ghost size boost while Flea/Hammer are pinned 1.0x. Live KSP never scales model-particle size with power (`ModelMultiParticleFX.OnEvent` scales emission/lifetime/velocity only), so the faithful boost for ReStock-authored model FX is 1.0 everywhere: `ResolveModelFxSizeBoost(restockAuthored) = 1.0` (also stops the stock-tuned Rhino 2.7x / Mainsail 2.0x overrides from inflating ReStock plumes). Live ReStock uses the SAME smoke asset at the same size for all SRB classes, so Mite == Flea is the install-faithful look.
- **Mammoth (and friends) showed a rising "vapor" column**: that is its authored `fx_smokeTrail_veryLarge` aimed straight UP by the stock parent-up rotation heuristic, which mis-aims on ReStock's smokePoint rigs. Fix: `TryComputeExhaustAimedPrefabRotation` aims the prefab emission axis (+Y) along the exhaust axis (parent-local) for ReStock-authored parts without a cfg localRotation; managed from-to-rotation implementation (`Quaternion.FromToRotation` is a native ECall, untestable in xUnit). Stock rigs keep the existing heuristic byte-identically.
- Thoroughbred "no smoke" report: the log shows Thoroughbred and Clydesdale built byte-identical smoke (same asset, same floor vector along the thrust axis); no part-specific defect found. Re-check in round 4 (the newly-resolving smoke trails change the SRB picture anyway).

**Round-4 playtest (jets confirmed fixed; smoke-trail ORIENTATION still wrong on several parts; observability escalated, `../logs/2026-06-12_2206_restock-round4/`):** the newly-resolving white smoke trails flow UP on several engines (LES at ~45 degrees), and some dark smoke trails still rise. KEY LOG FINDING that killed the axis-assumption approach: EVERY smokeTrail prefab instance logs its +Y axis pointing world-UP (angleFromDown=180), on the correct-looking jets AND the wrong-looking engines alike, so instance +Y is NOT the emission direction and neither the stock parent-up heuristic nor the round-3 exhaust-aim can be validated from transform axes at all (the #242 dir lines cannot discriminate good from bad). New tool: `GhostFxEmissionProbe`, a one-shot component attached to every cloned ghost engine FX instance that samples LIVE particles after the FX starts and logs the MEASURED mean particle velocity direction (`[FxEmissionProbe] measured: part=... meanDirWorld=... angleFromDown=...`), mechanism-agnostic (KSPParticleEmitter EmitParams and shuriken self-emission alike), once per part-midx-fx per scene session, with a timeout line for never-emitting instances. Showroom fixtures stand upright, so angleFromDown ~0 = correct downward flow and ~180 = the bug; one showroom pass + grep names every misaimed part with measured data. NEXT: collect a round-5 log, list offenders from the probe lines, and fix orientation from measured reality (the round-3 exhaust-aim stays in place until the probe data says what is actually right).

**Round-6 (LES smoke, `../logs/2026-06-12_2251_restock-round6-les/`):** orientation confirmed good everywhere except the stock LaunchEscapeSystem: its single white smoke jet flowed at ~31 deg (the user read it as "only one of the 3 nozzles works"). Probe + rig dump + decompile closed it: the ReStock LES rig has ONE fxSmoke whose -Y is authored straight down the stack (a central smoke column) while its single escape thrustTransform is deliberately canted ~30 deg (Apollo-style asymmetric escape burn; the canted flame core and the up-and-out pitch wisp are authored looks). The live contract (decompiled `PrefabParticleFX`) parents prefab FX with IDENTITY local rotation (cfg localRotation is an angle-axis Vector4), and `SmokeTrailControl` (decompiled) is pure altitude alpha-fade, no steering. Round-6 parentUpWorld data across all 36 smoke-trail rigs shows a clean bimodal split: transform -Y within ~1 deg of exhaust-down (trust the rig) or ~90/180 deg off (smokePoint-style rigs that need the aim, user-validated in rounds 5-6). Fix: `PrefabRigTrustAngleDegrees = 45` in `TryComputeExhaustAimedPrefabRotation`: when the FX transform's -Y is within 45 deg of the exhaust axis, identity (live contract; LES becomes a straight central column), else aim -Y onto the exhaust axis. Also noted: the v1 deprecated `liquidEngine` smoke measures ~92 deg off (stock part, not ReStock-authored, pre-existing heuristic path); cosmetic, deprecated, left alone.

**Round-7 (depth-mask see-through holes + orphan smoke localization):** the "blueish missing texture" under the ReStock claws and at the jet exhaust interiors is ReStock's DEPTH MASKS: `ModuleRestockDepthMask` (33 uses across 10 patch files: claws, jets, intakes, antennas, RCS, solar panels, science, ladders) adds depth-only mask meshes at render queue ~1999 that the live plugin manages; cloned onto a ghost they occlude everything behind them, punching a see-through hole showing the sky/ocean (the blue). Fix: the ghost renderer clone loop skips depth-mask renderers, detected by (a) config `maskTransform` names from any MODULE whose name contains "DepthMask" (covers the community ModuleDepthMask pattern too) and (b) depth-mask shader names on the prefab material; counter in the clone summary line. Cost: the interior seam the mask hid is visible on ghosts (minor, vs a hole). Stock installs hit neither branch. ALSO: the "dark smoke trail suspended in air near the pad" report round 1 attribution (Flea Flight ascent trail) did not match the user's localization (fixed spot toward the runway, toggling with FX cadence, no part above); the emission probe now also logs `posWorld` + `root`/`rootRenderers` (enabled mesh renderers under the FX's ghost root; 0 = orphan FX with no visible part) so the next showroom pass names it mechanically.

**Round-8 (the suspended dark smoke NAMED and fixed, `../logs/2026-06-12_2350_restock-round8-twinboar/`):** the new probe posWorld fields measured the Twin-Boar's `fx_smokeTrail_veryLarge` instance 199 m from its own flame models (same ghost root, samples 0.3 s apart so no origin-shift artifact; `rootRenderers=16` so the part itself was visible, just 200 m away, matching the user's "no part above it"). Root cause is the RIG, not the mirror: ReStock's twinboar .mu mounts `smokePoint` at scale (20,20,20) under further-scaled ancestors, placing the mount ~200 m exhaust-ward of the part. On a live ascending booster that is the authored launch-smoke column far below the rocket; on a static rotated showcase fixture it becomes a horizontal orphan column. Ghost mirroring reproduced the prefab geometry exactly (all parent-align deltas 0.000). Fix: `IsFarFxMount` (threshold 25 m, uncritical: no other rig in the install mounts FX beyond a few meters) re-anchors prefab FX instances from far mounts to the engine's first thrust transform, where the trust-angle/aim logic then orients them exhaust-ward. Stock rigs never trip the threshold. **Round-9 correction:** the re-anchor silently no-oped: prefab ModuleEngines carry an EMPTY thrustTransforms list (populated at part start, not on prefabs), and the first cut iterated only that list, with the skip unlogged (a logging-requirements violation that cost a round trip). The exhaust ANCHOR resolution now shares the same chain as the direction resolver (thrustTransforms, else thrustVectorTransformName lookup), and both the re-anchor and the no-anchor skip are logged. **Round-11 (the actual mechanism, measured):** per-instance placement forensics gave the answer in one line: `Size2LFB.v2 mountDistPrefab=5 ghostInstDist=200 srcLossyScale=200.0`. The Twin-Boar smokePoint sits 5 m from the part (why the mount-position detector never fired) but carries lossyScale 200 from stacked rig scales, so the cfg `localOffset = 0,0,1` lands the instance 200 m out (live PrefabParticleFX applies the same raw localPosition, so the live column genuinely sits 200 m exhaust-ward). The far-mount detector now measures the EFFECTIVE placement point, `srcFxTransform.TransformPoint(localOffset)`, which includes the scale; every other rig measures 0-10 m and is untouched. **CONFIRMED FIXED in-game (round 12, user-verified): Twin-Boar smoke pours from its own nozzles; no orphan column.** All visuals from the ReStock-alone playtest campaign are now closed (orientation, sizes, jets, depth masks, LES, Twin-Boar). **STOCK PARITY PROVEN (2026-06-13, `../logs/2026-06-13_0028_stock-parity-check/`):** with ReStock + ReStock+ uninstalled and the showcase re-injected (RS+ rows correctly dropped to 0 by the install-conditional generator, 241 stock rows), the session's `[FxFingerprint]` lines diff against the pre-ReStock stock baseline (`../logs/2026-06-12_1745_waterfall-runB-stock/`) with ZERO divergences across all 55 FX-bearing parts (offline canonicalization applied to the baseline's pre-canonicalization format: suffix strip + Euler-to-emission-direction, same procedure as the Waterfall parity proof). Every change on this branch (index, standdowns, builtin probing, size boosts, smoke aims, velocity floor, depth masks, far-mount re-anchor) is mechanically invisible on a stock install. User also visually confirmed stock looks normal.

**Final hardening re-review (clean-context, 2026-06-13):** focused on the 12 post-review playtest commits. Verdict: math and probe lifecycle merge-ready; findings actioned: (M1) the depth-mask SHADER branch could in principle fire on module-less stock parts (the fingerprint A/B cannot see mesh-clone counts); empirically zero depth-mask skips across all 243 stock showroom parts in the stock-parity log, AND the branch is now gated structurally: the shader check is consulted only when the part carries a DepthMask module, so module-less parts are never skipped by construction. (m1) the SkinnedMeshRenderer clone path now applies the same depth-mask filter (was MeshRenderer-only). (m2) InvariantCulture on the forensics line floats. (m3) probe doc corrected: loggedKeys is once per PROCESS, not per scene session (deliberate, cheap). (m4) return after Destroy in probe Start. (m5) probe sampling list hoisted to a reused field (the probe is a permanent regression guard, not a temp diagnostic).

**FINAL VALIDATION (2026-06-13, `../logs/2026-06-13_0110_restock-waterfall-final/`, user-confirmed visuals):** with the multi-root index fix deployed, the fingerprint A/B vs the ReStock-alone baseline reads 85/85 parts, full parity; the only 12 deltas are size=1.50 -> 1.00 on the MH/legacy parts (same models, transforms, counts, directions), which is the size-fidelity rule CORRECTLY engaging now that those parts are index-covered (the older baseline carried the stock 1.5x boost on them, the same inconsistency class as the Mite/Shrimp report, never noticed on MH engines; a fresh ReStock-alone run would match the new leg exactly). Index: 87 files across Patches + PatchesMH + PatchesLegacy, 57 EFFECTS-bearing parts, zero failures/conflicts. 29 live recoveries served from ReStock-authored EFFECTS under the Waterfall kill. Zero errors / NREs; warns are the known ledger-guard, frame-budget, and post-inject synthetic-tree-sidecar patterns (byte-similar counts in the first ReStock-alone session). The full configuration matrix is now validated: stock (mechanical parity proof), ReStock-alone (12 rounds), ReStock + RS+ + Waterfall + SWE + WaterfallRestock + RestockWaterfallExpansion (this run).

**First ReStock+Waterfall config run (2026-06-13, ReStock + RS+ + Waterfall + SWE + WaterfallRestock + RestockWaterfallExpansion, `../logs/2026-06-13_0058_restock-waterfall-config/`):** the recovery path ran in-game for the first time. Fingerprint A/B vs the ReStock-alone round-12 baseline: 85/85 parts present, 76 byte-identical, NINE divergent, and all nine are Making History or v1-deprecated engines (no flames / stock-look recovery; the user-visible no-flame engines and the oversized Mastodon verniers). Root cause: ReStock ships THREE patch roots (Patches, PatchesMH, PatchesLegacy) and the index scanned only Patches/, so MH + legacy engines were invisible to recovery and fell back to stock pristine. Fix: the index enumerates every `GameData/ReStock/Patches*` root. Also: `SwivelPristineFallbackRecoversLegacyFx` was a STALE test (donor-cache-only resolution; the runtime has been builtin-Effects-inclusive since #1128 and the donor cache is empty under ReStock) and now mirrors the runtime chain. In-game results otherwise: ReStockCompat 8/8 passed (1 correct skip), WaterfallCompat parity sweep passed. RS+ engine rows came out byte-identical to ReStock-alone.

**Round-5 probe data (168 instances measured, `../logs/2026-06-12_2241_restock-round5-probe/`):** two frame lessons + one one-line fix. (1) `Vector3.down` is MEANINGLESS as a reference in the flight scene (KSP world Y is the planet's rotation axis, not local up); the analysis reference must be derived from measured-good instances (the 59 fast flame cores all agreed on one world direction = true exhaust-down). (2) Against that reference, 150/168 instances measured correct; the offenders were EXACTLY the smoke trails the round-3 exhaust-aim touched (177-180 deg inverted, every single one), while every heuristic-path smoke trail was correct: **smokeTrail prefabs emit along local MINUS-Y, not +Y**. Fix: `TryComputeExhaustAimedPrefabRotation` maps -Y (not +Y) onto the exhaust axis. The remaining 30-90 deg entries are authored looks (LES angled nozzles, separation motors firing sideways, turbopump vent wisps) and were left alone. `GhostFxEmissionProbe` stays in permanently as the regression guard; the analysis recipe (derive the reference from fast flame cores, then rank by angle) lives in this entry.

## Done 2026-06-11 - Waterfall support: pristine-config ghost FX fallback (branch `waterfall-ghost-fx`)

With Waterfall + Stock Waterfall Effects (SWE) installed, every SWE-patched engine and RCS part lost its ghost plume: SWE deletes the stock EFFECTS node (`!EFFECTS {}`), deletes the legacy top-level `fx_*` keys, and rewrites the module effect names to point at new audio-only groups, so the ghost FX build (post-MM `partInfo.partConfig` scan -> legacy `fx_*` prefab children -> give up) found nothing. Confirmed in-game 2026-06-11 (`../logs/2026-06-11_1925_waterfall-baseline/`: Swivel/Poodle/Mainsail all `filtered 4 EFFECTS groups to 1` + `no legacy fx_* children found`, zero FX clones in the session; live vessel Waterfall plumes fine, ghost audio fine via `GhostAudioPresets`).

**Fix:** `PristinePartFxResolver` recovers the part's ORIGINAL effect definitions from the pristine on-disk .cfg (ModuleManager patches in memory only), keyed per runtime part name with a session cache; `WaterfallCompat` gates the fallback per part on the prefab carrying `ModuleWaterfallFX` (name check, no compile-time Waterfall reference), so stock installs are behavior-identical. Engine side: pristine EFFECTS groups filtered by the PRISTINE module's effect names per engine-module ordinal (multi-mode safe, runs for midx > 0 too; ordinal mismatch skips recovery rather than scanning all groups), legacy `fx_*` keys synthesized as PREFAB_PARTICLE-style entries at the thrust transform with `engine.fxOffset` (midx 0; `fx_exhaustLight_*` filtered), best-effort `fx_exhaustFlame_white` last resort (skipped for secondary modules of legacy-keyed parts). Legacy names resolve through a candidate CASCADE (exact, then size-suffix-stripped: `fx_exhaustFlame_blue_small` -> `fx_exhaustFlame_blue`, `fx_exhaustFlame_yellow_medium` -> `fx_exhaustFlame_yellow` which survives on SWE-unpatched SRBs), duplicate resolved names dedupe to one instance, and a FLAME GUARANTEE adds the white flame whenever a flame was wanted but none resolved (first validation playtest 2026-06-11, `../logs/2026-06-11_2017_waterfall-validation/`: Poodle/Mainsail ghosts had smoke but no flame because the exact size-suffixed flame prefabs lost all donor parts under SWE while smoke resolved, so neither the synth nor the zero-entries last resort caught it). RCS side: pristine running-group MODEL_MULTI_PARTICLE recovery by RCS-module ordinal. IMPORTANT shape fact from review: stock Swivel/Poodle/Mainsail are LEGACY parts (plain ModuleEngines + `fx_*` keys, NO pristine EFFECTS node), so the legacy-synthesis path is the MAIN path for them; Spark/RAPIER-class parts use the pristine-EFFECTS path.

**Known limitations (accepted):** RealPlume/SmokeScreen-style packs kill stock particles WITHOUT adding ModuleWaterfallFX, so the gate stays closed and ghosts go dark (out of scope; this feature is Waterfall support). ~~ReStock blocks Squad/FX model loading~~ (CORRECTED 2026-06-12: `Restock.restockblacklist` lists only `Squad/Parts` model/texture assets, zero `Squad/FX` entries, so `GetModelPrefab("Squad/FX/...")` keeps working under ReStock; the real ReStock+Waterfall problem was pristine recovery restoring the STOCK look instead of ReStock's, solved by the ReStock support entry above). MM-generated clone parts (`+PART`) have no pristine disk node (same degradation). The white-flame last resort itself is best effort: the prefab cache is fed by legacy `fx_*` keys surviving on unpatched parts (stock carriers are two Making History SRBs); the `WaterfallCompat` in-game test asserts resolvability post-install.

**Validation:** xUnit fixtures shaped like real SWE patch output (+~30 cases) + `WaterfallCompat` in-game test category (Waterfall-dependent tests skip cleanly on stock installs; the gate-closed contract and builtin-variant tests run in stock; the 4 then-runnable tests PASSED on the Waterfall+SWE install 2026-06-11, before the category grew to 6). In-game showroom validation PASSED 2026-06-11 (`../logs/2026-06-11_2042_waterfall-showroom/`): 35 distinct engine recoveries with zero unresolvable names and zero flame fallbacks, Panther both modes + RAPIER closed cycle recovered, RCS on 7 part types incl. pod built-ins, user confirmed visuals. The 3 `prefab not found` supplements (Rhino/Puff/Vector hardcoded size-suffixed names) were fixed by routing the prefab-resolution site through the same cascade.

**Post-validation regression (user-observed, branch `waterfall-flame-variants`):** the cascade's family-base substitution changed flame CLASS, not just size: `fx_exhaustFlame_yellow` (the substitute for Mainsail's `yellow_medium`/`yellow_mini`) IS the big billowy SRB flame asset, its only surviving SWE donors being Thumper/Hammer/Flea, so Mainsail ghosts wore an SRB plume (and the dedupe collapsed both verniers into it). Also affected: Rhino (supplement yellow_medium), Poodle/Terrier/Thud (oversized blue for blue_small), Bobcat (blue_medium), Vector (double-stacked blue), Puff. ROOT FIX (investigation 2026-06-11): KSP's part compiler loads legacy fx prefabs from the builtin Resources path `Effects/{name}` which ModuleManager cannot delete, and Parsek's `FindFxPrefab` never probed it. `GhostVisualBuilder.FindFxPrefabIncludingBuiltinEffects` now probes `Effects/{name}` (with ParticleSystem check + cache insert) at the two Waterfall-gated sites ONLY (legacy synthesis candidates + ProcessEnginePrefabFxEntries cascade), so exact variants win and the cascade/white-flame become true last resorts. Do NOT add `Effects/` to the shared `TryResolveFxPrefabExact` probe list: stock paths rely on `fxPrefabFallbacks` deliberate substitutions (smokeTrail orientation). Summary line gains `builtinResolved=N` (expected: Mainsail substituted=0 builtinResolved>0). Bonus: removes the fragility where all liquid blue flames + light smoke resolved only because SWE's Skiff/Wolfhound configs forgot their `!fx_*` deletes.

**Parity-certainty tooling (same branch):** "are ghost FX identical stock vs Waterfall?" is answered on three tiers. (1) Code: decompile-verified asset identity + placement math (review of this branch). (2) Automated: in-game `AllEnginesPristineFxResolveExactly` sweeps EVERY Waterfall-patched engine and asserts every pristine legacy name / EFFECTS prefab resolves EXACTLY and every EFFECTS model is loaded; any miss means a cascade substitution or white flame would alter the look, so this fails on the whole class of the Mainsail bug, on future SWE donor changes, and on orphaned variants. (3) Mechanical A/B: `GhostFxFingerprint` logs a canonical per-part FX fingerprint (`[FxFingerprint]` lines: sorted asset<parent pos/rot/scale/size/speed tuples + curve key counts) after every ghost FX build in BOTH stock and Waterfall installs; procedure = run the showcase save once with the config pack disabled in CKAN and once enabled, extract+sort -u the fingerprint lines from both KSP.logs, diff; any non-identical line per part is a divergence finding. **A/B RESULTS (2026-06-12, `../logs/2026-06-12_1739_waterfall-runA/` vs `../logs/2026-06-12_1745_waterfall-runB-stock/`):** 55 parts on both sides, none missing; after canonicalization exactly TWO real divergences, both fixed on this branch: (1) Mainsail 3 vs 4 systems (dedupe collapsed the duplicate yellow_mini vernier keys; fix = preserve duplicate pristine keys + collapse only SUBSTITUTED duplicates in the synth loop), (2) RAPIER airbreathing midx=0 2 vs 5 systems (SWE leaves the aerospike spool smoke behind, the nonzero scan blocked pristine recovery, ghost got white-flame supplement + smoke at z=7 instead of stock shockExhaust_red_small models + smoke at z=1; fix = `TryReplaceSweRemnantsWithPristine`, gate-open + scan-nonzero now prefers the full pristine EFFECTS when it yields particles). The other 12 diffs were fingerprint artifacts, eliminated by canonicalization: strip ALL `(Clone)`/`(Keep Pos)` suffix repeats, and capture orientation as the EMISSION DIRECTION (local +Y image) instead of raw Euler (stock vs fallback rotations differ only by roll about the plume axis, invisible for axially symmetric FX). Canonicalization verified OFFLINE by re-diffing the same two logs with the new rules: 12 artifact diffs vanish, exactly the 2 real ones remain. FINAL RE-RUN (2026-06-12, `../logs/2026-06-12_1800_waterfall-runA2-parity/`): **ZERO divergences across all 55 parts** (RAPIER remnant replacement confirmed in-log; Mainsail at stock multiplicity); stock-vs-Waterfall ghost FX parity is mechanically PROVEN, plus user visual confirmation. The fingerprint tooling + parity sweep stay in place as permanent regression guards (rerun the A/B after any SWE/Waterfall update or FX-path change).

## Done 2026-06-11 - dotnet test clobbered the deployed KSP DLL from every worktree (branch `fix-test-deploy-clobber`)

The `CopyToGameData` post-build target ran `AfterTargets="Build"` unconditionally, so `dotnet test` in ANY worktree (which builds Parsek as a ProjectReference) deployed that branch's DLL to the shared `Kerbal Space Program/GameData/Parsek/Plugins`. With several sessions active, the deployed DLL belonged to whoever ran tests last; during the 2026-06-11 Waterfall validation the install was clobbered twice within minutes of an intentional deploy, and one KSP launch picked up the wrong branch 48 seconds after a sibling's build.

**Fix:** deploy is now intentional-only via a `ParsekDeployToKsp` property: true only when `$(MSBuildStartupDirectory) == $(MSBuildProjectDirectory)` (the documented `cd Source/Parsek && dotnet build` flow) or `-p:ForceKspDeploy=true`; `-p:SkipKspDeploy=true` suppresses it. Skipped builds print `KSP deploy skipped` so the absence of a deploy is visible. `dotnet test`, repo-root builds, and `release.py` (which packages from `bin/Release`, never from the install) no longer touch the install. Sibling worktrees keep clobbering until they rebase past this commit.

## Done 2026-06-11 - In-game OrbitArcSampler test asserted orbital distance from the floating origin, not the body centre (branch `fix-orbitarc-test-frame`)

`GhostMapPresenceTests.OrbitArcSampler_ClipsLiveOrbitToOpenArc` failed in the 2026-06-11 Run All + Isolated session (`../logs/2026-06-11_1811_m1-ingame-tests/`, "sampled points sit at orbital distance from the body centre (world-frame)") with the active vessel "Jumping Flea" PRELAUNCH on the pad. Root cause is in the TEST, not the sampler: `OrbitArcSampler.SampleSegmentArc` returns WORLD-frame points (`referenceBody.position + relative`), but the assertion checked `buffer[0].magnitude > body.Radius * 0.5` - the distance from the FLOATING ORIGIN, which rides the active vessel. The synthetic orbit's periapsis (720 km from Kerbin's centre, along the Planetarium reference direction in the equatorial plane) passes within ~120 km of a launchpad origin whenever KSC's rotational longitude lines up with the reference direction, so the check failed or passed depending on planet rotation / vessel position. The forward-render review's NIT-6 fixed the sampler doc + assertion message to say "world-frame" but left the origin-relative measurement in place.

**Fix:** the assertion now measures body-relative (`(point - body.position).magnitude`) and checks EVERY sample lies inside the orbit's radial band (periapsis*0.99 .. apoapsis*1.01), deterministic for any active vessel and any planet rotation, and a tighter check of the property the old floor intended (the two predicates are formally incomparable: the failing pad scenario passes the new check). Clean-context Fable review (ship-ready) follow-ups actioned: assert messages now carry the sample index, measured radius, and band/floor bounds (a bare constant string is what forced this forensic dig in the first place), and the hyperbolic block gained the body-relative periapsis floor it never had (350 km for the synthetic e=1.5 orbit; finiteness-only before). Sampler behaviour unchanged (every other assertion in the failing run passed: 180 finite samples, open arc, hyperbolic flagging, degenerate routing). Test-only change; verification is the next in-game test session.

## Done 2026-06-10 - Logistics M1: non-KSC origin debit, the network unlock (branch `logistics-m1-origin-debit`, 0.10.2-dev)

**Milestone M1 of the logistics roadmap shipped** (design `docs/parsek-logistics-supply-routes-design.md` 19.4 M1, which now carries per-item as-built notes; plan `docs/dev/plan-logistics-m1-origin-debit.md`). Six deliverables, one commit per phase:

1. **Physical origin debit:** `LiveOriginDebitWriters` + pure `RouteOriginDebitPlanner` drain the route's `CostManifest` from the live origin vessel at each loop dock crossing (loaded `PartResource.amount` / unloaded `ProtoPartResourceSnapshot` split, shared flow gate); the `RouteCargoDebited` row carries actual-debited manifest, requested-on-shortfall, and origin pid (additive codec). Direct write at emit time in `EmitDispatchDebit`, LOOP-PATH-ONLY (plan D11: legacy `ApplyDispatch` keeps v0 rows byte-identical); `RouteModule` stays observe-only (T-ROUTEMODULE-OBSERVE; the design doc's "applier through RouteModule" wording was corrected in 19.4/19.7). Test seam `OriginDebitApplierForTesting` returns an `OriginDebitOutcome` (plan D12; true-with-null-vessel resolution counts as unresolved).
2. **`OriginHasCargo` un-stub:** `LiveOriginCargoProbe` (stored deliverable amounts) + pure `RouteOriginCargoCheck.HasRequired` gate all-or-nothing against `CostManifest`, naming the first short resource ordinal-first; inventory-payload routes hold with `inventory-origin-debit-unsupported` (plan D6, deferred to M3).
3. **Origin endpoint descriptor capture:** `OriginPartnerCandidate` / `RouteOriginProof` carry the docked partner's body/coords/situation (excluded from the proof hash so existing routes stay stable); `RouteBuilder` builds a surface-typed origin endpoint reaching the destination-style proximity rebuild fallback.
4. **Undocked-start workflow rejection:** `RouteAnalysisStatus.UndockedStartOrigin` at analysis with workflow guidance text (start docked / record the mining / launch from KSC).
5. **Dispatch priority:** persisted sparse `Route.DispatchPriority` (lower first, floor 0), `CompareRoutesForTick` (priority, `NextDispatchUT`, ordinal id) on the tick snapshot, detail-panel stepper. Upgrade note: equal-priority routes in existing saves reorder from commit-list order to (stale, activation-era) `NextDispatchUT` order - deterministic and spec-mandated, only visible when several routes contend in one tick.
6. **Scenario-lifecycle harness (3-layer, plan D10):** codec round-trips + ordered source-text gates + in-game `LogisticsOriginDebitRuntimeTests` (loaded/unloaded debit through the production tick, empty-origin hold, save round-trip of the proto debit). See the RESOLVED scenario-gates entry below for detail.

**Test delta:** +63 xUnit cases (14898 -> 14961, all green) + 4 new isolated-run in-game tests. In-game validation of the new runtime tests is pending the next FLIGHT test session.

## Done 2026-06-09 - TS Fly canary never ran: SetVessel reflection probe used a nonexistent one-arg signature (branch `fix-ts-fly-canary-probe`)

The manual-only in-game canary `TrackingStationMaterializedOrbit_FlyLoadsMaterializedVessel_NotStaleSelection` (#554/#550) always skipped with "SpaceTracking selection/Fly reflection helpers are unavailable", confirmed in the 2026-06-09 isolated run (`../logs/2026-06-09_2319_pr1104-test-isolation/`). Decompiling KSP 1.12.5 `Assembly-CSharp.dll` (ilspycmd) showed the cause: stock `SpaceTracking.SetVessel` is `SetVessel(Vessel v, bool keepFocus)`; the test probed `GetMethod("SetVessel", ..., new[] { typeof(Vessel) }, ...)`, which has no match. `selectedVessel` and `BtnOnClick_FlySelectedVessel()` exist as probed.

**Fix:** the canary now resolves `SetVessel` through `GhostMapPresence.FindTrackingStationSetVesselMethod` (widened to `internal`; prefers the two-arg stock signature, falls back to one-arg) and builds invoke args via the already-tested `BuildTrackingStationSetVesselArguments`. The graceful skip is kept for genuinely missing members and now names which probe failed. Note: decompile shows `SetVessel` has a same-frame re-entry guard (`lastSetVesselFrame == Time.frameCount`); the canary's ghost-focus call is prefix-blocked (original body skipped), so the follow-up materialized-vessel call still passes the guard. Unit tests: 2 new direct resolver tests in `GhostTrackingStationPatchTests`. In-game verification: pending next Tracking Station test session (run Isolated; the canary is `AllowBatchExecution=false`).

## Done 2026-06-09 - Logistics Tier-1: Mission / Route structure-list window aka the Log window (0.10.1, PR #1107 / M-MIS-0)

**Feature (roadmap Phase 13 Tier-1, first bullet; now M-MIS-0):** a popup that lists a run step by step (launch, staging / separation, dock, undock, deliveries, terminal), each with its time, status (vessel situation), and location (always "SOI/body, biome" order), complementing the Missions-tab composition tree. One reusable window covers both a mission (Missions-tab "Log" button, first in the header group) and a supply route (Logistics route-detail "Log (Route)" + "Log (Mission)" buttons next to Rename; the latter opens the source mission's log).

**Implementation:** two pure, headless-tested builders feed a reusable IMGUI sub-window. `MissionStructureListBuilder.Build(tree, structure)` flattens the cached `MissionStructure` (root launches + branch-point dock/undock/decouple/eva/breakup events + terminal legs) and supplements it with debris-staging `PartEvents` (`Decoupled` / `FairingJettisoned` / `ShroudJettisoned`), de-duplicating a `Decoupled` event against a controlled Separation branch point by **decoupler part PID**, and cross-recording duplicates of one physical staging by (pid, eventType) with a **5s UT tolerance** (UT-tolerant, NOT UT-blind: a craft-baked PID re-staged hours later by a Re-Fly fork in the same tree is a distinct event and survives; recordings iterate in RecordingId order so the surviving representative is save/load-stable). Staging Status/biome honesty: the owning recording's start context is used only within 30s of the recording start, else Status blanks and Location keeps the segment-stable body only. A post-sort `CollapseSimultaneous` pass folds identical same-instant events (0.25s window, head-anchored) into one "xN" row (e.g. "Shroud jettisoned x4"), confirmed against collected logs (`logs/2026-06-09_2135_mission-log-dups`: staging=17/20 per mission from same-frame multi-shroud/decoupler separations). `RouteStructureListBuilder.Build(route, sourceLookup)` emits Origin -> Dock -> Delivery(per stop) -> Undock from `Route.Origin` / `IsKscOrigin` / `RecordedDockUT` / `Stops` plus the dock-member recording's `RouteConnectionWindow`; the source recording is resolved through an injected `Func<string,Recording>` so the builder stays free of the store singleton. `StructureListWindowUI` (owned by `ParsekUI`, drawn in KSC + Flight) renders a scrollable Time / Event / Status / Location / Vessel table (header reserves the scrollbar gutter so columns align with the scrolled rows) reusing the existing opaque-window + resize + input-lock scaffolding (`SpawnControlUI` pattern). Per-step location is the coarse body + biome / launch-site / terminal context; per-step coordinate resolution from `TrajectoryPoint`s is deferred.

**Notes:** read-only over already-recorded data, no capture / scheduler / serialization / route-model change, nothing runs per frame except the window draw while open. `StructureListWindowUI` is allowlisted in `scripts/ers-els-audit-allowlist.txt` for the by-id dock-member resolve (physical connection-window proof, not a visibility-scoped enumeration; same rationale as `MissionsWindowUI` / `TimelineWindowUI`). `MissionHeaderRightBlockWidth` bumped by one header-button width so the looped-period label still fits; the Logistics "Next" delivery column widened 90 -> 135.

**Files:** `Source/Parsek/MissionRouteStructureList.cs` (read model + both builders + location formatter + simultaneous-collapse), `Source/Parsek/UI/StructureListWindowUI.cs` (renderer), `Source/Parsek/InGameTests/StructureListRuntimeTests.cs`, `Source/Parsek.Tests/StructureListBuilderTests.cs` (14 cases), plus button wiring in `UI/MissionsWindowUI.cs` + `UI/LogisticsWindowUI.cs`, ownership in `ParsekUI.cs`, host draws in `ParsekFlight.cs` + `ParsekKSC.cs`. Plan: `docs/dev/plan-structure-list-window.md`.

## Done 2026-06-09 - Zero-drift per-window reschedule: same-parent (Mun / Minmus) verify-and-harden (branch `zero-drift-harden`, Phases A-C)

**Scope:** SAME-PARENT only (Kerbin -> Mun / Minmus, including land-and-return). The cross-parent "Duna-One-class" single-moon arrival hold is a different subsystem (re-aim, `UnsupportedCrossParent`) and is a separate sibling pass, not part of this work. The mechanism (`MissionPeriodicity` `NextJointNearCoincidenceUT` / `TryBuildRelaunchSchedule` / `MissionRelaunchSchedule`, attached in `MissionLoopUnitBuilder.TryBuildMissionUnit` and consumed by the shared `GhostPlaybackLogic` span clock across flight / KSC / Tracking Station) was already SHIPPED; this work lifted it to a flawless bar by closing the test-coverage / verification gaps, adding the missing self-defending guards, and fixing the stale docs.

**Done:** the same-parent zero-drift hardening (tests + span-clock guard + the R3 amber-tint fix that stops the launch-window status showing a false amber warning when the schedule is actually on target). Plan + per-phase breakdown: `docs/dev/plans/zero-drift-reschedule-hardening.md`; shipped spec: `docs/dev/done/plans/zero-drift-reschedule.md`.

**Carried forward (deferred to a follow-up):** the Phase D in-game VISUAL-parity tier (per-frame ghost activation, scheduled debris render, and three-scene visual parity) is NOT closed by this work and is deferred to a follow-up; Phases A-C shipped on branch `zero-drift-harden`. The two Tracking-Station playtest-pending lines below also remain open (they need a live playtest, not closed here).

## Done 2026-06-08 - Bug 1 (funds-economy-divergence): a stock contract re-fire baked N copies of the reward into the ledger

**Symptom (log-verified):** a single contract completion fired the stock award sequence 4 times within 22 ms (and a second contract 3 times), and Parsek recorded a `ContractCompleted` row per fire. Evidence: `logs/2026-06-08_2110_funds-bug/KSP.log`. `KSP.log:17201, 17227, 17250, 17271` (19:15:43.089-.111): four `Awarding 63250 funds to player for contract completion` STOCK lines for ONE contract (`1eb2baf9-afce-48c7-82d6-364dae85f57a`, "Science data from surface of The Mun"), live funds 305131 -> 494881. `KSP.log:17225, 17247, 17269, 17289` (`AddEvent: ContractCompleted ... total=33..36`): four store rows, same contractId / UT 475409.6 / recordingId tag. At commit those convert to four `ContractComplete` ledger rows (4 x 63250 = 253000).

**Root cause:** Parsek faithfully emits one `ContractCompleted` event per stock `Contract.onCompleted` fire (`GameStateRecorder.OnContractCompleted`, subscribed via `GameEvents.Contract.onCompleted`). Parsek never calls `Contract.Complete()` and no Parsek Harmony patch touches the award path, so the re-fire is STOCK / external re-entrancy (each repeat re-emits the full stock banner + a fresh stock `ContractOffered`); the precise stock trigger is NOT pinned (the log does not capture it). The carried resource events DID coalesce (`GameStateStore.AddEvent` collapses same-type/same-tag resource deltas within `ResourceCoalesceEpsilon = 0.1s`), but `ContractCompleted` is not a resource event so it was not coalesced; `GameStateEventConverter.ConvertEvents` had no intra-batch dedup and `DeduplicateAgainstLedger` only dedups candidates against the EXISTING ledger, so all four survived and `Ledger.AddActions` appended them blindly. The no-recorder direct path (`OnKscSpending`) was equally vulnerable.

**Fix (branch `fix-funds-economy-divergence`):** DEFENSIVE observation-time de-dup (no stock cause-fix; Parsek does not own the stock contract system). (1) **Recorder debounce (primary chokepoint).** New pure helper `GameStateRecorder.IsDuplicateContractCompletion(contractGuid, ut, lastSeenByGuid, window)` returns true (suppress) when the same guid completed within `window` (= `GameStateStore.ResourceCoalesceEpsilon`, 0.1s, now `internal const`), otherwise records `lastSeenByGuid[guid] = ut` and returns false. A static `lastContractCompletionUtByGuid` map mirrors the `PendingMilestoneEventById` precedent and is cleared via a new `ClearContractCompletionDedup(reason)` called from `Subscribe()`, `Unsubscribe()`, and `ResetForTesting()` (NO `onGameSceneSwitchRequested` hook), so a legitimate re-completion in a different session / timeline is not suppressed. `OnContractCompleted` calls the helper at the TOP and RETURNs before BOTH the `Emit` store write AND the `ShouldForwardDirectLedgerEvent -> OnKscSpending` direct forward, covering both inflation paths; a single Info "DEDUPED" line logs the drop. Scope is `ContractCompleted` only (the only observed re-fire / positive-reward inflation; ContractFailed/Cancelled left as a possible follow-up, not gold-plated). (2) **Converter belt-and-suspenders (§3.2a).** `GameStateEventConverter.ConvertEvents` now tracks converted contract-lifecycle actions by `(Type, ContractId, UT-bucket)` (bucket = floor(UT / `ResourceCoalesceEpsilon`)) within the batch and skips a duplicate, logging a summary count, so even a pre-existing burst already in the store cannot double-bake at the single commit chokepoint.

**Limitation:** recordings / ledgers already inflated by a past burst stay as-is (immutable, matches the no-modify-recordings rule); they are not repaired by this fix, and the original burst's extra payouts already hit live funds in real time (a separate, explicitly-authorized save repair if ever wanted). Bug 2's symmetric uplift clamp independently STOPS the inflated ledger from re-inflating live funds further on a future non-authoritative recalc (it caps a too-high target down to live), but it does NOT undo the past live inflation.

**Files:** `Source/Parsek/GameStateStore.cs` (`ResourceCoalesceEpsilon` promoted to `internal const` as the single source of truth), `Source/Parsek/GameStateRecorder.cs` (`IsDuplicateContractCompletion`, `lastContractCompletionUtByGuid`, `ClearContractCompletionDedup`, `OnContractCompleted` debounce, Subscribe/Unsubscribe/ResetForTesting clears), `Source/Parsek/GameActions/GameStateEventConverter.cs` (intra-batch contract-lifecycle dedup + summary log), `Source/Parsek.Tests/ContractCompletionDedupTests.cs` (`IsDuplicateContractCompletion_*`: first-seen / within-window / outside-window / different-guid / null-guid), `Source/Parsek.Tests/GameStateEventConverterTests.cs` (`ConvertEvents_DuplicateContractCompletedSameUt_ConvertsOnce` + distinct-contracts + far-apart re-completion). Plan: `docs/dev/plans/fix-funds-economy-divergence.md`.

## Done 2026-06-08 - Bug 2 (funds-economy-divergence): a plain scene change silently REFUNDED a facility-upgrade spend (asymmetric drawdown guard)

**Symptom (player-reported, log-verified):** the player upgraded a facility (live funds 517386 -> 66387), then a normal SPACECENTER -> EDITOR scene change refunded most of the spend. Evidence: `logs/2026-06-08_2110_funds-bug/KSP.log`. `KSP.log:164416` `FundsChanged -451000 (StructureConstruction) -> 66387`; `KSP.log:166417` `RecalculateAndPatch: drawdown-guard authoritativeReduction=False (rewinding=False, reFlyMarker=False, mergeJournal=False, tombstone=False, rewindResAdjust=False)` (no time-travel authority); `KSP.log:166422` `PatchFunds: 66386.5 -> 415466.3 (delta=349079.8, target=415466.3)` (the refund). The SAME recalc clamped reputation DOWN (`KSP.log:166423` `PatchReputation: GUARDED DRAWDOWN clamped ... clampedTo=71.61`), capturing the asymmetry in one frame.

**Root cause:** the "keep what you earned" drawdown guard (the entry below) was DOWNWARD-ONLY. `IsGuardableDrawdown(running, live, eps) = running < live - eps` fires only when the ledger running balance is BELOW live and `ApplyDrawdownGuard` floored the target UP to live. When the player spends on a facility, `GameStateEventConverter.ConvertEvent` returns null for `StructureConstruction` `FundsChanged` (only the two Bail-Out-Grant strategy reasons convert), so the spend is patched as a facility LEVEL change but never enters the funds ledger as a spending. The ledger funds model is therefore structurally `running > live` after any facility spend, and the asymmetric guard did nothing in that direction: `PatchFunds` applied the full upward delta and refunded the spend. `PatchScience` / `PatchReputation` share the same `ApplyDrawdownGuard` call shape and the same upward hole.

**Fix (branch `fix-funds-economy-divergence`):** made the no-authority guard SYMMETRIC on the same running-balance discriminator (NOT a blanket clamp-to-live, which would re-enable a legitimate reservation). New pure predicate `KspStatePatcher.IsGuardableUplift(running, live, eps) = running > live + eps` mirrors `IsGuardableDrawdown`. `ApplyDrawdownGuard` gained a 2-out overload `(out bool clamped, out ClampDirection direction)` (`enum ClampDirection { None, Up, Down }`); the existing 1-out signature is kept as a thin delegating wrapper so the existing `DrawdownGuardTests` call sites compile unchanged. Logic when `!authoritativeReduction`: `running < live - eps` -> clamp UP to `max(target, live)`, direction Up (UNCHANGED, incl. flagging clamped even when target>live); `running > live + eps` -> cap DOWN to `min(target, live)`, direction Down, flagging clamped ONLY when the value actually LOWERED (`min < target`) so a partial-reservation-on-top-of-a-leak no-op does not emit a misleading WARN/toast; otherwise unchanged (reservation: running at live, target below live -> written through). The authoritative path is untouched, so a genuine time-travel restore still moves funds either way. `EmitDrawdownGuardClamp` takes a `direction` and logs `GUARDED UPLIFT clamped ... spent value held` (vs `GUARDED DRAWDOWN clamped ... earned value preserved`); a dedicated `fundsUpliftClampToastShownThisSession` latch (+ science/rep analogs, reset in `ResetDrawdownGuardSessionLatches`) toasts "Held your funds at the spent value" once per session independently of the drawdown latch. All three `Patch*` sites pass `out direction` and branch the toast/latch on it. This bounds FUTURE non-authoritative recalcs; it does NOT claw back funds the original spend / a prior burst already applied live (immutable past).

**Safety invariant preserved (plan §2.5):** the DOWN clamp is correct only because two existing gates guarantee live is ground truth on every non-authoritative recalc: the patch-deferral gate (`LedgerOrchestrator.GetKspPatchDeferralReason` defers the patch entirely while a recording / uncommitted-or-pending tree is in flight, so stock earnings reach live in real time and never hit a clamp) and the cold-load deferred-seed wait (`PatchFunds` early-returns on `!HasSeed`). A future change that lets a commit-time recalc fire while the ledger genuinely LEADS live (an earning Parsek recorded that stock did NOT apply live) must re-evaluate this guard.

**Files:** `Source/Parsek/GameActions/KspStatePatcher.cs` (`IsGuardableUplift`, `ClampDirection`, `ApplyDrawdownGuard` 2-out overload + 1-out wrapper, `EmitDrawdownGuardClamp` direction wording, uplift latches), `Source/Parsek/InGameTests/RuntimeTests.cs` (`DrawdownGuard_RefundLeak_ClampedDownToLive`, `DrawdownGuard_ScienceRunningEqualsLive_NoSpuriousDownClamp`), `Source/Parsek.Tests/DrawdownGuardTests.cs` (`IsGuardableUplift_*`, `ApplyDrawdownGuard_RunningAboveLive_*`, `Reservation_RunningEqualsLive_TargetBelowLive_NoUpliftClamp`, science/rep down-clamp facts, `EmitDrawdownGuardClamp_Funds_Down_WarnsWithUpliftWordingAndToastsOnce`). Extends the downward-only "Recalc-patch drawdown guard" entry (2026-06-07) below to symmetric. Plan: `docs/dev/plans/fix-funds-economy-divergence.md`.

## Done - BUG-H (2026-06-07 vessels-disappearing): a stock Revert silently deleted the player's REAL landed/orbiting craft from unrelated missions

**Symptom (player-reported):** after a normal forward-play flight, hitting stock Revert (Esc -> Revert to Launch / Prelaunch, NOT a Parsek rewind) made several of the player's real, separately launched vessels vanish from the save. Evidence: `logs/2026-06-07_2312_vessels-disappearing/KSP.log`; the 21:49:46 Revert-to-Prelaunch (reverting the fresh mission `L4-B2-U1-S8`) logged `StripOrphanedSpawnedVessels: removed 7 vessel(s)` (`R3-B2-U1-S7` LANDED, `R2-B2-S5` ORBITING, `R.2-S.3`, `R.1-S.3`, `R.1-S.2` x2, `R.1-S.1` SPLASHED) - all real craft from unrelated prior missions. Pre-strip `saves/c1/persistent.sfs` had 8 vessels; the live save dropped to 3.

**Root cause (`persistentId` is craft-baked, NOT launch-unique - see CLAUDE.md):** on a stock Revert, `RevertDetector` arms `RevertKind`, `ParsekScenario.OnLoad` collects the `VesselName` of EVERY committed recording with `SpawnedVesselPersistentId != 0` into a GLOBAL name set, and `StripOrphanedSpawnedVessels` removed any flightState protoVessel whose `vesselName` was in that set (matcher was NAME ONLY, skipping only PRELAUNCH + ghost-map). ProtoVessels carry the craft-baked name/pid, which KSP reuses on every launch of a design, so a real, separately launched craft was indistinguishable from a recording's spawned vessel and got deleted on ANY revert that loaded a quicksave containing it. Cross-checking the 7 by launch Guid: 6 had `SpawnedVesselPersistentId` == live pid but a CONCLUSIVE Guid MISMATCH (a different launch wrongly deleted); the 7th (`R3-B2-U1-S7`, pid 364626662) was a real vessel Parsek had legitimately ADOPTED (`SpawnedVesselPersistentId == VesselPersistentId`, Guid match) but from an unrelated mission. The adoption path itself (`VesselSpawner.MaterializedSourceVesselExists` -> `VesselLaunchIdentity.LiveVesselIsRecordedLaunch`) was already Guid-gated; the STRIP threw that gating away by keying on name, and `ReconcileSpawnStateAfterStrip` keyed on bare pid.

**Fix (branch `bug-h-revert-vessel-strip`):** two corrections plus a centralized guid-aware deletion predicate so no strip/cleanup path can match a relaunch of the same craft. (1) **Launch-Guid gate.** New `VesselLaunchIdentity.LiveVesselIsRecordedSpawn` (genuine Parsek spawns use a KSP-unique spawn pid -> pid match conclusive; adoption stamps reuse the craft-baked pid -> require the launch Guid to not conclusively differ) + `CandidateMatchesRecording` / `FindMatchingRecording`. Every deletion routes through the centralized pure predicate `ParsekScenario.ShouldStripVesselForRecordings`, which resolves the candidate's pid + `Vessel.id`/`ProtoVessel.vesselID` Guid (the stale "ProtoVessel doesn't expose pid" comment was wrong and is removed) and only strips on a same-launch match. A conclusive Guid mismatch is NEVER stripped. (2) **Scope to the reverted flight.** The stock revert events fire with the state being left, not the target, so `RevertDetector` now captures the revert-target vessel pids from `FlightDriver.PreLaunchState` (Prelaunch) / `PostInitState` (Launch) `GameBackup.Config` (`ExtractFlightStateVesselPids`: GAME -> FLIGHTSTATE -> VESSEL[] persistentId) as a pre-existing whitelist; the revert strip removes only vessels NOT in that whitelist (i.e. they appeared during the reverted flight) and FAILS CLOSED (strips nothing) when the whitelist is unavailable. This protects the legitimately-adopted same-launch vessel (the 7th) that a pure Guid gate alone would still delete. `StripOrphanedSpawnedVessels` was rewritten to take the committed recordings + flags + whitelist; both callers updated (revert: matchSource=false, requireWhitelist=true; rewind: matchSource=true, requireWhitelist=false to preserve the rewind contract - genuinely future-timeline vessels are still removed via the launch-identity match plus the existing `StripFuturePrelaunchVessels` pid-whitelist pass). The whitelist is applied as a protect-set whenever supplied (not just on revert): the rewind path passes `RewindContext.RewindQuicksaveVesselPids` so a vessel that pre-existed the rewind point is never deleted even for the rare guidless adoption-stamp recording where the Guid gate falls back to pid-only (adversarial-review follow-up; `requireWhitelist=false` keeps identity-only behaviour when the quicksave pids are absent). `ReconcileSpawnStateAfterStrip` gained a guid-aware overload (a surviving same-pid DIFFERENT-launch vessel no longer keeps a recording's spawn state alive); the revert reconcile routes through it. `ParsekFlight.CleanupOrphanedSpawnedVessels` (OnFlightReady belt-and-suspenders for FLIGHT->FLIGHT launch revert) now uses the same predicate + scope instead of name/pid recovery. `ShouldStripFuturePrelaunch` audited: pid-whitelist-based (keep-if-present), not in the defect class, behaviour unchanged. Tests: `VesselLaunchIdentityTests` (spawn/adoption/source matchers), `RevertVesselStripTests` (pid-collision-different-Guid not stripped; same-launch adoption protected by scope; genuine during-flight spawn stripped; fail-closed; rewind matchSource contract; guid-aware reconcile; `ExtractFlightStateVesselPids` parser), and in-game `RuntimeTests.RevertStrip_LiveGuidGate_ProtectsDifferentLaunch`. Note: recovering the already-deleted vessels in save `c1` is a separate manual repair, not part of this code fix.

**Known residuals (from two adversarial Opus reviews; accepted, not blockers):** (a) Fail-closed trade-off - when the revert-target snapshot is unavailable the revert strip removes NOTHING, which trades a rare contamination risk (a genuine Parsek-spawned orphan persisting into the next quicksave, the original #109/#110 concern) for never deleting a real vessel; this is the deliberate data-safe direction. (b) `RecordingStore.PreProcessRewindSave` still strips the rewind-target `.sfs` by NAME (`removedByName`) - the same defect class, but narrowly scoped to one `BuildRewindStripNames(owner)` (not the global set) and operating on the rewind-target save rather than the live save, so far lower risk; left as a follow-up to migrate onto the same launch-identity predicate. (c) The OnFlightReady cleanup can consume a stale whitelist across a prelaunch-revert -> EDITOR -> relaunch sequence; benign because the Guid gate is the real backstop (a fresh launch's fresh Guid will not match an adoption-stamp recording).

## Done - BUG-F (2026-06-07 career-load regression): cold-loading an established career wiped the stock economy (funds to seed, science to 0)

**Symptom (player-reported):** loading the `c1` career save (build 0.10.1, all recent fixes merged) collapsed funds to 20095 (= seed 25000 - 4905 spent) and science to 0, with NO Parsek feature in use. The live save was overwritten on first cold-load. New-session log: `logs/2026-06-07_1934_career-load-regression/KSP.log`; pre-wipe backup `Kerbal Space Program/saves/c1_backup_pre_fix_20260607` (funds 72906, sci 1.0).

**Root cause (latent, not a 0.10.0->0.10.1 regression):** the load-time ledger recalc applies a "current-UT cutoff" that filters committed actions to the live game clock (built for post-rewind / future-timeline saves so future rewards are not paid out early). During a cold `ScenarioModule.OnLoad` the universe clock is not yet initialized, so `Planetarium.GetUniversalTime()` returns 0; the load passes `maxUT=0`. `LedgerOrchestrator.OnKspLoad` then took the cutoff path because `HasActionsAfterUT(0)` is true (every committed action is after UT 0), filtering 141 of 144 actions and patching funds/science down to the seed (`Current-UT ledger recalculation: reason=ksp-load cutoffUT=0` -> `PatchFunds: 72906 -> 20095`, `PatchScience: 1.0 -> 0.0`). The `DeferredSeedAndRecalculate` coroutine that was supposed to re-seed correct values fired with the same UT=0 (it waited for resource singleton VALUES, which were already loaded, not for the clock) and re-confirmed the wipe (`reason=deferred-seed cutoffUT=0`). The 0.10.0 session (`logs/2026-06-07_1638_career-playtest/`) only looked fine because that load had an empty ledger (`before=0, validRecordingIds=0` -> `HasActionsAfterUT(0)=false` -> safe full replay); both builds ran identical code with `maxUT=0, preserveFutureTimelineActions=True`. The in-session FLIGHT->FLIGHT load path was already guarded (`ShouldUseCurrentUtCutoffForPostRewindFlightLoad` checks `planetariumReady`); only the cold-load `OnKspLoad` + `DeferredSeed` paths were unguarded.

**Fix (branch `bug-f-coldload-wipe`, PR #1092):** added `LedgerOrchestrator.IsCurrentUtReadyForCutoff(double ut) => ut > 0.0` and gate every load-time cutoff/prune decision on it. (1) `OnKspLoad` (`LedgerOrchestrator.cs`) applies the current-UT cutoff only when `useCurrentUtCutoffForFutureActions && IsCurrentUtReadyForCutoff(maxUT) && HasActionsAfterUT(maxUT)`, otherwise falls back to the safe full replay (`RecalculateAndPatch`, cutoffUT=null) that replays every committed action; logs an `OnKspLoad recalc decision` line. (2) Both `Ledger.Reconcile` calls now pass `preserveFutureTimelineActions: useCurrentUtCutoffForFutureActions || !currentUtReady`, so a not-ready clock preserves all committed rows regardless of scene. This closes a sibling catastrophe found in review: a cold-load into a NON-cutoff scene (TRACKSTATION / EDITOR, where `useCurrentUtCutoffForFutureActions` is false) at maxUT=0 would otherwise let Reconcile PERMANENTLY PRUNE the whole career's spend history (not just mis-patch it). (3) The shared `RecalculateAndPatchForCurrentTimelineIfFutureActions` helper got the same guard (in-session callers pass a valid UT via `GetCurrentTimelineUTForLedgerRecalc`, so only the not-ready path changes - belt-and-suspenders against any future caller passing UT<=0). (4) `DeferredSeedAndRecalculate` (`ParsekScenario.cs`) now adds a bounded Phase-3 wait for the universe clock to report a positive UT before deciding, then routes through the guarded helper; a timed-out wait falls back to full replay. The per-frame clock poll reads through `TryReadReadyUniverseTime`, which wraps `Planetarium.GetUniversalTime()` in a try/catch (it can throw during very early load - same precedent as `Update()`), so a throw cannot kill the coroutine. This preserves the legitimate post-rewind case: a valid positive UT with committed actions still ahead of it keeps the cutoff (future rewards stay filtered). Tests: `IsCurrentUtReadyForCutoff_*` predicate; `OnKspLoad_ColdLoadWithUnreadyClock_ReplaysEntireCareer_NoWipe` (the regression test: maxUT=0 -> full replay, actionsAfterCutoff=N, no `reason=ksp-load` cutoff); `OnKspLoad_ColdLoadNonCutoffScene_PreservesCareerRows_NoPrune` (the prune sibling); `OnKspLoad_ReadyClockWithFutureActions_StillAppliesCutoff` (post-rewind case still cuts off); `OnKspLoad_ReadyClockPastAllActions_ReplaysFullLedger` (guard does not over-trigger); `RewindUtCutoffTests.CurrentTimelineIfFutureActions_NotReadyClock_ReplaysFullLedger` (shared helper guard); plus the existing `OnKspLoad_WithFutureLedgerActionsAndCurrentUtCutoff_RecalculatesAtLoadUt`.

**Follow-up (NOT in this fix, separate save/ledger repair):** after BUG-F lands, the `c1` save recalcs back only to its pre-wipe state (sci ~1.0, funds ~72906); fully restoring the lost Mun science (~124.8 - a BUG-A symptom) is a separate save repair.

## Done 2026-06-07 - Recalc-patch drawdown guard (defense-in-depth, BUG-A follow-up)

**Source:** The anticipated BUG-A follow-up (see the BUG-A entry below: "a defense-in-depth guard that refuses a large negative drawdown when no rewind/re-fly is active is a sensible follow-up but was not needed to fix the root cause"). Plan: `docs/dev/plans/recalc-patch-drawdown-guard.md`.

**What it does:** When a ledger recalc would patch live funds / science / reputation DOWN past the per-resource rounding epsilon (funds 0.01, science 0.001, rep 0.01) AND no time-travel context is active, the patch is CLAMPED so the player's value is preserved (`max(patchTarget, currentLive)`), a single session-scoped native `ParsekLog.ScreenMessage` ("Kept your earned funds/science/reputation") is posted per resource, and a WARN with the full numbers fires on every guarded recalc. Always on, no setting.

**Predicate (Blocker 2 / plan §3.3):** The guard keys on the NON-RESERVED running balance (`FundsModule.GetRunningBalance` / `ScienceModule.GetRunningScience` / `ReputationModule.GetRunningRep`), NOT the reservation-aware patch target (`GetAvailableFunds` / `GetAvailableScience`). A reservation legitimately lowers `available` below `running` on cutoff walks (committed future spends), so keying on the target would defeat overspend prevention; a missing-earning leak lowers `running` itself below live. Reputation has no reservation, so its running balance IS its target. Per-subject science (`PatchPerSubjectScience`) stays unclamped (a documented limitation called out in the pool clamp WARN, MINOR 5).

**Authoritative-reduction bypass (five signals, plan §3.2):** the clamp is suppressed when any of `RewindContext.IsRewinding`, `ParsekScenario.Instance.ActiveReFlySessionMarker != null`, `ParsekScenario.Instance.ActiveMergeJournal != null`, the tombstone path (`RecalculateAndPatchAfterTombstones` -> `tombstonePath: true`), or the NEW `RewindContext.RewindResourceAdjustmentInProgress` is set. The fifth signal (Blocker 1) is the ONLY one true at the deferred plain-Rewind-to-Launch authoritative recalc (`ApplyRewindResourceAdjustment` -> `RecalculateAndPatch(adjustedUT)`): it is set synchronously in `HandleRewindOnLoad` before `StartCoroutine`, cleared in the coroutine's try/finally around that patch (authoritative), and cleared as a race-free fail-safe in the next scene's `ParsekScenario.OnAwake` (NOT a blanket scene-switch clear, which would race the coroutine's ~2s singleton wait).

**Plumbing:** `RecalculateAndPatchCore` computes `authoritativeReduction` from the five signals and threads it (plus a new `tombstonePath` Core param) through `ApplyRecalculatedStateToKsp` -> `KspStatePatcher.PatchAll` -> `PatchScience` / `PatchFunds` / `PatchReputation`, parallel to the existing `suppressSuspiciousDrawdownWarnings`. The legacy log-only `IsSuspiciousDrawdown` 10% WARN is untouched.

**Files:** `Source/Parsek/GameActions/KspStatePatcher.cs` (`IsGuardableDrawdown`, `ApplyDrawdownGuard`, `EmitDrawdownGuardClamp`, session-scoped toast latches, three patch methods), `Source/Parsek/GameActions/LedgerOrchestrator.cs` (`IsAuthoritativeReduction`, Core/Apply threading), `Source/Parsek/RewindContext.cs` (signal 5 + Begin/End + ResetForTesting), `Source/Parsek/ParsekScenario.cs` (HandleRewindOnLoad arm, coroutine finally, OnAwake fail-safe, save-boundary latch reset), `Source/Parsek/InGameTests/RuntimeTests.cs` (live clamp + signal-bypass test), `Source/Parsek.Tests/DrawdownGuardTests.cs`.

**Status:** Fixed for v0.10.1. Full xUnit suite green (14559, +25). In-game validation pending: a clean career playtest must produce ZERO guarded clamps; a deliberately-leaked / forced-too-low ledger must clamp + preserve live + toast on funds/science/rep; a real rewind / re-fly / tombstone reduction must still apply (authorized). Run `RuntimeTests.DrawdownGuard_ClampsLeakAndAuthorizesSignal` (Ctrl+Shift+T, SPACECENTER) to verify the live patch path.

## Done - Rewind read-back divergence guard (audit rec #1, `docs/dev/ledger-state-reconstruction-audit.md` §8)

**Source:** Recommendation #1 (highest leverage, most self-contained) of the ledger-state-reconstruction audit. At the Rewind-to-Separation apply boundary, detect (loudly log; optionally abort) when the recalc would write the career economy BELOW the real career economy, turning a silent career-corruption clobber into a caught, logged event.

**Design - two-witness "economy floor", downward-only, realized-vs-realized.** The §6 oracle premise was CORRECTED: the loaded quicksave is the OLD at-RP economy, NOT the live-tip the recalc targets, so a naive "target vs quicksave" check false-flags every healthy rewind (legit post-RP earning/spending), and the `authoritativeReduction` flag is true at this boundary (ReFly marker armed) so it cannot be used to excuse the drop. Instead the guard captures TWO independent witnesses of the real career economy and flags only when the recalc's realized target falls below BOTH: `E_before` (live funds/science/rep captured in `RewindInvoker.StartInvoke` BEFORE `GamePersistence.LoadGame`, parked on the surviving `RewindInvokeContext`) and `E_rp` (live economy captured post-load in `RunStripActivateMarker` immediately before the recalc = the loaded quicksave economy). `floor = min(E_before, E_rp)` per resource (finite witnesses only). The min-floor structurally encodes legit drawdown (post-RP spending lowers `E_before`) and absorbs uncommitted-in-flight effects (#466: older quicksave `E_rp` approximately equals target, so floor = `E_rp`, no false flag), so the guard does NOT gate on `authoritativeReduction` (but logs it). Compared against the recalc's REALIZED running value: funds `GetRunningBalance()`, rep `GetRunningRep()`, science the SAME pending-adjusted running value `PatchScience` uses (extracted into `KspStatePatcher.ComputePendingAdjustedRunningScience` and called from both so they are byte-identical). `FlaggedDivergence iff target < floor - tolerance` (downward only; upward restore is Verbose-only); a NaN/Inf target is itself corruption -> FlaggedDivergence; no finite witness -> NotEvaluated (logged skip). Per-resource absolute tolerances `funds 1.0 / science 0.1 / rep 0.1` (a touch looser than the patch no-op epsilons).

**Default = warn-only, never alters a successful rewind.** Abort is opt-in via `RewindReadbackGuard.AbortRewindPatchOnDivergence` (default OFF). When abort is enabled and a divergence is flagged, `PatchAll` early-returns before the `Patch*` dispatch (crew roster already applied by `kerbalsModule.ApplyToRoster`; loaded quicksave economy values stand). The guard is armed only for the post-load recalc and cleared in a `finally` so it never leaks onto an ordinary recalc patch.

**Files:** `Source/Parsek/RewindReadbackGuard.cs` (new: `EconomySnapshot` struct + `RewindReadbackGuard` holder), `Source/Parsek/GameActions/KspStatePatcher.cs` (`RewindReadbackVerdict`, pure `ResolveRewindDivergence`, `RunRewindReadbackGuard`, `ComputePendingAdjustedRunningScience` extraction, PatchAll wiring + tolerances), `Source/Parsek/RewindInvokeContext.cs` (`ReadbackPreRewind` runtime-only field + Clear), `Source/Parsek/RewindInvoker.cs` (E_before capture + arm/finally-clear), `Source/Parsek.Tests/RewindReadbackGuardTests.cs` (20 tests), `Source/Parsek/InGameTests/RuntimeTests.cs` (`RewindReadbackGuard_WarnsOnDivergence_LeavesLiveUnchanged`, warn-only).

**Status:** Implemented. Full xUnit suite green except the known `InjectAllRecordings` environmental flake (KSP.log lock). In-game validation pending: run `RuntimeTests.RewindReadbackGuard_WarnsOnDivergence_LeavesLiveUnchanged` (Ctrl+Shift+T, FLIGHT) to confirm the WARN fires and live values are untouched; a real healthy rewind should log only within-range / Verbose lines (no FLAGGED DIVERGENCE).

## Done - Per-identity logging at the apply boundary (audit rec #2, gaps 1-3, `docs/dev/ledger-state-reconstruction-audit.md` §4.2)

**Source:** Recommendation #2 of the ledger-state-reconstruction audit: promote the three HIGH-risk per-identity logging gaps from Verbose-only to the default (Info) apply line so a per-subject-science / tech-node / contract corruption is diagnosable from a normal `KSP.log`, not only Verbose.

- ~~**Gap 1 - per-subject science (`KspStatePatcher.PatchPerSubjectScience`):**~~ DONE. The Info summary now carries a bounded `changedSubjects=[subjectId:old->new, ...]` clause (old read before the write), full list at Verbose.
- ~~**Gap 2 - tech-node availability flips (`KspStatePatcher.PatchTechTree`):**~~ DONE. The Info summary now carries bounded `madeUnavailableIds=[...]` (the dangerous re-lock direction, listed first) and `madeAvailableIds=[...]` clauses, full lists at Verbose. (The `...Ids` suffix keeps the identity-list clauses distinct from the existing `madeAvailable=`/`madeUnavailable=` count fields on the same line.)
- ~~**Gap 3 - contract remove/restore (`KspStatePatcher.PatchContracts`):**~~ DONE. The Info summary now carries bounded `removedIds=[...]` (targeted removal keys, current set before finished set) and `restoredIds=[...]` clauses, full lists at Verbose.

**Mechanism:** shared pure formatter `KspStatePatcher.ComposeBoundedIdentitySample(list, cap=10)` returns `string.Empty` for a null/empty list (steady-state Info lines stay byte-identical), joins under the cap, and appends ` (+N more)` over the cap; each clause is appended only when the sample is non-empty. Contract removed-identity derivation is the pure `DescribeRemovedContractIdentities`. Logging-only, no schema/serialized-field change.

**Files:** `Source/Parsek/GameActions/KspStatePatcher.cs` (formatter + `DescribeRemovedContractIdentities` + the three Info-line clauses + paired Verbose full-list lines), `Source/Parsek.Tests/KspStatePatcherTests.cs` (6 pure-helper tests).

## Done - xUnit apply-boundary tests (audit rec #5, `docs/dev/ledger-state-reconstruction-audit.md` §5.1 layer (e) / §5.3 risk 1-3)
