- **SHIPPED via re-aim (branch `reaim-transfers`, 2026-05-31): interplanetary looping now re-plans the heliocentric transfer to the target's CURRENT position each synodic window** (the RE-AIM model, see `docs/dev/done/plans/reaim-interplanetary-transfers.md`), superseding the replay-as-is plan below for the interplanetary case. Steeply-inclined targets (e.g. Moho) still decline to faithful replay (ecliptic-projection limitation, see the design-doc deferred list). Original Phase-4 replay-as-is plan kept for reference: a sibling/interplanetary target was reported `UnsupportedCrossParent` (falls back to the raw anchor, never mis-scheduled). The clean replay-as-is extension reuses the Phase-2 joint best-fit: emit heliocentric `Orbital` constraints for BOTH the origin body (Kerbin) and the target body (Duna) around the shared parent (Sun) and let `FindBestJointMultiple` find the multi-period near-resonance (the dominant = the longest heliocentric period). The body-hierarchy walk to the common parent is already designed in the logistics doc (`docs/parsek-logistics-supply-routes-design.md` §8.1) and `IBodyInfo.ReferenceBodyName`/`OrbitPeriod` already expose the inputs. NOT the synodic period (that is the re-aim model). Interplanetary near-resonance periods are very long (the ghost is rare), so pair with the warp-to-window quick-win below.
- **Re-aim follow-up (#26) DONE: orbit-line blink at the transfer-start and Duna-approach phase boundaries.** Symptom (playtest re-aim Kerbin->Duna, ghost pid 2439764378): the ghost's map orbit line blinked on/off every few frames at the heliocentric transfer START just after Kerbin SOI exit (live UT ~378,375,254-378,375,730) and on the Duna SOI approach / capture (live UT ~385,368,033-385,375,335). Root cause: an undamped per-frame three-way exclusive visibility decision in `GhostOrbitLinePatch.Postfix`. At a phase boundary the recording fragments into many short orbit segments interleaved with short non-orbital legs, and the per-frame orbit reseed (`GhostMapPresence.UpdateGhostOrbitForRecording`) lags the head by up to one refresh interval, so the decision ping-pongs `visible-body-frame` (ON) -> `stale-segment-awaiting-reseed` (OFF) -> `polyline-owns-phase` (OFF) -> `visible-body-frame` (ON) with no hysteresis. Both OFF reasons are legitimate in isolation (the polyline ownership IS correctly head-UT-gated to the recording's own current leg, not a cross-phase leak); the defect was purely the lack of a debounce on the TRANSIENT off transitions. **Fix:** a short UT grace window (`GhostOrbitLinePatch.OrbitLineGraceSeconds = 1.5`, UT-based so it is warp-stable) is stamped per-pid (`GhostMapPresence.ghostOrbitLineGraceUntilUT`) whenever the line is genuinely shown (`visible-body-frame` / `terminal-visible`). When the decision would flip to one of the two TRANSIENT off reasons AND `currentUT <= graceUntil` AND the orbit is finite + elliptical, the pure helper `GhostOrbitLinePatch.ShouldDeferOrbitLineHide` keeps the orbit LINE visible for that frame. The DURABLE off reasons (`below-atmosphere`, `past-body-frame-end`, `before-body-frame-start`, terminal below-atmosphere) are never graced and hide instantly. A SUSTAINED transient phase (e.g. the below-surface Duna descent that #27 makes the polyline own) still hides because the grace deadline was last stamped during a genuine show, so it expires within ~1.5s and the off takes effect (no double-draw of line + polyline). The grace map clears alongside `ghostsWithSuppressedIcon` in every ghost teardown / scene-change spot. **Icon handling differs by branch (clean-context review CHANGE 1):** the `polyline-owns-phase` grace-defer keeps the orbit LINE on but leaves the proto ICON SUPPRESSED (`drawIcons=NONE`, icon stays in `ghostsWithSuppressedIcon`), because `IsPolylineOwningGhostPhase(pid)` is TRUE there, so `ClassifyAtmosphericMarkerSkip` / `DrawMapMarkers` still draw the non-proto marker regardless of the suppressed flag; re-showing the proto icon (`OBJ`) would draw BOTH it and the non-proto marker for the deferred frame (a transient double-icon, the exact symptom the polyline-owns branch exists to prevent). The `stale-segment-awaiting-reseed` grace-defer DOES re-show `OBJ` + clear the suppression, because the polyline does NOT own the phase there (`IsPolylineOwningGhostPhase` false) so the marker is already skipped and the proto icon is the right sole indicator. 19 `GhostOrbitLineGraceTests` (transient-inside-window defers, deadline-inclusive, expired-sustained hides, durable-never-graced, non-elliptical hides, per-pid map round-trip + reset clear, plus the CHANGE-1 symmetric-line-defer + distinct-reason-constants pins). Pure decision + per-pid map are xUnit-tested; the Unity Postfix wiring (stamp on show, defer on transient dip, branch-specific icon side-effect) is playtest-validated. **Playtest check:** the two blink UT windows above should now show a steady line; the Duna descent tail should keep its polyline (#27) with the orbit line off.
- **Re-aim follow-up (#26b) DONE: orbit line STILL blinks at transfer start/end (second, distinct mechanism from #26).** Branch `fix-orbit-line-soi-blink` off `origin/main`. The user re-reported the transfer-start / transfer-end blink on a build that ALREADY has both prior `line.active` blink fixes (#26 grace window at todo line ~100, and the body-frame-bounds same-body carry in the `### Known limitations` SOI-flicker entry). Confirmed the deployed build is the shipped re-aim baseline (`origin/main`, deployed `Parsek.dll` md5 555de026 from `investigate-loopshift-stored-bounds`; has `covering-segment`/`icon-pos-delta`/`re-aimed transfer ready` but NONE of the unmerged `reaim-arrival-fix` symbols), so this is NOT a `reaim-arrival-fix` regression. **Root cause (KSP.log `logs/2026-06-01_1147_transfer-blink`, member #30):** `GhostMapPresence.ApplyOrbitToVessel` (and the sibling state-vector update path) computed `soiChanged = vessel.orbitDriver.referenceBody != body` and, on true, force-toggled `orbitRenderer.enabled = false; enabled = true` (a FULL renderer teardown/rebuild, separate from the `line.active` toggle the #26/carry fixes debounce). KSP's own orbit propagation re-transitions an unloaded ghost's `OrbitDriver.referenceBody` between Parsek's per-frame reseeds (the Kerbin escape hyperbola gets kicked out to the Sun; the center-aimed transfer's endpoints fall back inside Kerbin / Duna SOI), so `soiChanged` tripped EVERY frame near an SOI boundary even though the covering segment was stable on one body. Evidence: **115 `Forced orbit renderer redraw for recording #30`** in one window, with `SOI change ... new body=Kerbin` repeating 8x (escape hyperbola) then `new body=Sun` dozens of times while `covering-segment CHANGED` showed ONE stable Kerbin segment then ONE stable Sun segment; a 77s quiet gap mid-transfer (far from any SOI) had zero redraws, exactly matching "blinks at the start and end of the transfer." The per-frame `enabled` toggle overrides the `line.active=true` the #26 grace sets, so the prior fixes could not suppress it. **Fix:** gate `soiChanged` on the body PARSEK last applied to this ghost, tracked in new `Dictionary<uint,string> ghostLastAppliedOrbitBody` (keyed by persistentId, cleared/removed alongside `ghostOrbitBounds` at all five lifecycle sites + `ResetForTesting`), via the pure `GhostMapPresence.GhostOrbitBodyChanged(lastApplied, newBody)` (null/empty or differing name => change). The renderer rebuild + the `SOI change` log now fire ONCE per genuine Parsek-driven body change instead of every frame; `drawMode` stays `REDRAW_AND_RECALCULATE` after the first change so the line keeps tracking the per-frame reseed without the disruptive enable-toggle (no clip-staleness regression). Applied to BOTH `ApplyOrbitToVessel` (orbit segments: parking/escape/transfer/capture - the transfer blink) and the state-vector update path (surface/relative ghosts share the bug). 5 `GhostMapPresenceTests.GhostOrbitBodyChanged*` (no-prior/same/different/case/transfer-sequence-fires-once-per-seam). Clean-context Opus review verdict SHIP (no blockers; only added the sequence test it flagged as an optional gap; confirmed via in-repo decompilation note that `drawMode` stays REDRAW_AND_RECALCULATE so dropping the per-frame enable-toggle does not leave a stale/wrong-SOI line). **PLAYTEST (2026-06-01, `Kerbal Space Program/KSP.log` ~12:20, deployed fix build): the forced-redraw fix WORKED on its target (forced redraws 115 -> 3) but the VISIBLE heliocentric blink PERSISTED** - it is a SECOND, distinct mechanism (see #26c). The forced-redraw fix is correct + reviewed but was NOT the visible blink; polylines confirmed NOT broken by it (byte-identical 16-leg build pre/post; the drawn/not-drawn churn pre-exists). Lesson re-applied: a redraw-count win is not a blink fix; confirm against the visible mechanism (`feedback_confirm_diagnosis_against_evidence`).
- **Re-aim follow-up (#26c) DONE: heliocentric orbit-line blink under time warp = the #26 grace is defeated by warp.** Read-only diagnosis (KSP.log `logs/2026-06-01_1147` + the ~12:20 fix-build run): for the transfer member (pid 2010250405 = rec 61e91771) the orbit line `line.active` flips `visible-body-frame` (ON) -> `polyline-owns-phase`/`stale-segment-awaiting-reseed` (OFF) every 1-5 s through the heliocentric phase = the blink. Both OFF reasons are TRANSIENT (head momentarily in a short non-orbital leg, or a one-refresh reseed lag) and the #26 grace exists to defer them. **Root cause:** the #26 grace deadline was a UT window (`OrbitLineGraceSeconds = 1.5`), tested `Planetarium.GetUniversalTime() <= lastShownUT + 1.5`. The blink is per-RENDER-FRAME chatter, and under warp one render frame advances UT by far more than 1.5 s (the log showed ~431.9 UT advanced in 5.77 real s ~= 75x => ~2.5 UT/frame, already > 1.5), so a transient dip's `currentUT` is past the deadline on the very next frame and the grace deferred ZERO frames. That is why #26 passed its low-warp playtest but blinks at transfer-watching warp. **Fix (branch `fix-orbit-line-soi-blink`):** denominate the grace in RENDER FRAMES, not UT. `OrbitLineGraceFrames = 20` (tunable; observed dips ~1-12 frames); stamp `Time.frameCount + OrbitLineGraceFrames` on every genuinely-shown frame; `ShouldDeferOrbitLineHide` defers while `Time.frameCount <= graceUntilFrame`. Warp-independent: defers a few-frame transient dip at any warp, while a SUSTAINED off (> N consecutive off-frames, e.g. the #27 below-surface descent the polyline owns) still expires and hides (grace last stamped while visible), preserving the #27 handoff. Per-pid grace map retyped `Dictionary<uint,double> ghostOrbitLineGraceUntilUT` -> `Dictionary<uint,int> ghostOrbitLineGraceUntilFrame` (accessors `GetOrbitLineGraceUntilFrame` / `StampOrbitLineGrace(int)`, default `int.MinValue`, cleared at all 5 lifecycle sites). 20 `GhostOrbitLineGraceTests` retargeted to frame ints (pure decision is unit-agnostic: `current <= graceUntil`), incl. a stamp->defer->expire composition test. Clean-context Opus review verdict SHIP-WITH-FIXES (both items applied: stale "(in universe time)" doc comment corrected; the composition test added). **PLAYTEST 2 (2026-06-01, KSP.log 13:23): the frame-grace fix CORRECTLY RAN (2 `hide deferred by grace ... currentFrame=.. graceUntilFrame=..` lines) but the visible heliocentric blink STILL PERSISTED long after Kerbin SOI exit.** Per-pid line.active decision counts were minimal (4 visible-body-frame ON, 1 polyline-owns OFF total in the whole capture), so the orbit line is NOT chattering at the patch-decision level - meaning the THIRD mechanism is something the existing logging cannot see: KSP / another patch toggling line.active or renderer.enabled BETWEEN our Postfix calls (our `VerboseOnChange` decision log only fires when OUR decision changes), or an intra-window icon teleport invisible to the 5s-rate-limited `icon-pos-delta`. **Diagnostic added (commit 9d1f87cb? -> see below):** new `Source/Parsek/GhostRenderStateProbe.cs`, a [DefaultExecutionOrder(10000)] DDOL MonoBehaviour that LateUpdates AFTER OrbitRendererBase.LateUpdate (where our Postfix runs) and samples each ghost map vessel's actually-rendered state - `OrbitRendererBase.line.active` (cached reflection on the protected field), `orbitRenderer.enabled`, `drawMode`, `drawIcons`, `orbit.referenceBody`, sma/ecc, `Vessel.GetWorldPos3D` - logging via `ParsekLog.VerboseOnChange` keyed per-(pid,field) so any 1-frame toggle out-and-back is two log lines. Adds an icon JUMP detector (per-frame, soft 0.5s rate-limit, threshold 1000 km/frame) catching intra-window teleports the existing icon log misses. READ-ONLY: never mutates renderer / orbit state. Build clean, deployed. **Playtest 3 watch:** launch with the new build, watch the transfer through SOI exit + coast. Grep `render-state line.active CHANGED` / `render-state renderer.enabled CHANGED` / `render-state icon JUMP` in KSP.log. If those fire during the blink window the blink IS line/renderer toggling and we now know what is doing it; if those stay silent through the blink the blink is downstream of `line.active` (e.g. Vectrosity material/clip state, OrbitRendererBase.DrawOrbit internals, or another renderer entirely). **PLAYTEST 3 PROBED (2026-06-01, `logs/2026-06-01_1348_orbit-line-blink-probe`): the probe nailed it. 49 `icon JUMP` events of ~13.6 Gm/frame and 69 `body/orbit CHANGED` events showed the orbit ping-ponging body=Sun (sma=1.77e10 ecc=0.23 - correct re-aim) <-> body=Kerbin (sma~-4M ecc=1.0000 - DEGENERATE state-vector-derived) ~once per second through the heliocentric coast. `line.active` and `renderer.enabled` were stable (only 2 changes each), so the prior two `line.active` and `orbitRenderer.enabled` fixes were targeting the wrong subsystem entirely. The smoking gun is one log line above each Kerbin flip: **`[OrbitDriver]: On-Rails SOI Transition from Sun to Kerbin`** (stock KSP log, no `[Parsek]` prefix). KSP's own `OrbitDriver.UpdateOrbit` is doing an on-rails patched-conic SOI transition INTO Kerbin (because the orbit's `patchEndTransition`/`nextPatch`/`EndUT` predict one - either from a stale ENCOUNTER on the synthesized transfer or from a recorded escape segment's past EndUT), and re-derives the elements from the state vector relative to Kerbin at a heliocentric position (~13.6 Gm out), producing a degenerate ecc=1.0000 conic. Within ~30 ms Parsek's per-frame re-aim resolver reseeds body=Sun, then KSP transitions again, etc. The visible "blink" is the line redrawing on wildly different conics each pass.
- **Re-aim follow-up (#26d) DONE: neutralize KSP's on-rails SOI transition for ghost orbits.** Fix on branch `fix-orbit-line-soi-blink`. New `GhostMapPresence.NeutralizeGhostOrbitOnRailsTransition(Orbit orb)` helper, called from BOTH reseed paths (`ApplyOrbitToVessel` orbit-segment path and the state-vector update path) immediately after `vessel.orbitDriver.updateFromParameters()` + `NormalizeGhostOrbitDriverTargetIdentity`. Sets `orb.patchEndTransition = FINAL`, `orb.nextPatch = null`, `orb.closestEncounterBody/Patch = null`, `orb.EndUT = double.PositiveInfinity` (no past-EndUT trigger), `orb.UTsoi = -1.0`. After this, `OrbitDriver.UpdateOrbit` has no patched-conic prediction to act on and leaves the orbit where Parsek put it. Ghost map presence does not need patched-conic transitions: every body/orbit change is driven explicitly by the per-frame Parsek lifecycle (re-aim resolver + `ApplyOrbitToVessel`), and the orbit line / icon position are computed from the current Keplerian elements alone. Tested xUnit-green (321 ghost-map tests pass). Unity-runtime semantics (KSP no longer logging `On-Rails SOI Transition` for ghost vessels) are playtest-validated. **Playtest 4 watch:** the `[OrbitDriver]: On-Rails SOI Transition from Sun to Kerbin` log lines should DISAPPEAR for ghost vessels, the probe's body=Kerbin events during the heliocentric coast should STOP (the body should stay Sun), the icon JUMP events should stop, and the line should hold steady. Clean-context Opus review verdict SHIP-WITH-OPTIONAL-FOLLOWUPS. MAJOR-1 + MINOR-1 applied: neutralizer now ALSO called inside `BuildAndLoadGhostProtoVesselCore`; switched `orb.EndUT` sentinel to `double.MaxValue`. **PLAYTEST 4 RESULT (2026-06-01, `logs/2026-06-01_1414_orbit-blink-postneutralize`): the neutralizer FAILED.** KSP loaded my build at 14:11:20.6 (every GameData assembly loaded in that burst, ~70s BEFORE a sibling-worktree clobber landed at 14:12:30, so the running game DID have the neutralizer); yet 45 `[OrbitDriver]: On-Rails SOI Transition from Sun to Kerbin` lines still fired with the body still ping-ponging Sun<->Kerbin + 60 icon JUMPs. Clearing `patchEndTransition`/`nextPatch`/`EndUT`/`UTsoi` did NOT stop it. **Decompiled OrbitDriver to find the TRUE trigger (`tmp-orbital-decompile/OrbitDriver.decompiled.cs`):** `UpdateOrbit` (UPDATE mode, which ghosts use - confirmed `updateMode=UPDATE` in the create log) calls `CheckDominantBody(referenceBody.position + pos)` EVERY FRAME (line 346; TRACK_Phys/IDLE call it with `vessel.CoMD` at line 316). `CheckDominantBody` runs `FlightGlobals.getMainBody(refPos)` and, if the dominant body != current referenceBody && !`FlightGlobals.overrideOrbit`, calls `RecalculateOrbit -> OnRailsSOITransition`. It is a LIVE position-based check, recomputed every frame, completely independent of the cached patch fields the neutralizer cleared - which is why the neutralizer was a no-op. **The neutralizer was REMOVED (proven ineffective + misleadingly named) and replaced with the real fix (#26e).**
- **Re-aim follow-up (#26e) DONE: suppress KSP's per-frame dominant-body SOI transition for ghost vessels.** New Harmony Prefix `Source/Parsek/Patches/GhostOrbitDominantBodyPatch.cs` on `OrbitDriver.CheckDominantBody`: for a vessel whose `persistentId` is in `GhostMapPresence.ghostMapVesselPids` (pure `ShouldSkipDominantBodyCheck(uint)`), set `__result = false` (= "no dominant-body change") and skip the original, so KSP never runs `RecalculateOrbit`/`OnRailsSOITransition` on a Parsek-owned ghost. Real vessels (and non-vessel celestial-body drivers, caught by the null check) are byte-identical. Ghost map presence fully owns these orbits: every body/orbit change is driven by the per-frame Parsek lifecycle (`ApplyOrbitToVessel` / re-aim resolver) and the line/icon are computed from current Keplerian elements alone, so KSP's SOI transition is pure interference. Rate-limited (5s/pid) `Suppressed KSP on-rails dominant-body SOI transition for ghost pid=...` log confirms the patch is live. 3 `GhostMapPresenceTests.DominantBodyCheck_*` (ghost-pid skipped / real-vessel not / removed-then-not). **Playtest 5 watch:** zero `[OrbitDriver]: On-Rails SOI Transition` for ghost vessels, probe body stays Sun through the coast, zero icon JUMPs, line steady. NOTE: a sibling worktree (`Parsek-fix-ghost-map-icon-frozen-arc`) keeps clobbering the shared `GameData/Parsek/Plugins/Parsek.dll` on its builds - verify the deployed md5 has `GhostOrbitDominantBodyPatch` immediately before each launch. Clean-context Opus review verdict SHIP (independently confirmed via decompiled `Assembly-CSharp` that ghost map pids are KSP-unique via `FlightGlobals.GetUniquepersistentId()` - NOT craft-baked - so the pid gate can never suppress a real vessel; that `updateFromParameters` positions the orbit before the line-346 `CheckDominantBody` call so skipping it loses no positioning; and that `CheckDominantBody` is the SOLE on-rails SOI trigger). MINOR applied: suppressed-path log switched to the `Func<string>` overload so the message is not formatted every physics tick. **PLAYTEST 5 CONFIRMED FIXED (2026-06-01, KSP.log 14:38-14:43, user confirms blinking solved):** `[OrbitDriver]: On-Rails SOI Transition` dropped 45 -> 2 (the 2 residual are the real active vessel, correctly transitioning), the probe's transfer-ghost `body/orbit CHANGED to Kerbin` ping-pong dropped 94 -> 4, the `Suppressed KSP on-rails dominant-body SOI transition` log fired 70x (patch live), and the remaining icon JUMPs are now `body=Sun sma=16.7e9` (the ghost moving along its CORRECT heliocentric orbit under high warp, not the old `body=Kerbin sma=-3.7M ecc=1.0` teleport). The three-strikes root-cause hunt is closed. **CLEANUP done for PR (review of the full branch, verdict SHIP-WITH-FIXES, all applied):** consolidated the 3 redundant "orbit line blink" CHANGELOG bullets into one user-facing bullet crediting the real (SOI-transition) fix; softened the forced-redraw-gate comments (KSP no longer re-transitions ghost referenceBody per-frame, so that gate is now defense-in-depth, not the blink fix); the diagnostic probe `GhostRenderStateProbe` is gated DISABLED-BY-DEFAULT (`Enabled = false`, early-return in LateUpdate) since file deletion was unavailable in the authoring environment - it is safe to delete in a follow-up. Kept (both independently justified, not dead): the forced-redraw gate (#26b, correct invariant + avoids a redundant rebuild) and the frame-based grace (#26c, fixes a real warp bug in the line.active chatter debounce). **Deeper-issue note (deferred, unrelated to this fix):** if a multi-SECOND `polyline-owns-phase` remains during the coast, the polyline should not claim the heliocentric coast the re-aimed Sun ellipse already covers (a `ComputeOrbitalCoverIntervals` change); revisit only if playtest 5 shows it.
- **Re-aim follow-up (#27 Problem 1) DONE: Duna descent polyline coverage hole.** Symptom (playtest re-aim Kerbin->Duna): the final Duna approach / descent tail had NO map line at all (neither orbit line nor polyline). Root cause: in the descent tail the recorded orbit segments are degenerate (seg#20/21 have periapsis BELOW Duna's surface: `sma~340660 ecc~0.11 -> peri alt ~-17 km`), so the orbit line's drawn conic plunges below the surface and cannot be drawn there, while `GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer` DROPPED the descent samples because they fall INSIDE an OrbitSegment interval (treated as orbit-owned). Neither surface drew -> hole. **Exclusion boundary = SURFACE, not atmosphere top (clean-context review CHANGE 2):** the orbit line only becomes UNUSABLE when the conic is DEGENERATE (dives under the ground); a valid conic that merely grazes the atmosphere at periapsis but stays above the surface (periapsis altitude in `[0, atmosphereDepth]`) is still drawn correctly by the orbit line, so the polyline must NOT claim it (excluding such an in-space eccentric orbit, e.g. this recording's Kerbin seg#00/01 with periApt ~12.6 km / apoApt ~131 km, would double-draw it). The choice is PER-SEGMENT periapsis-below-SURFACE (NOT per-sample, and NOT apoapsis-below-atmosphere which would un-exclude seg#20/21 whose apoapsis is ~58 km): the recording's descent samples are ~58 km down to ~50 km (min recorded alt 49998 m), so a per-sample `alt < atmosphereDepth` test would keep only ONE sample and orphan the 50-58 km tail; the clean arrival segments (seg#18/19, peri alt ~58 km, above surface) stay orbit-owned and draw fine, while only the degenerate descent segments (peri below surface) are abandoned by the orbit line. **Fix:** `GhostTrajectoryPolylineRenderer.ComputeOrbitalCoverIntervals` now EXCLUDES a degenerate below-SURFACE OrbitSegment from the cover (pure `IsOrbitSegmentBelowSurface`: periapsis radius `sma*(1-ecc) < bodyRadius`, valid for the hyperbolic sma<0/ecc>1 arrival too), so the polyline picks up exactly the descent samples the orbit line abandons and they merge into ONE continuous Duna leg the head-UT gate selects for the descent head UTs. The per-body radius is injected through a pure seam (`BodySurfaceProvider` delegate + `BodySurfaceInfo` struct, radius only), populated by the Driver from `FlightGlobals` (the pure builder never calls FlightGlobals); the seam is null for the xUnit builder, so a recording with no degenerate segments is BYTE-IDENTICAL to before (a normal in-space or grazing orbit's samples stay orbit-owned). One-shot build log `[GhostMap] excluded N below-surface orbit segments from cover rec=... -> descent leg [start,end]`. Coupling with #26: the descent's now-sustained polyline ownership still hides the orbit line (the #26 grace only debounces a TRANSIENT single-frame dip; a sustained ownership expires the grace and hides), so no double-draw. **Merge across frameless gaps verified (clean-context review CHANGE 3):** the leg-break is driven SOLELY by `OrbitalIntervalBetween` against the (now-reduced) orbital intervals, NOT by section boundaries or frameless `ref=2` OrbitalCheckpoint sections (which contribute no points via `ResolveSourceListForSection`), so after excluding seg#20/21 the real descent geometry (ref=0 Absolute frame clusters separated by frameless ref=2 gaps the degenerate segments span) merges into ONE Duna leg `~[70963373, 70963652]` that `ShouldDrawLegAtHeadUT` selects for head 70963566 (inside the seg#21 frameless gap). No merge fix was needed. New tests in `GhostTrajectoryPolylineBuildTests`: `IsOrbitSegmentBelowSurface` degenerate/clean/grazing-not-excluded/null-provider/unknown-body/hyperbolic-below-surface/hyperbolic-grazing-not-excluded, `ComputeOrbitalCoverIntervals` excludes-degenerate-keeps-grazing / null-keeps-all, the REAL-section-geometry end-to-end (`BuildLegs_RealDunaDescentSectionGeometry_MergesAcrossExcludedGaps`: one merged leg with provider that the head selects, head in NO leg without provider, log assertion), and the NO-OP regression guard (clean + grazing recording -> byte-identical legs with/without the provider). **Cache-guard follow-up (review optional finding #9, left as a note):** `ComputeContentHash` ignores the surface provider, so a build that ran before `FlightGlobals.Bodies` was ready (provider returns body-unknown -> no exclusion -> hole-y legs) could be cache-pinned. Low probability: `EnsureBodyMap` runs before the committed-recording walk and bodies are loaded long before a map-enabled flight/TS scene, so the window is effectively nonexistent; not guarded because the clean fix either blocks the common case (whole-frame defer) or threads unresolved-body state out of the pure build. Revisit only if a hole-y polyline is ever observed sticking after scene entry. **Playtest check:** the Duna descent tail should now show a continuous polyline.
- **Re-aim DEFERRED (#27 Problem 2 / S4 arrival-restitch): descent "not exactly aligned" / arrival SOI-entry seam stays deferred.** The recorded Duna-relative descent already lands on the LIVE Duna at its correct recorded landing site; only the re-aimed transfer's SOI-entry asymptote differs from the recorded approach hyperbola at the S2->S3 seam (design doc `docs/dev/done/plans/reaim-interplanetary-transfers.md` §3 S4 row + §4 "S2 -> S3"). Any partial re-orientation of the recorded descent to close that seam would MOVE the recorded landing site off its correct spot, which is worse than the momentary, far-from-camera seam. So v1 keeps the snap (S3 re-anchored to the synthesized SOI-entry UT, descent S4 replayed as-is) and the alignment fix is NOT attempted; #27 Problem 1 above only ensures the descent gets a polyline (coverage), it does not re-orient it. Tracked as the S4 arrival-restitch follow-up (a playback-engine change, see the design doc deferred list). **Playtest evidence + fix spec (2026-05-31, `logs/2026-05-31_0311_duna-descent-position`, user chose "merge #982, defer the seam").** With #27 Problem 1's coverage fix in, the descent draws and made the pre-existing seam visible: the user reported the descent polyline "far from Duna" and "later than it should be, ghost approached, went back, approached again." Root-caused (read-only investigation): NOT a polyline-geometry bug (the descent is body-fixed and renders correctly at the live Duna surface via `GetWorldSurfacePosition`, draws exactly once, monotonic head), NOT a clock desync (the polyline head and the ghost mesh both use `ResolveTrackingStationSampleUT`), NOT loop doubling. It IS this seam: the re-aimed heliocentric leg reaches Duna SOI (mesh `dist[Duna]` ~14.7 Mm), then the recorded Duna arrival hyperbola is spliced on with its RECORDED approach vector, so the mesh jumps back out to ~33 Mm and re-approaches along the recorded direction (the "approached, went back, approached again"); the seam jump at the recorded Sun->Duna boundary is ~1.37 Gm (`ReaimSeam seg#9->10 body=Duna jump=1374718336`). The descent polyline then draws at the END of the recorded arrival/capture/parking replay (recorded segs 12-19), hence "later," at the recorded landing site, which no longer lines up with the re-aimed approach. CONFIRMED no regression from #982: the seam is pre-existing in the shipped re-aim (#981) and independent of the polyline. **Fix direction when undeferred:** in `Source/Parsek/Reaim/` segment assembly (the `ReaimedTrajectory` / "re-aimed transfer ready ... segs=20" segment-list build), apply a rigid transform mapping the recorded SOI-entry state (position + velocity relative to Duna at recorded arrival) onto the re-aimed transfer's actual SOI-entry state, rotating the recorded arrival hyperbola AND the body-fixed descent points about Duna's center so the seam closes. Carries a product decision: rotate approach only (land at the recorded site) vs rotate approach + descent (land at a re-aimed site). Optional diagnostic to add first: in `ParsekFlight.LogReaimGhostTrace`, on the Sun->arrival-body SEAM, log both endpoints' Duna-relative state vectors (not just the scalar `jump`) so the alignment transform can be verified directly.
- **quick win (done): "Warp to..." button on a looped mission row.** The recurring "the icon rarely appears" complaint is inherent to faithful inter-body cadence (one launch per ~14.5 days for the Mun). New `DrawMissionWarpToWindowButton` (after Delete, before Loop; `"Warp to..."` label per the existing convention, the adjacent TTL column says "to what") fast-forwards the clock to `RewindToLaunchLeadTimeSeconds` (15 s) before the mission's next relaunch (`periodicity.NextRelaunchUT`). **Playtest follow-up:** the first cut routed through `WarpToTimeController.RequestWarp` which, IN FLIGHT, did a full flight->Space-Center scene exit + reload (confirmed in the log: `Deferred flight warp ... returning to the Space Center`). Reworked to use the SAME in-place fast-forward as the Forward button (no scene change): `ShowMissionWarpToWindowConfirmation` -> in flight `ParsekFlight.FastForwardToEventUT(relaunchUT, label)` (new; applies `ApplyJumpLead`, `NotifyRecorder`, `TimeJumpManager.ExecuteForwardJump`), at the Space Center a direct `ExecuteForwardJump(ApplyJumpLead(...))`. Dropped the now-obsolete component machinery (`WarpToTimeMath.ComputeComponentsFromUT` + `MissionsWindowUI.RoundWarpTargetUpToMinute`, both added in the first cut, and their tests - `ExecuteForwardJump` takes a precise UT, so no minute-truncation round-trip is needed; the earlier review-fix for that truncation is moot). Enabled only when looping + an engine unit was built + the relaunch is finite and >1s in the future + the scene is warp-capable (flight or Space Center), via the pure `ShouldEnableWarpToWindow` (unit-tested). `ColW_PeriodLocked` trimmed 184->160 (still fits the longest basis label) to make room in the fixed-width header right block; Watch/Rewind stay column-stable (fixed-width button on every row). The `FastForwardToEventUT` / confirmation / IMGUI paths are runtime/playtest-verified.
- **mission title bubble spacing (done):** `missionHeaderRowStyle` padding was `(0,0,0,4)` (0 top, 4 bottom), leaving a visible extra band under the buttons/text inside the dark bubble (the gap above != below). Set to `(0,0,2,2)` (equal top/bottom) so the spacing is symmetric.
- **first-play floor (done):** a looped mission must never relaunch before its first real play (the original recording, `[spanStart, spanEnd]`, which spawns a real vessel at `spanEnd`) completes. `TryBuildMissionUnit` now clamps the phase anchor to at least `spanEndUT`: `baseAnchorUT = Math.Max(baseAnchorUT, spanEndUT)` (unlocked path) and `referenceUT = Math.Max(referenceUT, spanEndUT)` before `Solve`/`NextWindow` (phase-locked path - keeps the result a faithful `UT0 + k*P` window AND `>= spanEndUT`). The span clock (`TryComputeSpanLoopUT` / `ComputeNewestMissionInstanceSpanLoopUT`) already plays nothing before `phaseAnchorUT` and floors `missionCycle` at 0, so the anchor clamp is the whole fix. Normal flow (loop enabled after the recording, `LoopAnchorUT > spanEndUT`) is a no-op; this only bites a NaN anchor or a future-dated recording (e.g. after a career rewind, whose faithful window could otherwise fall before the launch via negative `k`). Updated `Build_NaNAnchor_*` (NaN now clamps to `spanEndUT`, not `spanStartUT`) + new `Build_LoopAnchorBeforeFirstPlay_ClampsAnchorToAfterTheFirstPlay` (both the locked faithful-window path and the unlocked direct-clamp path).

## TODO - v0.10.0 Missions: docking/undocking effect on mission structure (decision recorded, gaps deferred)

**Tracked as M-MIS-5 (gaps 1+2, dock interval boundary + docked composition) and M-MIS-8 (gap 4, cross-tree foreign dock)** in the Missions feature completion milestones at the top of this file.

- **Decision (2026-05-26 design chat, recorded in `docs/dev/design-mission-abstractions.md` "Docking & undocking (v1)"):** dock / undock affect the mission structure ONLY as tree topology (the existing Dock/Board merge + Undock fork branch points). NO Mission-entity lifecycle is auto-created/closed on dock/undock; loopable segments are interval-level Mission selections over that topology. "Main controller A or B" is not a choice we impose - the docked stack has one KSP active controller and the combined leg records into its tree.
- **Verified loopable today:** A-solo / B-solo (pre-dock), A-after / B-after undock (undock is a structural peel so the line splits + the departing vessel is its own offshoot), peeled offshoots, and a whole-vessel journey. Audited against `MissionLoopUnitBuilder` (drives looping from `Mission.ExcludedIntervalKeys` via `MissionIntervalSelection`) + `MissionCompositionBuilder` (intervals split at structural peels).
- **Gaps (DEFERRED until after supply-routes v0 integration; do NOT fix yet):**
  1. **Dock is not an interval boundary.** `MissionCompositionBuilder.BuildNode` edges only at structural-peel UTs (children leaving), never at a Dock/Board merge UT (a vessel joining), so the docked "AB" stretch is lumped into the continuing vessel's pre-dock interval and can't be looped in isolation. Fix sketch: emit a merge-UT edge on the continuing line when its controller count increases.
  2. **Docked composition understated.** Interval composition = head start composition MINUS structural peels; it never ADDS controllers gained at a dock, and a later undock peel subtracts the departing vessel's parts that were never in the head count (clamped at 0). Tied to gap 1.
  3. ~~**Undock continuation vs offshoot is non-deterministic.**~~ DONE. `ContinuationSuccessor` now honors the recorder's `BranchPoint.ChildRecordingIds[0]` convention (the continuing/active vessel, or the single merged Dock/Board child): `MissionStructureBuilder` marks that leg `MissionLeg.IsBranchContinuation` (derived, not serialized) and `MissionThroughLineBuilder.ContinuationSuccessor` prefers it among the children that already pass its non-anchored/non-EVA filter, so an undock fork's main line follows the controlled vessel instead of a GUID tiebreak. No schema change. Validated by `MissionStructureTests` (`BranchContinuation_IsMarkedOnFirstChild_OfForkAndMerge`, `UndockFork_ContinuationFollowsActiveChild_NotGuidTiebreak`) plus the existing decouple/EVA/dock cases (anchored/EVA children are filtered before the preference, so they are unaffected).
  4. **Cross-tree (foreign-vessel) dock.** Combined leg + post-undock continuation land in the controller's tree while the foreign partner's pre-dock flight stays in its own tree, so "loop the whole shared docked journey from the foreign side" spans two trees. Remaining half of design-doc open question 6; revisit with cross-tree dock-link following (PID-linking like `GhostChainWalker`).

---

## 640. Stock committed-future overlay v2 follow-ups

**Status:** TODO - future investigation / review item from PR #721.

PR #721 ships the v1 scope: stock R&D, Astronaut Complex, and Mission
Control committed-future overlays, plus click-blocks for duplicated tech,
contract accept, kerbal hire, and facility upgrade actions. The following
ideas are deliberately out of v1 scope and should be reviewed as separate
follow-ups after in-game verification:

- KSC facility-upgrade visual overlays in the top-down KSC view. The
  click-block already exists via `FacilityUpgradePatch`; v2 would add the
  visual badge and extend the overlay/click-block invariant to facilities.
- Future-completed / future-failed contract badges in Mission Control, not
  only future-accepted contract badges.
- Administration strategy activation overlays, paired with matching
  click-block behavior if the stock UI has a clickable affordance.
- Per-row claim / override UI for cases where the player intentionally wants
  to bypass a committed-future action, instead of using the global setting.
- Per-user dismissible badges for "hide this warning until next session" style
  workflows.
- Non-stock screen integrations, such as Contract Configurator's own Mission
  Control replacement or other mod-provided building screens.
- Modded flight-scene building overlays. The current v1 overlays are
  `SPACECENTER` scene-bound, while the lower-level click-blocks remain
  scene-agnostic.
- Tooltip styling polish using KSP's richer
  `KSP.UI.TooltipTypes.TooltipController_Text` path instead of the v1
  `GUI.skin.box` fallback.

**Review guidance:** keep the v1 invariant intact for every clickable action:
if a stock or modded UI exposes a clickable affordance, the overlay candidate
set and the click-block predicate must share the same `MilestoneStore` source
helper, with any UI-only suppression kept outside the click-block predicate.

## Phase 6 known gaps (deferred to later phases)

- ~~§7.7 BubbleEntry / BubbleExit candidates are not emitted by the Phase 6 builder.~~ Shipped: `AnchorCandidateBuilder.EmitBubbleEntryExitCandidates` walks adjacent `TrackSection` pairs and emits at every `Active|Background ↔ Checkpoint` source-class transition; `IAnchorWorldFrameResolver.TryResolveBubbleEntryExitWorldPos` reads the LAST/FIRST physics-active sample as the high-fidelity world reference. Mainline shipped this at `AlgorithmStampVersion=5`; on the Phase 5 stack it lands inside the v8 alg-stamp window. Residual gap: RELATIVE-frame physics-active sections adjacent to a Checkpoint segment are deferred with a `bubble-entry-exit-relative-section-deferred` Verbose (uncommon in practice — vessel docked to its anchor while a Checkpoint splices in).
- ~~§7.8 CoBubblePeer anchors are reserved in the enum but emit no candidates.~~ Obsolete: the co-bubble subsystem was retired in PR #912 (v0.9.3). The enum slot 7 (formerly `CoBubblePeer`) is now `Reserved7`, kept only to preserve the persisted `.pann` `AnchorCandidatesList` byte layout; there is no co-bubble pipeline. Close-formation accuracy is delivered by the parent-anchored debris contract instead.
- The 2.5 km bubble-radius HR-9 Warn (`RenderSessionState.cs:836-848`) only fires from the LiveSeparation path inside `RebuildFromMarker`. Anchors written via `AnchorPropagator.TryWriteAnchor → PutAnchorWithPriority` (§7.4 / §7.5 / §7.6 / §7.7 / §7.10) skip the magnitude check, so a non-LiveSeparation ε of, say, 12 km lands silently. Lift the magnitude check into `PutAnchorWithPriority` (or the per-source dispatch) in a follow-up PR so all anchor types are uniformly guarded — pre-existing gap, not introduced by §7.7.
- §7.9 SurfaceContinuous emits a marker only with ε = 0; the per-frame terrain raycast that resolves ε is Phase 7 work. Phase 6 demoted the rank from 2 to 6 to prevent the zero stub from winning ties against real OrbitalCheckpoint ε; Phase 7 must promote back to rank 2 once the resolver ships and bump `AlgorithmStampVersion` so existing `.pann` re-resolve.
- The split anchor sources (Undock / EVA / JointBreak) currently share the `DockOrMerge` enum byte (priority rank 4 either way). Logs label them by `BranchPointType` rather than by enum value to preserve telemetry granularity. If a future phase needs to differentiate split priorities from dock priorities, expand the `AnchorSource` enum and bump `AlgorithmStampVersion`.

## Observability Audit - 2026-04-26

Full report: `docs/dev/observability-audit-2026-04-26.md`.
Implementation plan: `docs/dev/plan-observability-logging-visibility.md`.

Open implementation follow-up: make Parsek's runtime decisions reconstructable
from `KSP.log` without reintroducing per-frame spam. The audit prioritizes:

- P1 current spam hygiene: finalizer-cache summaries, patched-snapshot /
  extrapolator repeats, current map/proto-vessel/tracking-station repeaters,
  diagnostics sidecar warnings, ledger no-op summaries, sandbox patch skips,
  and KSC playback spam fixes.
- P2 ~~flight ghost skip reasons, playback frame skip summaries~~, rewind
  `CanInvoke` reason logging, sidecar/path severity and context, duplicate
  `OnLoad` timing cleanup, post-switch auto-record no-trigger summaries,
  background recorder drift warnings, game-action skip summaries, and ~~UI/map
  marker skip summaries for ghost/proto-vessel map presence and watch focus~~.
- P3 shared rate-limit key cleanup, repeated-warning rate limits, noisy resource
  event aggregation, production warning-prefix cleanup, and low-risk
  cleanup/reflection summaries.

Phase 0 guardrails started on `observability/guardrails`: retained-log signal
analysis, stricter post-hoc log validation, and guaranteed validation artifacts
from `collect-logs.py`.

2026-04-26 Phase 1 update: the current retained-log hygiene slice is closed for
the finalization/map signal called out in
`logs/2026-04-26_0118_refly-postfix-still-broken`. The fix keys
`FinalizerCache refresh summary` by owner/recording/terminal state, rate-limits
stable no-delta and repeated classification summaries, collapses the
patched-snapshot missing-body / captured and extrapolator seeded-OFR repeaters
with `VerboseOnChange`, rate-limits empty GhostMap cleanup, gates map-visible
window diagnostics on source/window changes, and folds the Task 1.5 ledger /
sandbox-patcher repeaters into state-change gated summaries. Focused xUnit log
assertions pin each gate. The broader observability audit remains open for later
missing-decision logs and save/load context work.

Status update (`observability/playback-visibility`): closed the Phase 2 flight
playback visibility slice for ghost skip reasons, on-change skip logging, engine
aggregate skip counters, fast-forward watch handoff reasons, and watch-camera
infrastructure failures. The branch also added map-view/proto-vessel visibility
reasoning for missing map objects, orbit renderers, draw-icon state, native-icon
suppression, renderer force-enable, and watched-ghost map-focus restore blockers.
Review follow-up: map-focus restore logging now uses one stable on-change
identity with the watched recording/pid/reason in the state key, avoiding
per-recording cache growth while preserving reason-change visibility.
Review follow-up: Flight scene teardown and `DestroyAllTimelineGhosts` now clear
ghost-skip reason state and the matching `Flight|ghost-skip|` `VerboseOnChange`
identities, with coverage showing per-recording skip reasons re-emit after
scene cleanup and rewind/timeline destruction.
Remaining observability audit items stay open.

Phase 3 persistence/rewind observability is closed on
`observability/persistence-rewind` (2026-04-26): `OnSave` / `OnLoad` now carry
top-level exception context and single phase/status timing; recording sidecar,
snapshot-probe, path-resolution, and transient cleanup failures now surface
Warn/Error context with recording id, save folder, epoch, ghost snapshot mode,
file kind, paths, staged-file count, and exception details; Rewind/Re-Fly
`CanInvoke` plus disabled slot decisions now log only on reason changes. This
closes the audit follow-up for duplicate/miscounted `OnLoad` timing, sidecar/path
failure severity/context, and rewind precondition reason visibility. Remaining
observability-audit work stays in the non-persistence phases: KSC/playback spam
hygiene, ghost skip summaries, recorder/auto-record decision logs, game-action
aggregation, and map/UI/test-runner visibility.

Review follow-up: legacy text snapshot parse exceptions again flow to the
outer `exception:<Type>` sidecar failure path; resolve-only path lookups now log
missing save context at Verbose while directory-creation entry points keep Warn;
and Rewind/Re-Fly slot `VerboseOnChange` identities are cleared when RP state is
loaded, closed, reaped, discarded, or rolled back.

Runtime-gaps branch progress (2026-04-26): Phase 4/5 recorder and
game-visible runtime decisions are now covered for the high-priority gaps:
background recorder attach/clear and drift warnings, active-to-background
missing-vessel/finalizer diagnostics, post-switch auto-record no-trigger and
manifest-delta summaries, EVA/boarding split skips, ParsekUI map-marker skip
summaries, Tracking Station atmospheric-marker skip summaries, ghost orbit-line
suppression decisions, game-action converter skip-by-type summaries, event
reject logs, kerbal recalculation counters, Real Spawn Control auto-close
reasons, and test-runner scene-eligibility skip aggregation.
Review follow-up: post-switch manifest logging preserves trigger-priority
short-circuiting, marking lower-priority delta families as `skipped` instead of
diffing every manifest category on each 0.25s evaluation tick; the background
state-drift throttle now has a backwards-UT rollback test.

Remaining observability follow-up after runtime-gaps: the earlier P1/P2
save/load exception context, sidecar/path severity expansion, rewind
`CanInvoke` reason-change logging, playback-engine frame skip counters, and
Phase 6 retained in-game log-package validation still need separate passes.

Review follow-up coverage (2026-04-26): closed the deferred log-assertion gaps
for finalizer refresh identity isolation, Diagnostics missing-sidecar path
warning scopes, `ComputePlaybackFlags` ghost-skip emit/suppress behavior,
`OnSave` exception context/RecState, and unsupported snapshot probe logging.

Post-merge spam fix (2026-04-26, `fix/rewindui-canInvokeSlot-spam`): the
2026-04-26_1025 playtest log showed 1389 identical `[RewindUI] CanInvokeSlot:
slot-ok` lines in 6 seconds for a single rp/slot — the existing
`ParsekLog.VerboseOnChange` gate did not suppress the repeats from the OnGUI
draw loop, while the matching `[Rewind] CanInvoke:` site (same code path,
same dictionary) suppressed correctly. The xUnit 200-call repro passes, so
the failure is Unity-runtime-specific. `LogRewindSlotCanInvokeDecision` now
tracks the last-emitted decision stateKey in a file-local
`Dictionary<string,string>` and only calls `ParsekLog.Verbose` when it
changes — mirroring the `lastCanInvoke` pattern already used by
`DrawUnfinishedFlightRewindButton` ~300 lines above. Existing
`ClearRewindSlotCanInvokeLogState` callers (LoadTimeSweep, RewindPointAuthor,
RewindPointReaper, TreeDiscardPurge, ParsekScenario.OnLoad) clear the new
dict alongside the original `ParsekLog.ClearVerboseOnChangeIdentitiesWithPrefix`
call. Review follow-up: removed the per-OnGUI-pass clear that
`RecordingsTableUI.DrawIfOpen` was firing while the Recordings window was
closed — it wiped the cache before TimelineWindowUI's Fly button could
reuse it, re-spamming `slot-ok` whenever Timeline was open without
Recordings. Regression tests:
`RewindSlotCanInvoke_ManyConsecutiveCalls_EmitsOnceForStableSlotOk` drives
200 calls and asserts a single emit;
`RewindSlotCanInvoke_TimelineOnlyCalls_DoNotRespamAfterRecordingsClose`
drives 200 Timeline-style calls after a single close-transition clear and
asserts only 2 emits total.

## Done - Logistics supply-route per-run cost display (Career + KSC origin)

- ~~Surface the per-run funds cost of a Supply Route in the Logistics UI (route detail panel, Create Route summary, Candidate row).~~ DONE. The pure `RouteRunCostCalculator` (`net = launch - recovered`, recovery summed over the whole source TREE via `ComputeELS()`, gotcha G1) feeds the throttled `RouteLegibility` cache (Phase 2) and the candidate-cost cache (~1 Hz, never on the draw path). The pure `LogisticsCostPresentation` shapes the detail line + tooltip, the creation-summary block, and the compact candidate-row suffix; the `*UI` files only draw. Display is Career + KSC-origin only and is suppressed when the source snapshot has not hydrated (no "0 funds" line, gotcha G7). Phase 4 closed the test matrix: `RouteRunCostCalculatorTests` and `LogisticsCostPresentationTests` pin the arithmetic and every formatted surface (with-recovery and no-recovery shapes, InvariantCulture under a comma locale, ASCII-only with no em dash). Review follow-up: the candidate-path KSC gate (creation summary + candidate row) now derives KSC origin from the tree ROOT recording via `RouteRunCostCalculator.IsCandidateKscOrigin` (mirroring `RouteBuilder`), not from the dock-child `analysis.SourceRecording` whose `LaunchSiteName` is null on the common docking flight; pinned by the `IsCandidateKscOrigin_*` tests.
- ~~**Deferred follow-up (decision D1, display-only):** the per-cycle ledger CHARGE is still the GROSS launch cost; only the DISPLAY is the recovery-aware net.~~ DONE (logistics-recovery-credit). The per-cycle charge now reconciles to the displayed net via a deferred recovery credit. The orchestrator emits a `RouteRecoveryCredited` ledger row at the next dock crossing (one dispatch interval after the dispatch it pays back, keyed on the prior dispatched cycle via `Route.PendingRecoveryCreditCycleId`, persisted sparsely through `RouteCodec`), and `FundsModule` processes the gross debit (`RouteCargoDebited`) as a spending and the credit (`RouteRecoveryCredited`) as an earning (Option A), so both reverse through the recalc cutoff walk (rewind) and the tombstone path (re-fly); `RouteModule` observes the credit row into a per-route diagnostic counter only (observe-only, never mutates funds). The dispatch debit and the `KscFundsAvailable` gate stay on gross, so you still front the full build cost to launch. Routing the gross debit through the walk is a deliberate, more-correct behavior change (OQ3 resolved, KEEP Option A): a Parsek timeline rewind now also reverses a route's gross charge, closing the pre-feature fire-and-forget hole where only a stock quicksave / load did. The deferral's final owed credit is flushed at every transition that stops a route crossing (immediate `TryPause`, the armed pause-after-cycle delivery transition, EndpointLost-at-delivery, and `RouteStore.RevalidateSources` flipping a route into `MissingSourceRecording` / `SourceChanged`) so the last dispatched cycle's credit is never stranded. The credit is a constant per-cycle amount (`SumRecoveredCredits` over the source tree, scoped since M-MIS-9-R1 to the recordings that existed at route creation), exact in steady state but an approximation of each run's physical recovery-landing UT; precise per-run landing with cycle overlap is deferred (plan OQ1). Retroactive tombstoning of already-emitted credit rows on a non-rewinding supersede is also deferred (RESOLUTION 1 / OQ2). Pinned by `RouteRecoveryCreditTests` (pairing, T-CYCLE0 first-cycle no-same-tick-credit, deferral, pause/stop tails including the armed-pause and EndpointLost flushes, and T-CRASH-WINDOW-TOMBSTONE proving the replay flush recomputes fresh from ELS so a tombstone applied in the crash window zeroes the owed credit), `RouteStoreValidationTests` (the source-problem flush), `RouteModuleTests` (T-ROUTEMODULE-OBSERVE: the credit increments the diagnostic counter and mutates no funds), the `FundsModule` route credit/debit tests plus T-RECONCILE-NOOP (no-rewind reconcile delta ~0) and T-LEGACY-DEBIT (a bare legacy gross-debit row is counted once, not double-subtracted), the `RouteCodec` round-trip, the `GameAction` serialization tests, `LedgerTests` (T-SCENARIO-ROUNDTRIP: a `RouteRecoveryCredited` row survives the ledger save/load persistence path), and the rewind-reversal cutoff-walk proof `RewindUtCutoffTests.RouteRecoveryCredit_CutoffBeforeCredit_*` / `RouteCargoDebit_CutoffBeforeDebit_*` (a Parsek timeline rewind un-credits the recovery by exactly the credit amount, Option A's gross debit cutoff symmetric) plus T-REWIND-RESERVATION (`RouteRecoveryCredit_LiveEventRecalcAtCreditUT_FloorIncludesCredit` / `RouteRecoveryCredit_CutoffBeforeCredit_LowersReservationFloor`: the credit's reversibility holds on the cutoff-walk reservation-floor branch the live route emit actually triggers).

## Done - Route-creation dialog showed garbled origin and wrong auto-name for KSC routes

- ~~The "Create Supply Route?" confirmation window showed the Origin as garbage ("????") for a KSC-origin route and auto-named it "Route: Kerbin -> Kerbin" instead of "Route: KSC -> Kerbin" (playtest 2026-06-06, save "orbital supply route DELIVERY test"; route `name = Route: Kerbin -> Kerbin`, `isKscOrigin = True`, dock child `70667ab4` with no `launchSiteName`, root `44129e52` with `launchSiteName = Launch Pad`).~~ DONE (branch `fix-route-origin-label`). Two causes: **(1) origin read off the wrong recording.** The origin label and default name resolved origin identity from `analysis.SourceRecording` (the mid-flight DOCK CHILD, whose `LaunchSiteName == null` because it started at the dock) instead of the tree ROOT recording (`LaunchSiteName = "Launch Pad"`, `StartBodyName = "Kerbin"`), so every origin branch fell through to the placeholder even though the route was correctly classified KSC-origin (`Route.IsKscOrigin = true`, which `RouteRunCostCalculator.IsCandidateKscOrigin` already computes off the root). Fixed by a shared `RouteCreationFormatters.ResolveOriginIdentity(analysis, tree)` helper that resolves origin off `tree.RootRecordingId` with a dock-child fallback (mirroring `IsCandidateKscOrigin` / `RouteCreationDialog.ComputeRootToUndockSpan`), reading BOTH the KSC launch site and the start-docked depot proof from the resolved origin recording exactly like the authoritative `RouteBuilder` (`originRec.RouteOriginProof`), now routed through all three display surfaces (`BuildSummaryBlock` origin line, `GenerateDefaultRouteName`, `LogisticsWindowUI.FormatCandidateOrigin`) so they cannot diverge again; `tree` is plumbed into `GenerateDefaultRouteName` from every caller (the dialog, the window candidate row, and `RouteBuilder`). (The depot branch previously read the proof off the dock-child source; aligning it to the root also fixes a latent case where a real depot route rendered as an unknown origin.) **(2) angle-bracket placeholders eaten by TMP.** The dialog-body fallback placeholders used angle brackets (`<unknown>`); KSP renders the `MultiOptionDialog` body through TextMeshPro with rich text enabled, so `<unknown>` parsed as a bogus markup tag and rendered as "????". The dialog-body formatters (`BuildSummaryBlock`, `FormatEndpoint`, `FormatResourceLine`, `FormatInventoryLine`) now use bracket-free fallback wording ("unknown"). Pinned by `RouteCreationFormattersTests` (root-resolution origin identity, null-tree fallback, the KSC summary/name/candidate labels, and a no-`<`/`>`-in-the-rendered-body guard).

## Closed (not a bug) - Logistics send-once re-arm delivers at the NEXT dock crossing, up to a full span away

- Playtest observation (save "orbital supply route DELIVERY test", 2026-06-06): a KSC -> Depot supply route (recorded span ~16058s, recorded dock UT 17478, span end ~17594) delivered correctly on its first cycle (`Route ... Active->Paused reason=delivered-then-paused completedCycles=1`), the player re-armed a single cycle (`Route Paused->Active reason=send-once-arm`), and no second delivery fired in the ~59s before the scene changed. Every dispatch tick logged cleanly (`dispatched=0 ... errored=0 skipped=1`): no error, no stuck/errored state.
- **Verdict: correct by design, not a bug.** A v0 supply route is a looped Mission segment that renders `[root launch .. dock]` and **delivery fires when the loop clock reaches the recorded dock PHASE, not at cycle start** (design section 0.4 "Delivery fires when that loop clock crosses the recorded dock UT each cycle" and section 0.9 DEL-2 "Delivery fires when the loop clock reaches the recorded dock phase, not at cycle start"). One delivery == one full ghost run reaching its dock.
- **Why dock UT sits at ~99% of the span (NOT an anchor / off-by-one bug):** the route SEGMENT is `[launch .. dock]` by construction. `RouteBuilder` computes `transitDuration = recordedDockUT - rootLaunchUT` ([RouteBuilder.cs:153](../../Source/Parsek/Logistics/RouteBuilder.cs)) and the dock UT "is the route segment END ... with the [launch..dock] segment it equals spanEnd" ([RouteBuilder.cs:387-389](../../Source/Parsek/Logistics/RouteBuilder.cs)). The small gap between dock (17478) and span end (17594) is the post-dock recording tail / boundary epsilon; the dock is still inside the span (`RouteLoopClock.IsDockUTInSpan` true), so a crossing can fire. Moving the dock earlier in the span would deliver BEFORE the ghost visually docks, breaking the core "deliver at the dock" contract; the dock is genuinely the end of an outbound launch->dock run.
- **Why the second cycle did not fire in the window (the mechanism, confirmed):** after delivery #1 the dock-phase cycle was cycle 0, so `LastObservedLoopCycleIndex = 0`. The loop clock free-runs on absolute UT (it is NOT advanced by the orchestrator while paused, and re-arm does not reset it). At re-arm the clock had already rolled past cycle 0's dock into cycle 1 and was early in the run (`loopUT` ~3283, well below the dock at 17478), so `ComputeDockCycleIndex = cycleIndex - 1 = 0` ([RouteLoopClock.cs:154-157](../../Source/Parsek/Logistics/RouteLoopClock.cs)) and `IsDockCrossing` returns `dockCycleIndex (0) > LastObservedLoopCycleIndex (0)` == false ([RouteLoopClock.cs:190-202](../../Source/Parsek/Logistics/RouteLoopClock.cs)). The next delivery requires the clock to climb back around to the dock of cycle 1 (`loopUT` 3283 -> 17478, ~14000s of ghost-time), which the player's ~59s of warp did not cover.
- **The gate is exactly right (no extra forced wait):** the `>` comparison (not `>=`) is necessary so cycle 0's already-delivered dock is not re-delivered. The gate fires at the next UN-delivered dock crossing, firing exactly once and snapping forward on a warp jump ([RouteOrchestrator.cs ProcessLoopRoute](../../Source/Parsek/Logistics/RouteOrchestrator.cs), `crossing` branch). Send-once correctly does NOT reset `LastObservedLoopCycleIndex` (unlike `TryActivate`): resetting it to -1 would make a re-arm fire IMMEDIATELY while the ghost is mid-flight (`dockCycleIndex - 1 = 0 > -1`), delivering with no ghost at the dock, which is the wrong contract.
- **Intended send-once cadence (so this is not re-investigated):** re-arming send-once schedules ONE delivery at the loop clock's next un-delivered dock crossing. Because the dock is the end of the launch->dock segment and the clock free-runs, the wall-clock-UT wait is anywhere from ~0 (if a dock passed during the pause, in which case the next tick fires and snaps forward) up to one full span (`DispatchInterval = N x span`, default N=1). Re-arming right after a delivery lands near the worst case: you must warp the ghost through nearly a full outbound run for it to dock again. The Logistics window's "Next delivery" countdown (`RouteOrchestrator.TryComputeSecondsToNextDockCrossing`) surfaces this expected wait. This is the same near-full-span warp the FIRST send-once needs to reach the dock; it is fundamental to delivery == the ghost docking, not a regression.
- **Related observation (same playtest) - "the send-once ghost exploded / disappeared seconds after launch" is faithful ascent staging plus the loop overlap/zone behaviour under time warp, NOT the main vehicle dying.** Confirmed from the AUTHORITATIVE logistics-build log (`logs/2026-06-06_1408_logistics-supply-route/KSP.log`, `Parsek V0.10.0`, branch `logistics-v0-implementation` commit `f0855865` - this is the original 13:51-13:59 send-once session, captured by `collect-logs.py` BEFORE it was overwritten; an earlier read mistakenly concluded it was gone). The route's backing tree (`c9ef80ee`) is an orbital launch->dock run whose recorded ascent sheds booster stages, each a separate `Kerbal X Debris` recording (`terminalState=4` = Destroyed) parent-anchored to route member `44129e52`. Mechanism at re-arm (13:58:22, loop clock near the cycle-0 dock at loopUT~17508):
  - The loop's SELF-OVERLAP spawned the NEXT cycle's launch as ghost #9 "Kerbal X" (`OverlapPrimaryEnter`, cycle 1, loopUT~1449) near KSC at `dist=4101m` (Physics zone, visible), with its parent-anchored debris #10-#16 overlap-spawning alongside.
  - Those dropped stages fall back and are destroyed via stock `FXMonger.Explode` (8 debris explosions starting 13:58:23, parts `liquidEngine2` / `fuelTank` / `Decoupler.2` / `pointyNoseConeB`) - the "explosion", faithful staging.
  - The launch ghost then rapidly climbs and flies downrange: zone Physics (4101m) -> Visual (10128m at 13:58:31) -> Beyond within ~10-18s, accelerated by the player's time warp (`1x -> 16x -> 50x` in that window; a 314s ascent plays in ~6s at 50x). After 13:58:40 NO `Kerbal X` (non-debris) ghost remains in the Physics/Visual zone near the player - the "disappearance" is the ascent ghost leaving the local view, not a destruction.
  - The MAIN `Kerbal X` ghost NEVER explodes or retires anomalously (zero non-debris explosions in the log); it flew its recorded ascent into orbit/toward the dock. The "Chain dedup: removed ghost map for #9 (replaced by #21)" at 13:58:30 removes a MAP-view duplicate, not the flight mesh.
  This ties directly to the cadence finding above: at re-arm the loop was at the END of cycle 0 (near the dock), so the only thing rendered near KSC was the loop overlap of the next cycle's launch, which staged and then ascended out of view under warp. All faithful replay; no bug. (Separately note the loop-shift family already tracked for `Kerbal X` elsewhere in this file governs how the post-ascent orbital phase is positioned; it is not what makes the near-KSC ascent ghost leave view.)
- **Environment caveat (unrelated to the verdict):** the CURRENTLY deployed `GameData/Parsek/Plugins/Parsek.dll` was later clobbered to a NON-logistics sibling build (verified: zero logistics strings; a 14:12 session logged zero `[Route]` lines). Rebuild from the `logistics-v0-implementation` worktree and verify the deployed DLL before any further in-game logistics testing, per this file's "Diagnosing which build produced a collected log" note.

## ~~Open~~ RESOLVED 2026-06-10 (M1 Phase 6) - Logistics scenario-lifecycle coverage relies on source-text gates

**Resolution (the 3-layer harness shape, plan-logistics-m1-origin-debit design D10):** (a) xUnit codec layer - route round-trips including dispatch priority + the non-KSC origin endpoint descriptor (`RouteStoreScenarioIntegrationTests.Scenario_RoundTrip_PreservesPriorityAndNonKscOriginDescriptor`, `RouteCodecTests`) and the `RouteCargoDebited` actuals/requested/pid round-trips (`GameActionSerializationTests`); (b) `Scenario_OnSaveAndOnLoad_InvokeRouteStoreCodec` upgraded from presence-only to an ORDERED gate (`LoadRoutesFrom` index must precede `RevalidateSources("OnLoad")` within `ParsekScenario.cs`; the save-side and Tick gates stay presence); (c) in-game lifecycle tests `LogisticsOriginDebitRuntimeTests` covering the loaded AND unloaded (proto-snapshot) origin debit through the production `RouteOrchestrator.Tick` crossing, the empty-origin hold, and the unloaded debit surviving a real `GamePersistence.SaveGame` round-trip. The full Unity-shim harness (~120 affected files) was deliberately NOT built: layers (a)+(c) cover the M1 risk (state-mutation correctness + persistence) a shim would not cover better.

- The route system has three `ParsekScenario` lifecycle hookups (`RouteStore.SaveRoutesTo`, `LoadRoutesFrom`, `RevalidateSources`) and they are pinned by `RouteStoreScenarioIntegrationTests.Scenario_OnSaveAndOnLoad_InvokeRouteStoreCodec`, which greps the source for the three literal strings. The pattern matches existing precedents (`ChainSaveLoadTests`, `GrepAuditTests`, `Bug278SnapshotPersistenceTests`, etc.) but only verifies presence, not surrounding state or order.
- xUnit cannot drive `ParsekScenario.OnSave`/`OnLoad` end-to-end because both call `Planetarium.GetUniversalTime()` unguarded and the OnLoad path depends on `stateRecorder.Subscribe`, `SubscribeVesselLifecycleEvents` (Unity `GameEvents`), and `StartCoroutine` (Unity `MonoBehaviour`). No Unity-shim base class exists in `Source/Parsek.Tests/`.

**Risk:** Scales linearly with hook count. As later items (item 4 route creation UI, item 5 dispatch scheduler) add more hooks, the gate-test count grows and ordering bugs become invisible.

**Fix:** Scheduled with logistics milestone M1 (`docs/parsek-logistics-supply-routes-design.md` section 19.4): the non-KSC origin debit is the first feature mutating non-KSC vessel state per cycle (loaded AND unloaded vessels) and deserves lifecycle-level `OnSave`/`OnLoad` tests rather than grep gates, so the harness is built alongside it, not after. Building the Unity test harness (stubbed `Planetarium.fetch` + minimal `GameEvents` event-bus mock + `MonoBehaviour` shim) affects every existing harness-touching test (about 120 files reference one of those types); coordinating with the in-flight logging audit is still sensible if the timing lines up.

**Mitigation in the meantime:** When new hookups land in items 4-5, tighten the corresponding source-text gate to assert on an **ordered multi-string pattern** of the surrounding phase, not just presence. Example: gate for item 5's scheduler init should grep that `LoadRoutesFrom` precedes `RevalidateSources` precedes the scheduler init within the same load-phase block. `ChainSaveLoadTests` already has precedents for both presence-of and absence-of assertions.

**Status:** RESOLVED 2026-06-10 with logistics M1 (see the resolution block above). Filed 2026-05-16 alongside the items 1-3 blind-spot audit.

---

## Done - Logistics supply-route EC/IntakeAir pickup filter

- ~~`RouteAnalysisEngine.HasResourcePickup` tripped `MixedPickupDelivery` on ANY per-resource `transportGain` / `endpointLoss`, including ElectricCharge and IntakeAir, even though the design (section 5.3 rule 7, section 6) filters those two out as environmental noise. A clean delivery-only run that recharged its batteries from the docked depot, or whose IntakeAir reading drifted between the dock and undock snapshots, was falsely rejected at creation as a mixed pickup/delivery transfer.~~ DONE. Added `RouteAnalysisEngine.IsIgnoredResource` (ElectricCharge + IntakeAir, matching `VesselSpawner.ExtractResourceManifest`, the only two always-ignored resources the design names) and skip them in both `HasResourcePickup` (the pickup gate) and `BuildResourceDeliveryManifest` (so EC/IntakeAir never appear as delivered cargo, and an EC-only "delivery" where the transport charges the depot's batteries is rejected as no-delivery rather than treated as an EC supply run, per design section 6). The mixed-pickup rejection diagnostic now names the tripping resource/identity and its deltas. Pinned by `RouteAnalysisEngineTests` (`AnalyzeRecording_TransportRechargesEC_StillEligible`, `AnalyzeRecording_IntakeAirDrift_StillEligible`, `AnalyzeRecording_ElectricChargeDelivery_ExcludedFromManifest`, `AnalyzeRecording_ElectricChargeOnly_RejectsNoDelivery`, and the `_DiagnosticNamesResource` / `_DiagnosticNamesIdentity` log-assertions for the resource and inventory rejection diagnostics). Distinct from the post-couple crossfeed limitation below, which still trips on genuine same-resource equalisation (LiquidFuel/Ore), not EC/IntakeAir.

## Done 2026-06-09 - Logistics route window dock-side baseline is post-couple (0.10.1)

**Fix (done, branch `fix-dock-side-baseline`):** chose fix candidate 1 (pre-couple transport snapshot), mirroring the proven endpoint-side `endpointPreCoupleSnapshot` mechanism. `ParsekFlight.OnPartCouple` now captures the recorder's own (transport) pre-couple vessel snapshot into `pendingDockSelfSnapshot` / `pendingDockSelfSnapshotPid` (next to `pendingDockPartnerSnapshot`), in the same block where `data.from` / `data.to` are still distinct, via the new `ResolveSelfVessel` helper (matches `recorder.RecordingVesselId` regardless of survivor status). `RouteProofCapture.BuildDockRouteConnectionWindow` takes a new `transportPreCoupleSnapshot` parameter and extracts `DockTransportResources` / `DockTransportInventory` from it, selected self-validatingly (`SnapshotContainsAnyPartPersistentId(snapshot, transportPids)`, else falls back to the merged snapshot - current behaviour preserved). Fix candidate 2 (the `HasResourcePickup` approximate-equalisation heuristic) was rejected as it could misclassify a genuine net-out pickup. **Caveat:** the headless tests prove the SELECTION logic flips the `MixedPickupDelivery` classification; the equalisation-vs-`onPartCouple` ordering is a playtest-confirmable assumption (the merged snapshot is captured frames later, so the fix is strictly an improvement). In-game playtest pending. Tests: `RouteProofCaptureTests` (5 new: transport baseline pre-couple vs merged, self-validation fallback, inventory parity, and an end-to-end `AnalyzeRecording` repro that is rejected with the deflated baseline and accepted with the pre-couple baseline). Plan: `docs/dev/plan-dock-side-baseline-fix.md`.

- The `RouteConnectionWindow.DockTransportResources` / `DockEndpointResources` manifests captured in `ParsekFlight.CreateMergeBranch` come from the merged vessel's `mergedSnapshot` (built from the live merged vessel taken inside `onPartCouple`). By the time the snapshot is taken the parts are physically joined, so any same-frame stock crossfeed equalisation between transport and endpoint tanks of the same resource lands on the dock-side baseline, not the undock-side delta. The strict `RouteAnalysisEngine.HasMixedPickupDelivery` gate then sees `transportGain > 0` on a resource the player never intended to move and rejects the run as `MixedPickupDelivery`. (The endpoint side of this was already fixed via `endpointPreCoupleSnapshot`; this closes the symmetric transport side.)

**Workaround:** Re-record without crossfed same-resource tanks on both sides of the dock, or disable flow on the affected transport tanks before docking. The route-analyzer rejection logs at `Info` ("RouteAnalysis rejected: mixed pickup/delivery") and now names the tripping resource (`pickup resource=<name> ...`) so the affected tank's resource is visible in `KSP.log` without raising the verbosity dial. (ElectricCharge and IntakeAir are filtered out and never trip this gate; see the EC/IntakeAir filter item above.)

**Fix candidates (candidate 1 chosen, shipped):**

1. (CHOSEN) Capture a pre-couple transport snapshot inside the `onPartCouple` handler before stock physics runs the same-frame couple equalisation pass, and feed it to `BuildDockRouteConnectionWindow` instead of `mergedSnapshot`. The existing `AppendStructuralEventSnapshot` runs at the right moment but feeds the trajectory pipeline, not route proof.
2. (REJECTED) Detect the "approximate equalisation" pattern in `RouteAnalysisEngine.HasResourcePickup` (per-resource transportGain ≈ endpointLoss within a small tolerance) and treat it as not-a-pickup. Heuristic; could mis-classify genuine pickups that happen to net out.

**Status:** DONE in 0.10.1 (branch `fix-dock-side-baseline`), see the Fix note in the heading above. Filed 2026-05-16 alongside the second-pass review of the logistics-v0-implementation branch.

**Message (done, 2026-06-06):** The player-facing `MixedPickupDelivery` reject copy (`RouteCreationFormatters.FormatRejectMessage`, also reused by the Logistics near-miss list via `LogisticsRejectPresentation.DescribeNearMiss`) now explains the common cause in plain language (the transport ended the run with more of a resource than it started, e.g. fuel transferred back out to undock from a full depot) and gives the actionable fix (re-record without taking resources from the destination, transfer that resource back out before undocking, or disable flow on the affected transport tanks before docking). Copy/UX only: the `HasResourcePickup` gate, the strict one-way contract, and the status enum are all unchanged.
